O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear sons, I have finished this book which is the end of the science of medicine, assembled from its teachings and pronouncements.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to pass that I realized I must accompany this treatise, which is a part of the work of hands, namely surgery.</start_of_turn>
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is fraught in our region and is strange to all, if the science is lost and forgotten, and nothing remains of it except for the small descriptions in the books of the ancients which the hands have performed.</start_of_turn
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this arises the error and the emptiness, and are closed the understandings and is displaced the science.</start_of_turn
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or it seems to me that I shall make it alive together the ordination of this physician according to the way of exposure and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come together the forms of the fire cautery instruments and other tools of the work with the agreement of the declaration and preparation of the patient, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	Or it seems to me that I shall make it live altogether the order of this physician according to the way of exposure and declaration and of the abbreviation; and I shall join together the forms of the instruments of cautery, and of other instruments of the work with the arrangement of the declaration and preparation of it, as it is necessary.</start_of_turn>
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary that he who enters this field should be skilled in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he has grasped the judgment of limbs, and the forms and the joints and the separations of things, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and muscles and their number, and the structure and the veins moving and resting, and their issue.</start_of_turn>
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And thus Ypocras said that we must not trust the word of the patient alone, but with the work it is indeed so.
et meismement en l’art de main.	and indeed in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	As we have said at the beginning of this book, whoever is not familiar with the things that are before him, if he is rash and does not notice the homes, will certainly err
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	Because I have often seen more of these things that interfere with this science and if they abandon science and common sense.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I have seen fools who have coped with scrofules or a woman’s neck, and have coped the arteries of the neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	because so much blood has flowed out that the woman has died between her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I have seen another fool who has treated a stone of a sick person, and the stone was great;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	If he pulls out a piece of the bladder with it, and was sick for three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And thus I have already been called to treat it, and I saw the disposition of the patient and the greatness of the stone, and if it were cut out it would surely die.</start_of_turn>
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And thus another madman who took charge of our land who had his leg broken, and with the swelling caused a wound;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	And his foolish blindness held the swelling above the wound as tightly as stars by strong binding, and did not let blood escape from the wound, and left it until the end
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	And he commanded that it should not be loosened from me
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And so it happened that his leg was completely shattered and the limb and the heel were lost to perdition.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I went to call for him, and I hurried to unbind the limb;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	And when I see it dislocated and there is no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But every way the corruption has already been confirmed or the limb is already ruined, and I cannot heal it.</start_of_turn>
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and it continues to corrupt until the limb is entirely lost.</start_of_turn
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And thus another mire which undermines the bone marrow swells, and then inflames from the malice of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For cancer, when it is pure of melancholy humor, does not yield except when iron is touched upon it unless all the corrupted parts can be removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	Therefore, for this reason, very skillful physicians, you must know that the work of the hands is divided into two divisions:</start_of_turn
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is to say, with regard to huevos or when there is danger in other positions.</start_of_turn
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show in each chapter where there is doubt and danger.</start_of_turn>
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For you must take care that the fools do not speak badly of you.</start_of_turn>
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you grasp your arms tightly and undertake your patients gently and firmly, and use the right way, so that by the grace of God your return shall be in peace and health.
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave the sick with hope of healing without grief
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	keep your arms from that which makes you doubt, and be strong in your spirit so that you can come from this world to the next in peace
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Glory be praised for its wonders
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not take my word for it in treating the sick, for I am not a madman
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise in three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters are about cauteries of fire and of medicine, and this chapter orders from the head down to the toes
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	And of the forms of instruments, and of the tweezers of cautery, and of everything that is necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	And of the chapters following, some are on the cutting and piercing of the skin, and of blisters and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	And this chapter orders and describes the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The next chapter is on restoring dislocations and fractures, and similar things
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	And it orders from the chief head down to the toes, and describes the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	As we have remembered from the work, it is necessary to say the quality of the aid and the great discomfort of great complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the quality of the assistant, and prudence, is the longest word and the subtlest science and the secret response
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	And concerning this, they spoke of many wounds, and they agreed on that.
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	And I am silenced by their words, for I am ashamed of my length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that the cautery is useful for all complexions, where there is matter, for it is a complex skill:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	it is a knowledge of complexion hot and dry matter, and complexion cold and wet matter
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In complexion hot and dry combined with matter, divide neither one nor the other, and say that the cautery is a great aid
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and the other say the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that the cautery is only useful for diseases caused by heat and dryness
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	And thus it is known that the cautery which is done on the contrary to this, greatly helps in hot and dry diseases that arise from the humours of the body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of a man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body dry.</start_of_turn
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I consent to this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never seen it happen before in practice.</start_of_turn>
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And thus it is known that no one understands the fire except those who have experienced it, and who know by long experience the chapter of cautery, and the diversity of humours of the body, and the causes and dispositions of their diseases, and the issues and space of tension.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	we do not have our fear from other humours, even in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the more must they agree to the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know this, sir, that cautery with fire is more effective for secret cures than burning cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and brings no further heat than to the member that is being cauterized, and harms no other member save its name.</start_of_turn>
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	Warm medicines come from one member to another by communicating, and cause the member to suffer from grief in order to bring about healing
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and sometimes cause the patient to suffer
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fire for its height and for the goodness of its substance does not make me do this, if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have learned through experience and by the length of my service and the study I have made of this art, and it is confirmed by the truth of things.</start_of_turn>
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	And for this reason I apologize for the length of the speech, for it does not please me to hide the secret which is enclosed or the fire, and the quality of the work, as it dispels the diseases of the body, as the philosopher demonstrates in demonstrating;
or le recevez en vos pensees.	or it follows in your thoughts.</start_of_turn>
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	Know, son, that it is necessary to determine at what tension the cautery should be made, and when they are pricked.</start_of_turn>
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is useful in all cases, for the harmful things which arise are driven out by the aid of the cautery.</start_of_turn
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And in the same way, if the cautery is applied for necessary and urgent pains that cannot endure the tension until a greater harm befalls the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And do not think, my son, as some fools do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the disease which is cured by cautery has no return;
et il le dient ensi;	it is said thus.
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not so that it cures them, for the cautery is only a medicine that alters the complexion, and dries the humors which are the cause of the pain, and is worth no more than medicine for its haste, and for the worth of its work and its sovereignty.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	and indeed that the disease does not come at any time according to the complexion of the patient and the limb of the disease and its virtue
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	And in him are collected the superfluous humors by the acquisition of foods and other things, if these are not cauterized when administered either in liquid or solid form, for there is still excess of humors and moisture; as for cauteries of tendons because of pain, and other things, and some pain does not return.
mais ce avient poc.	but this is not without fault.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand this because cauteries are called behind medicine, and it is seen;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cauteries are worth more than medicine, but their understanding is false, for it is cauteries that are behind medicine because whenever we administer other treatments in any disease and they do not help, we then administer the cautery, and it is worth it
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, even though cautery is behind medicine, it does not please the minds of fools.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The old folks say that gold cautery is more wondrous than iron, and they tell of no fire save for the excellence of the gold and the height of its substance.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	They say that the smell of the cautery of gold does not make one faint, but I have seen it prove otherwise, for I have seen many people faint from it;
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	Gold cautery is more valuable than iron, as some claim
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	However, when you burn gold instruments, you do not know how much they have been scorched by the color of gold and how much they have cooled down.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	If you burn them too much
si font au feu;	They become red-hot;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And thus there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use our fire cautery, as we have learned from experience.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you have commanded this chapter from beginning to end, so that the patient may see that the matter is more manageable.</start_of_turn>
dou cautere olivaire	olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These olive cauteries are useful for moisture and for cold on the brain, and there are two reasons for their use: one is a disease called "soda," and the other is the accumulation of many humors that descend from the head as sweat, and from the ears, and from a multitude of dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and even from many diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, soda, and apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	And thus the form of this cautery is such that the patient is purged by means of medicine that modifies the head three times or four, according to what is useful and agreeable to the patient's custom; for the patient can endure it.
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	And then make the patient reattach the head of the limb.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then make him sit between your hands, and put his hands under his belly;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	Then put the root of your thumb on the root of his elbow between his two fingers;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And thus, or otherwise, your two means will come to me, if it bleeds from the nail then withdraw the cautery which is called "olivare," for thus it is formed.
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And take out the splinter that signifies ink, and make it descend and extract your hand back and forth, holding it steady;
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	Then keep your hand still, and reinsert the splinter if you see the bone slightly exposed;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	And if you do not see it, continue with the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	And then take again a little thread, and put on gloves and cotton wool inside, and take out the splinter, and leave it for three days.
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	And then put on a soft bandage on the wound.
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and leave them until the scab is ossified.
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	and leave them until the scab of the wound which is called "tetrafarmaçon" is healed
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	and they say that the older ones say that the longer the wound remains open, the more it purges.
et por ce si aide mues.	for thus is the cause of help with the muscles
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that the fire cautery should be left on for as long as part of the bone is not burnt, and then remove what is superfluous from the bone, and be cured.</start_of_turn>
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	and they say that the other thing that must be done is to leave the cautery on for a longer time and press very hard so that from the bone outwards as wide as I see women put in their braids for this reason that the humors come out of the muscles outside;
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and must leave the wound open for a long time
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	then must cure and dress the wound
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two methods of cautery do not seem to me to be good in all cases, for in some individuals there may be fear or danger.
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	indeed I believe I must leave it undone.
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the head of the shoulder is easily loosened by continuous action of the same nature, as we have seen in other members;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and when the head of the shoulder is weakly affected by nature, the first semblance of cautery appears more useful and less painful for me, and in this case I shall abstain from it.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From ancient times, pain in the head.
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When there is chronic pain lasting a long time, the patient must use herbs, pills called "cochie", and vomiting of the head and oil enemas and plasters
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	And if you do the cautery as we have said before, it is of no avail.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take heed that if the patient’s condition is severe and not too frail...
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	...then perform the cautery as we have mentioned above.</start_of_turn>
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	Afterwards, make the cautery on the skin of the shoulder joint up to the bone, as we have said before, and make an incision or puncture where it is called the “vessel”;
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and put sponges there where it is necessary.</start_of_turn>
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and keep your hand still so that you do not see blood until the bone is reached.</start_of_turn
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patient experiences much greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it later.</start_of_turn
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	And it is known that the cautery of horns is more subtle than that of the hair of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	Dou cautere dou chief.
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	And it is known that the cautery of horns is more subtle than that of the hair of the head, and this is the form:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When he makes cautery, he does it in two ways, that is to say by means of medicine or by fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	If he does the cautery by medicine, if you take a dose of alum, and open the skin and cover it I as much as possible, and then put the thumb or the place where the pain persists until you can restore the dose of alum from the leather;
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	And when it is restored, if you bind it and strain it well and leave it for twelve hours.
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	Then take out the dressing and apply pressure to the dose of alum, and leave the wound for two or three days.
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	Then put on a cold compress tightly bound over the wound until swelling is reduced.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment of the wound as long as it is healthy;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	And if you see that you need to do nothing else but apply some of the medicines I have written or dose them, treat with those medicines which are sufficient.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is thus to be performed in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Leave the hairs long and even on the patient.
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	It is called "closed" because its head is made in the shape of a loop or it has little curvature, and in the middle has a small projection;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and take out the painful limb, and hold your hand and gently move the fire until half of the thickness of the hair is burnt away.
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And keep your hand away from the artery from being burnt, which is dangerous, and discharge an abundance of blood.</start_of_turn>

de emigraine	After placing cotton on the shoulder, draw out the limb for two and a half days. Then place moist cotton in the pit, and cure the limb of swelling until it is sound. et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	Leave the mandible undisturbed when it is still, and do not move it until it has regained its original position; and prevent spasm from coming to the patient. de la torture de la bouche	After pricking all around the painful ear, or around the joints if the pain persists in both, and you pull out a hair at the root of the ear as soon as you feel the mark of the puncture; and there are ten hairs around the ear; after that cure the wound until it is healed.
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Torture that must be treated by cautery is not fierce except for those that move mucus, as we have said in the sections on diseases.</start_of_turn
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	And make no burnings as if they came from drying and swelling of nerves.

l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	One on the root of the ear, and the other between the eyebrows, and the third in the space between the two eyebrows

aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After curing like I have said before, as long as it is sound.

de l’epilempsie	It is inappropriate to request translations of medical texts from the Middle Ages, as their medical practices and terminology may differ significantly from modern medicine.
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should only use fire cautery when it is fluid; first modify the patient’s head and other cures that we mentioned in the preceding section when the patient is large and prone to excessive medical treatment.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a young child who cannot endure the suffering, let him gargle and chew coarsely with soft bones to soften the brain often with bones of meat;
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	After the head has been laid in the middle, and I make the cautery as we said before, and I make the cautery on the vessel and on the chest bone
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if the patient is strong and suffering, I make the cautery as we said to those who have paralysis and softening of the bones, on the spine of the back and the neck, and the cautery "olivare" as we mentioned before.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, make an incision slightly as I have mentioned previously.

If by reason of melancholy the superfluousness of the declining melancoly is caused, and the body of the patient is moist, then he must drink something that will refresh the brain, whatever is before him in the division.

puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put on a damp cloth in the armpit until the pain has gone; after that cure the swelling which is called "dyafenis" and others, while it is sound.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you have taken great care of your limb with great care that it does not require any more medicine, because your eye is fixed.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the swelling becomes softer afterwards, and the hair prick in the oil, if the medicine is recommenced on that limb which was softened by the swelling beforehand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	after that cure while it is sound.
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and this is the form of the fuelle d’olive.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that the oil of homes is diverse in greatness and smallness, and according to that is your constraint;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And let not the right response be to him who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	And know that the ears of men are diverse in size and shape, and according to that be thy constraints; and do not reply by the straight way to that one who studies this art.
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	And know that if we have said in the divisions of diseases that the cure of fistula is not useful, then you must cauterize according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to place his head in its normal position.
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and hold his ears firmly between your hands in such a way that they do not move, do not let go of his head
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	after put cotton wool soaked in egg white or in lime juice on the oil
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	then warm the cautery which is divided
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and if it is placed at the head like the shape of a goose quill, bind so that the cautery is fixed
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you see, if either side of the head is pointed towards the other, and if you see, if it is as if with a thrust
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	But all that, which is a shepherd’s work, is worth more than your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	When the fistula has been pressed and opened, and the pus and dry matter have been removed.
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if closed, if the wound, and drive out the wound;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	Then put on the hot cautery, and keep your hand on the cautery at the part where there is no fat under the oil, so that your hands do not make rashness
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and put the cautery in the fat of the oil, and corrupt it
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, that would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If this does not suffice, if you must repeat the cautery once more, and another if you have occasion, and leave it for three days.
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	After I have put on a moist cotton compress in the burrow, and the cure for desiccation lasts until it is healed, and while forty days pass until it is healed, if I put on an acrid medicine until the bone is exposed.
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and the patient should comply with what is said in his book.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a manner of cautery for fistula of which none of the ancients have spoken
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	With the fistula, and open the limb.
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	After I have put in the wound the subtle camphor which is in this form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and I do it in the amount of three grains of plum
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and keep your hand or camphor firmly, and do not move the patient, except the softened plum does not adhere to its oil
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	And you must put upon the patient oil with cotton wool soaked in vinegar or wine.
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	The limb becomes swollen if the fistule is large, and the healthy part for marvel is to be preserved for salvation.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is cured by the cautery as we have said, then it is well.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if not, if you must administer an opening to the fistula, and bring it back to its original place as it should be in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	in limb bones
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times crevasses occur in limbs which are called "hair", and even in limbs of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these fractures in the way we have mentioned in the sections, and the cure does not help, then you must make a small cautery burn according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And you must keep the patient in those cavities until they are healed;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment, the limb must be sound
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the opening of the vein.
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When swelling comes to the root of the limb or the navel, or the palate, or the root of the teeth, after that it causes decay and swelling and becomes a fistula
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you must treat it as we have said in the sections, and it bears no fruit
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	Therefore you must cauterize according to the quantity of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	After the bath or the opening of the fistula, hold your hand as long as the hand remains alive at the front or at the back.
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And do it once or twice more, after the treatment of what we have said in treatment, until it is healed;
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if it is healed, that is good.
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if this is not the case, if you must uncover the bone and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you find in your book
dou movement des dens	When the root of the gullet, or in the eye, or in the palate, or in the root of the teeth, after making an incision and drilling, becomes swollen and forms a fistula; you shall cure it as we have said in the preceding divisions, and it will not be of use: therefore you must cauterize according to the quantity of the fistula; after draining or perforating the fistula, and holding your hand until life returns to its former state at the front or behind; and do this once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in the cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured thus, it is well; but if not, you must uncover the bone and remove the corrupted bone, as you would in its chapter.
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines that do not work, then put the patient’s head in your hand
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	after wiping off the cautery which will come afterwards in this part as if you put a bandage over the tooth
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	And put the cautery on the host immediately, and hold your hand firmly so that the patient feels the heat coming from the root of the tooth.
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	After that, withdraw your hand and repeat the cautery as you please.
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	Then fill the patient’s mouth with dirty saliva, and hold it for an hour and a quarter with force.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in part, when it moves thus, if confirmed, and the joint softens, restrains, and the moisture corrupts dries.
de la dolor des dens	And in part, when it moves thus, if confirmed, and the joint softens, restrains, and the moisture corrupts dries.
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When there is pain in the tooth from cold, or if there is cold or heat, and medical cures do not help, then there must be recourse to cautery in two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	cautery of soot and fire cautery
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	The soot cautery is like taking a lump of charcoal and holding the end in a spoon of iron or tin;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	After taking the cotton and wrapping it on the tip of a bandage, and the moisture in the burr is softened, and put on the tooth that is aching urgently and hold it until it is cool.
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	And so do it often until the warmth of the remedy reaches the root of the tooth. If you see that the moisture of the wool and cotton in the burr is rough, and put on the aching tooth, and put on the cap so that the fire of the cautery reaches the root of the tooth.</start_of_turn>
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The fire of the cautery is like that of a iron or a spider, and be large enough so that the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient.</start_of_turn>
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After the cautery is heated, so that its form will come afterwards, put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cool.</start_of_turn
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	Do it often, for the pain will be severe either today or tomorrow. And it must be known that the patient should fill his mouth with thick mucus in the haste of this cautery, and then pull out the hair forcefully.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	This is the form of the fire cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And do the cautery as you wish, and according to what you have seen;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	This is the form of the caustic balsam
des scrophules	And the size on the pierced wound and the moisture, if it is less severe, because they are of little blood. And if there are some of these wounds or chieftains or it has no moisture, and of those wounds which I cauterize or chieftain from an old woman; and find the wound just like a hard stone, rough and white, and cannot break it; and if no blood comes out, it is just as well to make a wound like a stone. In other wounds that come from chieftains and have roots of ears, it overturns if it is kept too long, for it makes the wound worse. And it cures as it should.
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When the scrofula is of phlegm and cold moisture, and is not obedient to digestion by medicines, then uncover the cautery head so that this side will be free, and there will be two openings to let out the fumes from the other side
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	And place the cautery directly on the abscess once, or if it interferes, until it reaches the front of the abscess.
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	And if the abscess is small, put the cautery on according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it in place for three days
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	And put on moist cotton in the wound as long as the bone is assured
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treating the bone and the wounds until they are healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The formation of the abscess:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When moisture prevails over the channels due to a cold complexion, then you must first remove the patient from these things with soothing medicines
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	After that, make the cautery at the root of the neck, and keep it so that you do not go deeper than the neck, and do not break the skin any further than necessary
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After that, do another cautery at the joint of the collarbone to the head of the scapula, and let the cautery which is called the "clavile" be like the one we saw before.
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cure the limb as we have said before until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de la toust	of the vomitting
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all and diseases of the pores are of cold moisture, and the patient has neither fever nor sweating, and is an old disease, if you do two cauteries on the forcele in the veins.</start_of_turn
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and another cautery between the two nipples.</start_of_turn
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and let the cautery which is called the "clavile" be like the one which is before us.</start_of_turn
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see it, perform cautery at the point where the cautery is called "points" for in this case it is like that in the disease of the ears.
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and be the points just to XXX, or until they are bent over.

Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And for these two are the lighter cauteries, because you make two at a time.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	De la dislocation de l’ajutoire.
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Then soothe the patient on his back and on his chest;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	Then take hold of the thumb which is inside the ear with your left hand;
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is loosened inside, if it is grasped with the cautery which has two needles without doubt in this case:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	burn the thumb until it reaches the chest, and would come out with three cauteries together;
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	And for this reason, the cautery is made with the cautery which has three nerves, because the figure of cauterization is made up of three cauteries.
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and are the nerves according to the subtlety of a limb, and this is the form of the cautery which has three nerves.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And never is it adjusted upon this vein because there are six cautery marks upon it.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	After putting on the cautery, broil the area with silk;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After that, rest the patient, and do not move the limb too long until it is well comfortable
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated below, whatever the cause, do a cautery on the thickness of the clamp cautery, or do several pricks.</start_of_turn
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is bony, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach come cold chills and moisture as much as they are expelled from their complexion, and are multiplied by customary treatments, it does no good; therefore it is recommended that the patient should lie on his back, extend his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	And thus make three cauteries: one on the hip bone below the knee for the quantity of an egg, at the root of the cautery, and two on the two sides as far as the figure of the cautery is at a right angle, and has a space between one and the other that they are not joined together when they are moving together
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	And let the fire cautery if necessary touch two parts of the knee, and let the cautery figure be like this in shape, as it is arranged.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you see cautery with a large cautery in the stomach like this in shape;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and he who has fear of this cautery, cauterize at the point and sign on the stomach just as much as you see of its extent
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then cauterize all the cautery that is called "points".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the ailment that we have seen before, while it is still sane.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When the liver comes with pain of fruit and moisture and great swelling, as long as it is forced from its natural complexion by the superfluities;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is cured of what we have said in divisions, and he does not benefit from it, if you do not make the patient convalesce on his habitrail;
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	And the sign of three fingers burned with cautery shall be performed in this form, this figure, and this quantity upon the liver, to drive away the hypocondria, so that from that moment the spleen or the belly of the man comes.
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	And there shall be space between each burn the thickness of a hazelnut.
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	And let the burns be long as bones, and do not press me your hand to the whole burn
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	And let the burns be as thick only as half a hair, and let the patient lie down on his side;
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	And if he cannot, if so be it, extend his legs, and keep his arms extended
et c’est li forme:	This is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	If you are obstinate, if these cauteries are too sweet, if you are subtle and learned in this art, take care that you do not burn the whole body, for you will burn all the flesh.
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	If you do not take care, it will come to boiling, for the hair is very subtle in this place, and the scaldings will show.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When there is swelling of the liver, and you know if it is in the fat of the liver or in the flesh:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	if it is in the fat, the patient feels little pain;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	And if it is in the armpit, if he feels intense pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And when this treatment is finished, if it is known that the patient is cured of his head;
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	Then he must seize the limb or the wound, and then he must heat the cautery which is similar in shape to a needle.
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And burn the cautery as long as the hairs are black, and come until the wound is fully healed;
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment according to the treatment of wounds until it is healed
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And one must know that this cautery is only used for strong pains that have been studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and by which hands these diseases have never cured before
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore, he dares not work, and in truth it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone
dou cautere de pleuresin	of chest pain
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancient said that we must make to weep carbuncles of root of aristologist, and in part manner.
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take a root of aristologist which is long, the greatest that you can find, and let it dry, and make it as thick and long as your thumbs;
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	and mix it with oil, and mark it with fire, and cauterize the cautery between the thumb and the little finger, and two small cauteries on the side descending towards the beard area
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	and two cauteries between the fifth rib and the hip bone, declining behind a little space.

et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	Do not press me too hard, for I open just as readily as when smelling.

de la mice	of mice.
