ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir;	or if there is a little loss of blood, that the point of a razor can enter there;
et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main;	and put the container of that potion into another container, and put alkali and chalk and sweet oil upon it, until there is one dose below the powders that you can take with your hand easily
et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	and leave it until it descends hot water and blood or pot is plumped, then take all this oil and spit it out on chalk and alkali as before
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres.	And in this way if there is moisture and it is administered in the midst of medical treatments and other cauteries of other members.
Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galiens tells us of a cure for the pain of the hip and the sciatic vein, and he says that no other cure was done, and that he was healed at one time when they did this cure, and he bathed as he is taught afterwards.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	And take in part a handful of fresh and dry barley, break it down with a little fat, and put on the hip, thigh and leg where the pain persists, and bind.
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And leave it for three hours, so that the patient no longer feels the burning sensation.</start_of_turn>
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	Then let him enter the bath or wash as long as his body is relaxed, and let him enter the water or lie down, and the pain will vanish and be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And let no one use the fire cautery of such medicines, except after the evacuation of blood.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with fine hair, if it helps with saliva.</start_of_turn>
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	It must be done cautiously.</start_of_turn
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take lint and soak it in oil, and put it on the pit between the thumb and the great toe and the one that is called fossicle.</start_of_turn
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	After taking fine hair dry, grasp it with fire until it is charred, and put on wool, and leave it until it is stained.</start_of_turn
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	And do it again, and do not stop doing it until you think by sense that it is coming until the hip, and that the pain is gone.</start_of_turn
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	And this manner of cautery is called "cautery of the limb.
de la dolor dou dos	of backache.</start_of_turn>
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes from the back, or from sitting or percussion or from too great an evacuation, or from similar things of cold expanding matter, none of these signs are worth cautery, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir;	And it is to be known that when the patient is free from foul pus or other things, that we make this upon the back, loin or where the pain is found, three lines signed with a needle, and in each line five cauteries or more as is necessary for the virtue and the quantity that the patient can endure.
et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»;	And let the cautery be made according to the cautery which is called "points".
et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	And if you see, make three cauteries or four at the middle cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor;	Many times this disease comes as a small wound, and the sign of its beginning is that it has burst open when it happens, and fear
et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	And you find in the back bone of the shoulder and in us the appearance that comes after the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it healed, if you cauterize at the cautery of this circle in this fashion.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the fire cautery burns some part of the spine, it increases.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see that the burn penetrates the spine as much as two or three lines, and that the points are close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After treating the wound as much as necessary, and when it is healed as we have said, keep the cautery away from the bone which is close to a nerve
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere:	When joint pain arises from moisture that has spread throughout the limb and the pain comes in lumps, that they call "podagre" properly; and when the cause is cold and the disease is cured by medicine, it cannot be cured; but if it is cured by cautery in part manner.
fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	makes the mouth of the cautery enter the joint of the bone, and either the olive cautery is to be taken in this fashion:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary to prick on the face of the bone, do not make the burn with the whole cautery; rather mark it with the word "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire;	And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, if you make the cautery on each knee three cautery or four of each side, with the whole olive cautery;
et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	If you must do more, if you make more of it, but do not hold your hand firmly until the expected hour has passed.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend down to the groin and the back, administer the cautery as we have said in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes;	If the pains are at the fingertips, if you make holes two lines deep in the flesh;
et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main;	And if there remains no pain in that place, if you make holes above the joint and on the nail of the hand;
et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains come up to the hips or to the shoulders, if you cauterize some part, and make the patient bear well and prescribe medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you make him drink and purge phlegm, he will be healed by the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	from the root to the surface
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor;	When the pulse comes in anger, and the bowels descend like stones, it is new, if you can believe it, that when you see the cure, it does not make him vomit that matter.
et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre;	and that he uses things that let go of the belly, so that the pains descend from his belly
aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors;	after that, make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his arm tight until the bowels are repaired, and keep them close to you, and sign the pulse above the collarbone, and at all signs that there is like half of a circle below the ribs
puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Then withdraw the fire cautery; thus is the form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	As long as he is limp and groans senselessly.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu;	Then withdraw the fire cautery; thus is the form: withdraw the hair at its root.
et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier;	and hold the eyes steady so they do not move back;
et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains;	and well cover the wounds of the patient, and put some lint and a bandage on the wounds, and another on his hand that holds the eyes;
puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os;	then put the cautery on the sign at the whole hand, and keep it straight and hold it until you touch the bone, and if you do not touch it the first time, if you do it again as many times as you live until you reach the bone;
et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere;	and be careful that the hair does not slip when you are doing the cautery.
que tu ne le brulasses;	Do not burn it;
et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Do not burn it; and let the patient not suffer further harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And soaks that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is in vain.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure;	And you must know that the cautery of the veins must be subtle according to the measure of the small ones, and of the great people also in their measure
aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	After three days, cure the limb of the burn as long as the scab has become ossified.
aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee;	After curing other ailments, keep the patient lying down for forty days on his back until the wound is well healed
et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And you must know that his movements must be gentle and long, so that the fluid does not come out when he moves to go to bed
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors;	And after forty days, when he wants to rise, there appears a well-made mark, and he bears it for forty days more.
et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire;	and has had good rest, that he works little and avoids eating too much drink and meat, and excessive laughter.
et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	and when he has done this teaching, he is entirely healed.</start_of_turn>
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I shall speak of the cure of the tail in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	Of the evacuation of the belly.
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur;	When wounds come in other parts and are known, and you see that they do not grow any more, then you make the fire cautery again according to their quantity, and take away a third of the burn.</start_of_turn
aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit;	after the cure according to what we have said.</start_of_turn
et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	and none of the former have said that it should be cauterized with the fire cautery at three angles according to this shape.</start_of_turn>
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first sign the limb well and make a line along the width of the wound, and another at the bottom, and hold your hand firmly with all your might on the burn cautery clamp
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first burnings are lighter and milder.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	than the old ones in any limb.
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any limb, or to the hip or to the wound, and this pain lasts a long time, and the medical cure is not worth it, then it is advisable to burn it with the cautery which is called “points,” and to burn it according to the length of the limb and the width and its weakness and its toughness and its twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien;	If he is sane at the first cautery, that is well;
se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If so, commence another cautery on that one, because it is customary that it must move to the neighboring limb, so that you can make the cauteries until the patient is sane.</start_of_turn>
de meselerie	When pain arises in any limb, be it from sitting or injury, and this pain persists for a long time, and the medical cure proves useless, then it is appropriate to cauterize using the cautery called "poins," or to cauterize according to the length of the limb, its breadth and weakness, its toughness and flexibility, and its location of torsion and pain. If it is cured after the first cautery, that is well; if not, repeat the procedure. Indeed, it is customary to perform subsequent cauteries on the adjacent part of the limb so that you can make the cauteries until the patient is cured.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The disease never helps itself with a cautery, and even the sickness that comes from the corruption of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	Can you see the cautery being performed? Take guard if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and do not linger or stay, for you doubt that the corruption does not spread throughout the whole illness, so you make five cauteries on the head.</start_of_turn
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	I make the head new, and the other towards the front at the end of the beard.</start_of_turn
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	And on the two horns, and one behind the heel.
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	And I leave the hand as long as the cautery comes up to the bone, and as long as the scabs come out forcefully so that the vapors of the humors can escape.
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	And I cauterize on the mouse according to what is before me
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	And if the moisture is scattered everywhere;
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	and I cauterize thus in the manner we have said or in chief, and I cauterize on the nape of the neck, and two on the shoulder blades, and one on the armpit and one on the elbow and two on the two hips
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	And II on the flanks, and II on the strings of the teeth, and I on the knuckles of the hands and feet, and on the sockets of the hands.
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	And beware of the nerves that are under the calcaneus bone, do not burn them.
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	Never perform cautery on the os pisiform, or on the os of the stomach, or on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	And as many times as you make cautery, the more you will help, and the more benefit you will do.
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And the patients do not feel pain from the cautery if they already feel it, because the flesh is already corrupted
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And you must know that the burn should be large and small according to the members and joints, as you will do in handling various objects.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treating the wound with flour from time to time with honey and other cures until it is healed
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	When swelling comes to any limb and is cured by medicines, oils, and plasters, and is not serious, then you must perform cautery on the limb according to the greatness and smallness of the limb;
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	And let the cautery be applied in the middle of the wound, as thick as the current.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then hold the edges of the wound steady until it has healed completely.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	And never do we burn with the cautery on the hand, arm, or back, at the exit of nerves that cause the limb to move, and if so it swells the bone
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	and do not put anything in the way that hinders the movement of bones and nerves
de albaras	When swelling occurs in any limb and is cured by medicines, oils, and plasters, and is not completely healed, then it is necessary to perform cautery on the limb according to the size and severity of the swelling; and let the burn penetrate deeply into the flesh. Then cure with unguents until the swelling is healed. And never perform cautery on the hand, foot, or back, at the opening of a nerve that causes the limb to move, or if it is bony swelling; and in no case should anything interfere with it except one who is skilled in limbs and the issues of the moving nerves and bones.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	When the ailment called "albaras" is inflamed, and no medicine will help, then burn with a cautery a little in the middle, according to the thickness of the wound, until the blood is ossified and has changed colour;
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	Then the cure of wheat sometimes and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of colon and blood of alder, one part of each.
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then mix them all together, or bind them with a bandage, and keep it warm until it is healed
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure for fistula by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a boil comes at the beginning, and you see it stop, if you burn it with the cautery that seems like a circle, all around the boil.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	And all these things say that the burn is made in the middle of the abscess.
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	And I do not think that this is good, because I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen many times;
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And the right thing is to cauterize thoroughly, with the burn that is called the circle, as we have said before
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be measured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	When anyone has an ailment called "adubelati", and it delays in healing or through the excess it causes or because of the severity of the disease when it is decrepit (that is, too great), and there is much blood, or by the tension;
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	and you see it haste to heal.
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	then you should make cautery around the mouth of the wound with little cauteries in pricking;
aprés le laisse ensi.	and leave it like that.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will haste to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it turning pale with all the cautery, if the burn is large:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of this disease which is called "adubelati" until the cauteries have perceived the cold, and be such cauteries as the patient feels the pain depart in part as the process of putrefaction is accelerated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards, cure as long as he is perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cautery. Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another symptom of disease is called "corrodens," which is nothing other than the swelling of a limb, because it softens the bones like dry leather.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	If you see this ailment in which it is possible to suffer from cautery together with fire, then withdraw the large and small cauteries slowly and gently, as it is convenient for the limb or for the disease itself
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	then cauterize all the parts until you have eradicated all the corruption, and nothing remains except the bone itself
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized limbs, and cover them with oil until the blisters from the fire are ossified, and all the corruption.</start_of_turn
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of external medicines that cause carbuncles.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	And if you see after three days that the hair has not grown, that is well;
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if this does not happen, if you repeat the cautery on that which remains corrupted from the corrupt flesh.</start_of_turn>
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	And this matter is never cured by medicine except by fire cautery.</start_of_turn
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	but indeed fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure of medicine by water in the division.</start_of_turn>
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	take as much as you need.</start_of_turn
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	from pores that come as pieces
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often there arises a disease from the swelling of the feet, which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and is a great burdensome thing that swells the feet
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery of this disease is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery and hot water cautery
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	Fire cautery, if you are sparing one, do as with a pin of wool, and make it of good iron to the measure that it can penetrate the hair of all parts, and that there be slight margins;
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	After he puts everything on high above the cloud, and turns his hand all around the cloud as much as it comes to the front of the cloud;
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	and let him stay there for three days until it begins to putrefy.
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Then make him a poultice of bruised elderberries crushed with wool, and leave the poultice on all night, and bind his wound tightly and it will be extracted from its root.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	If thou art scorched by fire, I order thee to cauterise as doth a needle of wool. Make it of good iron of the measure that it may penetrate the heel of all parts, and leave subtle margins. Then put all about the heel, and lay thy hand round the heel until it comes to the front of the heel; and leave it there for three days until it begins to yield. Then make an embolus of wild mallow bruised with gel, and leave the embolus upon all night, and bind it firmly and it shall be plucked from its root.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	And if they are converted by boils, and often happen in hands and feet, if you must, bring a hot cautery there
et est en teil maniere:	it is in part like this:
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	take a needle of spiderwort or iron, or a piece of guttawel, and put on the cloud and the thread, which is to say little wrinkles;
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	And put the bandage upon so that it encompasses all around, then put a little ball of wool warm, and hold your hand well, and press your hand backwards so that the margin of the bandage comes to the root of the nail, and you will find the warm water deep until the root.
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	And offer the patient a little the biting of the warm water for an hour.
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	Then leave it like that, and it will discharge all its roots
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	So do another like that, until you have plucked out all that is at the source, and cure the sores that cause pain.
li cure dou trembler	you cure the tremor.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	When there are tremors of cold from nerves, or of quartan fever or of another kind, if you must, do three cauteries or four on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	and one on the hip or on the stomach at the olive cautery
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	If you let him tremble, and he will hasten the healing of the cold disease.
des pustules puans	When some tremble from cold, or from quartan fever or from any other cause, if you make for them three or four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, and one cautery or pinch on the stomach at the olive cautery, if you leave them to tremble, they will haste the recovery from the cold sickness.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never do wounds appear by chance, or boils filled with pus, which come from corrupted matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	When you first notice that we are performing cautery on each head of the pustule:
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	A subtle charcoal cautery of mustard seed, or that its point should be grasped by the fire, or of long aristoloke root, or the lenticular cautery
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	And never at the beginning when they begin, according to this manner, do they pierce forward, but are broken by the excess from which they come, and are healed;
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is severed.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	Many times there are great discharges of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes from the surgeon, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things;
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	It is a great shame thing to prolong.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	And whenever this happens without any [apparent] cause, if you hastily put your thumb on the wound of the vein, and hold it too tightly without calming the pain, no blood will issue any longer;
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	Then apply the olive cautery to the wound several times, making them small and large until they are all red;
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Then I take hold of it, great or small according to the wound and the position of the limb where the artery is straight, and put the cautery on that vein or hold your thumb there, and hold the cautery as long as it is not fixed
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts out when you take your thumb away from the vein, and the cautery is finished, take hold urgently of another cautery that is on the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	And do not stop doing this one after the other until the bleeding stops
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	And beware that you do not tear away the nerve that is below, and that no other harm comes upon the patient.
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	And keep that when the artery is large, without bursting, we cannot well fill it again without closing it in three ways which we have mentioned before.
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	Or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong ligation with thread, or by medicines placed above which have the power to stop bleeding;
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And let it be bound and strained afterwards.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will bring about a lasting restoration of the limb except by the strict draping of cloths or the application of hot things upon it, or other similar things, if it does not profit thereby in some way.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	And if this happens to him at no time and there is no remedy or medicine present, if he must put his thumb on the wound of the vein as we have said, and hold it firmly until it is healed above the wound and above the vein;
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	And do not move it [the shoulder], but moisten it with cold water often so that it becomes cold as ice until it becomes frozen and swells and rests.
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And make inquiry beforehand concerning that on which you must perform cautery and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	We have already said in the first chapter that every ailment for which cautery of fire or burning medicine is recommended, we must know the odiums, causes, instruments and forms of the cautery.
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	and I put this chapter of the head down to the foot, and I will speak of this chapter in the same way as forasmuch as we find it more conveniently in this way
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus, as I begin this chapter, it is necessary to say, my dear friend, that in this chapter there is more peril and fear than in all the previous cauteries, and for this reason it is necessary to take greater caution
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	Where there is doubt and fear, and comes the death of many.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I advise you not to be rash
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For in various ways people come to cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	When there is such fear, which comes with their ailment, that they move carelessly because of the suffering of their ailment, and from the greatness of their malice;
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And for this reason we must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	And for this reason there is sense in it, and it says:
«atendez, je sui garis»;	Wait, I am ready;».
et li maladie est despitouse.	and the ailment is grievous.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	You must only trust those who come to your aid who have this manner, but put more caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not be reckless but thoughtfully of what you are certain, and what you can have taken and lost;
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	And use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients so that health is either preserved or transformed.
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	and this will help you to achieve lasting fame, glory, and lasting memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, our Sirs, you must take good understanding and diligence, and if you yearn to be inspired by the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter in dividing by chapters, according to what is before or the chapter of cautery, that I have devised from the head to the toes, because you will find it more readily what you have to master.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Or I have commanded this chapter to be divided into chapters, according to what precedes or the chapter of cautery, that I have devised from the head to the toes, because you will more easily find what you have to learn.</start_of_turn>
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	The diseases which often accompany childbirth cause the head of the child to swell excessively; and when the swelling is too great, the head of the child is strained too much
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	and never is this caused by any other reason than that it has not been treated
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	I have never seen this disease except in childbirth, and with all those who have given birth;
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	therefore I believe that it is better for me to omit some parts of the work in order to heal the disease.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	And I saw a child whose shoulder was swollen with fluid, and the head was growing so large that he could not bear it.
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	and the moisture was so great that it became blood, and this blood if it is gathered together under the bone on the hump, between the bone and the marrow
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	when the moisture is between the bone and the marrow, and the abscess is small, you must make a wide incision at the head of the bone
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	and as long as the moisture remains corrected
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	and when the limb is restored to its normal position:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper and the incision is larger, if you make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the sutures of the head split over a wide area, and there is pain when you press your hand into it, and this does not return
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	If it seems that you have made three incisions here in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, drain out all the moisture forcefully.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	If it seems that you have made three incisions here in this manner: after that restrain the incisions of cloth and powder, and put wine and oil, and leave in place for five days.
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	Then take out the dressing, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and leave the head of the shoulder tightly bound, and give the patient dry meat from the same amount of moisture as before the limb is comfortable and healed
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	And another method of incision is that you look or open the size of the abscess, and collect the fluid.
car aucune fois est elle devant;	For it never comes to that;
aucune fois derrier;	Never before; never behind
aucune fois en destre;	Never in distress;
et aucune fois en senestre.	Never in distress; and never in weakness.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	and beware that you do not cover the artery;
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	and the vein will bleed blood, so that the patient dies from excessive bleeding and the evacuation of moisture
de reume	When the shoulder or the armpit is open, and the filling of the water, and you do as you please with it; and beware that you do not cover the artery; and let the vein flow blood, so that the patient does not die from excessive bleeding and moisture discharge.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When there is no known disease which is called "catarrh," and there is pus or a wound, and the disease is ancient, and the cure of medicine does not help, then the only cure is to cauterize with this that you cover the arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	You must therefore keep it covered, so that you do not see it covered, that the patient makes his head move back;
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	after you have wiped the limb with a rough cloth so that the arteries open, then stretch the patient’s neck with all your might
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	Then look if the vein bursts, and the blood from one and the other side is behind the ears, and then they are replaced.
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then mark the blood vessels, then grasp one and the other with a sharp clamp of two parts, as long as the vein reaches the bone, and that is from the large end of the head
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	If you see, hold the sponge below the artery and grasp above, cutting as much as two fingers deep.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	When the vein is cut, if blood spurts continuously, keep pressure on it without interruption.</start_of_turn>
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	And if the artery does not open by feeling, if you must measure the amount of space of three fingers, then mark it and do so until the bone;
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	And that which must be put away if there is blood, if it is six fingers, and by chance more or less, according to what the patient can suffer, and the refilling of the artery.
puis regarde la plaie:	Then look at the wound:
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone point where the abscess has burst, if the wound edges are raw and do not bleed, then strain the wound and ligate it, and cure it with oil until it is healed.
de emigrainne	If the artery does not open on inspection, if you suspect it is obstructed by a foreign body, measure the distance of two finger-widths, then mark the spot and proceed until you reach bone.  If there is blood loss of more than a quarter, and sometimes less or more, according to what the patient can tolerate and the refilling of the artery, then look at the wound: if it remains over the point where the artery was opened, if the surrounding tissue does not swell, then strain the wound and bind it, and treat the wound with oil until it is healed.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient weeping comes, and acute catarrh, because of the moisture of tears and the phlegm in the temples and the ancient saliva weaken and similar things, it is cured by means of medical treatments and all that does not benefit it, if we extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	And the method of extracting them is that if the patient frequently bites his temples, understand the artery that opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is much more easily closed than in other men who are too cold;
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	and if it is closed, strain the patient’s neck with some bandages, then rub the limb of no rough hair, and rise the limb of warm water until the artery appears open again
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Then take the sponge which is like this:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	Then take the sponge which is like this. Lightly scratch the skin until you reach the artery, then lift it up and take hold of the veins above the wound; remove the cloths that are underneath that part of the chest.
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	And if the artery is thin, if the clot is at the tip of the bone, then cut that part according to the quantity of blood that comes out
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not securely held, if it does not leap without doubt in all things.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	And take out blood six cubic centimeters, just until three
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	And if the artery is great, if you can, tie it up with two threads of strong silk, so that no blood flows in front of the healing of the wound, and let the blood flow out naturally
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	Then grasp the surplus that is between the two lines in that hour, and if you see it, if you cauterize with a blunt cautery until the head is cut off, the bone will be severed.
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And this is the painful thing, if the patient has no fever and is of a fair complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	For the cautery is useful for finishing off the moisture:
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	because it is more useful for moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	Or it is useful for extracting arteries that are filled with much cotton and put on tension well made
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and when they are loosened, if they are cured with dry medicines that cause the growth of hair, and tension, as long as they are sane

et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	And what is more languid and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery cutting through two parts, but the cutting should be well spaced in order to keep it longer warm.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too tight, it holds less heat.

et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	And let them be separated between the two shoulders because it is not enough soured from this burn throughout.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	This is the form of the burn:
des larmes	The fire must have between the joints of the handle a space of one inch; then when you have signed with the needle the bones, and you must let the loop of the burn be burning over until it comes up to the bone, and close the vein in one inch of bones; and let them be separated between the bones because it is not well soldered by this cautery in any way; and this is the form of the cautery: tears.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears of the eyes descend from the veins that are above the root of the arm, and it does not profit from any medical cure that we do, and you see the face of the patient twisted, and feels his front limp as from drunkenness;
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure. Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And they call it the old "contusion", and that you make at the patient who has this disease the hairs that he has or front, and then make three incisions or front equally according to the length of the front

de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the hairs
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Pus is an ointment that is made from rags of papers soaked in oil, and this causes more pain to no one, and causes the eyes to water, and comes the tearing out of the morning, and they cannot see the sunlight because the tears hurry out of their eyes.</start_of_turn
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	And for this reason they sleep with their faces towards the ground, and sleep on their backs, and their papery rags are wet with moisture that inflates and appears to cover them with pus from the ointment.</start_of_turn
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the limb towards your chest and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And thus the patient should place his head in his armpit.
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	Then take a bandage of linen, and make a loop in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains the excess of flesh from the chest part, and put it on him
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press from both sides, so that the excess is gathered in the circle
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then make in the middle of the moisture a wound as wide as a vein, and do not make it any larger than the wound made to the blood vessel
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and tighten the skin as much as you see to the excess
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in many cases the excess comes out of the wound, according to the shape of a white fat piece.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Remove the thumb entirely from the thick flesh between your thumbs, and bend your hand towards the right and left as much as possible;
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and keep that you do not tear the membrane, that you do not move the palm all the way to the edge, that you do not bleed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if it does not come out at the beginning of the incision, if you see a little piece of flesh, widen the incision slightly so that it comes out.</start_of_turn>
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	Then take it out as we have said, then moisten with gauze and water, and put on the limb, and strain gently.</start_of_turn
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such homes that break wind and put on top to corrupt this moisture that remains immobile.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it as long as it is sane
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to opening an abscess, the cure of packing absorbs as much as it is possible while it is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	hair of papers</start_of_turn>
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When paper nails grow long, do not cut them except as nature dictates, and when they are inflamed, if they irritate the eyes, they cause tears, and generate various diseases as tears are accustomed to and soften paper and mucus, as long as this is the cause of the irritation of the eyes.</start_of_turn
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	And it is the cure in three ways:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	Or by complete fire cautery, or by water-based medicine as it is before or alongside the fire cautery, and it is made by incision and suture or by sutures, as I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	You must put the patient’s head in your right hand, and take the oil from your left hand;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	If it is softened, that is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if not, if there is a splinter in all its fibers;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and let the hair grow at the margin of the wound or the hair grows from these hairs, and pull out the hair at its root and rejoin it at the tip

puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	Then pull out the thread and put on the papere a little loop of cotton and bandage, then mark on the papere a sign like a berry of mistletoe, and behold that the sign be in proportion to the quantity that you see elevate the papere that is destined for you
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if there is part which has mixed with it a great quantity of the papere according to what the papere is softened;
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	Then make throughout the whole circumference on the two lines that you have marked, from the great toe to the little one
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	And let there be one of the incisions close to the hair roots in the thickness of a root, then hold the ointment in one of the two angles downward, and then burn it all.

et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	If this does not suffice, if there is no improvement, then leave the suture and the thread for three days or four;
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	Then treat the wound with dry and constricting things, because the pus comes out at the bottom of the wound and joins together, but the suture is useless (as they say the old men), and this is work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere:	And if in another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if in another way: if you mark the mark of a figure which is like the fuelle of a myrtle, as we have said, at three inches deviate according to the shape which is like this.

mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	But the costure in one and in the other is more artificial
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of boils is in this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and that you convert the hair and the skin around it as I have said, and then make two incisions by art, and two fine threads as long as the hair and as large as a hazelnut is;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and hold as two cuts of two parts or you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	Then assemble the one and the other together smoothly over that which rests on the marrow of the oil, and strain the two thumbs of the two parts forming.
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and leave them together for a while, and the skin which is strained will be toughened, wrinkled, and swollen, until it becomes loose by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it is late, if the fire has a force, then cure it until it is sound

li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	the work is like taking a subtle needle and there is one thread of silk subtle.
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	Then assemble the bones and do not let one rest upon the other loosely, and let the length of the threads be as long as a palm of the hand.

et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve. de la porriture de l’oil	from the corruption of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this ailment which is called "aleacrati" or the swelling comes to the surface, if there are two methods:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this ailment which is called "aleacrati" or the swelling comes to the surface, if there are two methods: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And there may be from a wound, or a cut or burn, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the way of working in this is that you make that suture, dry the flesh of it, put in some linen threads, and keep it until it is healed.
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and do not use anything but dry and restrictive things in the treatment of it.

et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	These things that we have said do not apply to other ailments except for this one, for it does not return like before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	From the fire that comes in oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is called "axacrati" in truth is natural and sudden.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The causes are wounds, fissures, cautery and similar things
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	And the way of the work in this matter is if you take an awl, in which there is a double thread, and the needle through the skin, and it makes split the skin so that the thread comes out two fingers from the skin
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Then is the head of the shoulder above all awry, and the scapula has a wide space.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	If the limb returns to its natural position as it should, that is good.
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	If not, take hold of the limb and put it back into the socket, and twist the limb, and make two incisions or pierce through the flesh of the limb;
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	Make two incisions at two angles of the incision you made, and make an angle so that when they are reunited, the limb is as straight as a letter that has not been bent.</start_of_turn>
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	Then hold the limb firmly, according to the quantity of its bones and cartilages that are still inside, so that the dislocation is reset, and then join the two broken parts with a thread of linen.</start_of_turn>
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the treatment for what we have said of the mild medicines and bandages, as long as they are sound.

dou soudement de la papiere	And if the ailment comes from a fracture or sprain or burn, if you must make an incision, make it full through the hair of papers; then stretch between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and it must be done according to the form of the ailment, for it is diverse in form, and the wise masters perceive with great insight all sorts of things that must be done to return the limb to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is to be done and the instruments in multiple positions.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this inflammation occurs at home in a limb as the master of surgery has sutured with white oil, and cannot move or perform his natural works, if it is necessary, then you must bite the point of a scraper at the root of the limb and hold it high.
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and extend as much as possible, as long as you can bear the pain that is in the sensitive area, which must not be too great and not too little, so that the patient does not suffer more from the sensitive area than from the oil;

de l’ungle de l’oil	De l’ungle de l’oil.
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	The nails of the fingers are two ways:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	The first way is that it is nervous and looks like iron of a certain hardness, and another which is not nervous, but looks like white moisture frozen, which when touched with iron and warmed up again shows bites; if it does not die off immediately
