et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And they grow as I have told you in the division, and if you see them covered, if you overpour the oil on the patient, take the spatula lighter rather than acute following this form.
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And pull the hair out gently, and if you see that it comes out easily and the root is pressed, if you distill from your mouth into the oil of colocynth make of litharge and red colocynth and it boils, and stamp the oil until it reaches the other ear;
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Then repeat the work as I have said above, until it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing hinders you, if like an abscess you have post-surgery, then milk should be withheld and first cure the abscess thoroughly until it has healed, and then resume the work as before, until it has healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if at night in the oil there appears to be fat, suspend it to the bacon, and cut a part of it, rather than all at once, because of tears do not come;
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	Then distill in the red colander which is made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	from the hair that grows on the navel
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	There is never any red rose in the urine of healthy men; cover the navel and bind above the papers and turn towards the fire, and it appears like a rose of bulrush.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	If the patient puts his head in his right mind, then the urine will smell of vinegar; and all that red stuff has a suitable stench for this, and the sensation is strong
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	Then crush the first red thing, and go on crushing until the end, and keep that you do not spill the oil at the work;
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	Or the incision of the spleen which we mentioned in the incision of the vein and has small forces so that one can break the bone easily, as this chapter shows in practice.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	And when the incision is complete and the bone is exposed, if you use oil of rue or you distill collyrium rouge and similar corrosive medicines, put on cotton wool soaked in vinegar, so that it should adhere firmly to the wound.
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	If it does not stop bleeding and the wound is wide open, and you doubt that the wound has healed, if you leave the oil and treat the wound with soothing things that heal the wound
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	then return to your work when it is healed, and when the wound is complete, let the bones rest in the oil in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	However, it is necessary to alleviate the cure of each weak oil from its natural way.
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and from the violent way, in the work of fire;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	And do not strain your hand in any of these works until you see that the limb is suffering from the work.
des voines des eulz	From the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	The veins are red ones that are covered in oil, and they tolerate the gaze of the eye and disclose the oil throughout the days.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	And so it is with the first that you see that the limb is relaxed, in which case it is forced, and there is no other disease fierce than relaxation;
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	therefore take hold of it with part of your body:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient to place his head in your hand, then suspend the veins altogether according to his wisdom, and let them be loosely bound twice in this fashion:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	and be doubled superficially by degrees in a circle according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then gently pull the veins out, and keep the blood from flowing for a while afterwards until you see the fierce veins removed from the root
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and keep that you do not bleed at the points of the spatulas, and do this work at midday in front of the sun, and be vigilant in your work if you do not want to weaken only the veins
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	And when you have done this, if distilled in green and red oil of ravens, it will break up that which remains doubtful.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you do not wish to collect all of it in that hour, make a plaster on the oil of soothing things that calm the pain of the eyes, and leave it until the pain is calmed and is secured after the swelling has gone down; then repeat in this manner until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
et c’est li forme des forces:	And that is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	If you cannot firmly grasp all that is in this hour, make a plaster on the oil of soothing things to calm the eye pain, and leave it until the pain is soothed and is secure from after-pain; then start again in the same manner as before until you are healed; and this is the form of strength.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	Moisture which is called "arissati" is a fistula.</start_of_turn>
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	When you treat it with fire cautery and with strong water medicine as I have said before, and it does not heal, if it is deeply rooted in that which you have made on the swelling, then you must measure it there, and drain all the moisture from it, until the bone is exposed.</start_of_turn
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is discovered, you will see the corruption and blackness, if the wound has all the tools, for this is its form.
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And is called "open wound", and is made with a sharp knife at the head of the bone, and is pointed as if with a file when it is in this form.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And put on the bone's corrupted flesh, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a lot until you feel that the corruption is gone;
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	Do this only once, and then restore the limb of drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the limb is swollen and puffy, and the bone is fractured, and the skin of the limb is swollen, and remains so for forty days, and does not heal and is not sutured, and accidents happen to it, know that it is healed;
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	If not, if there is no other remedy except to restore the fistula to its proper place without delay according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If not, if there is no other remedy except to restore the fistula to its proper place without delay according to this form: uncover the bone a the second time with iron, and with strong medicines. When it has been uncovered, take hold of the fistula according to this form, and let the iron clamp be at a 90-degree angle, and the fistula must be narrowed until it is flush with the surface as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	Then place it upon the bone without moisture, and wipe your hand with oil, and draw the clamp completely until it breaks the bone and the patient feels pain in that place where it comes into contact with the fistula if it is held in its place
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and leave the dry medicines in place, as I have taught you, and when the wound heals and becomes firm, if there is still matter in the fistula.
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	If it is easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	Then place your thumb on the bone below the armpit, and wipe your hand with oil. Indeed, once you have grasped the whole forearm, pull it until it pierces the bone and the patient will feel it through what comes into being at that moment if he holds his hand on his elbow. Then restore the dry medicine, as I have taught you, and when the wound has healed and hardened, if there is anything that troubles the elbow; if it is less serious for the patient.
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eyes are wide open and do not suffer from any pain or discomfort, if it is easier for the patient, bind his eyes tightly.</start_of_turn>
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	Then do the same, then put on a bandage or dressing in a clockwise direction, then put some oil on it and apply acaice, aloe, incense, and ochre, and then strain the oil, and cover it with bandages and cloths.</start_of_turn
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	And keep the cloths in place if you take cloths thick enough, and double the layers in threes, and then put one on top of the other according to the amount of hair there is between them.</start_of_turn
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	Then strain with the hands of a strong bandage, and repeat the dressing in a clockwise direction.</start_of_turn
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	Then break the blisters and leave the oil strained for a while both day and night, and if it sticks, as you must know, pull it out whole.
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	Then break the wound afterwards the oil and the nut, and if you see the oil regain its place, that is good

si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	if it recurs, leave the dressing and the nut and the wound and the blisters until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Dou derrompement de toile uvee.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When dislocation comes in the armpit, then open it, and bring forth paper as with one grain of resin, and it is expected to see;
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	then if you see it covered, the work is like that of biting a needle at the root of the limb until it is below, then put in another needle or there is double thread at the elbow

et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	And leave it until the blood has clotted with the iris, then cure the oil with comforting things until the wound is healed
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And never is the wound held back by the surrounding tissue of a circle of fat until it is healed

puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then pull out the [foreign object] until it is whole.
de la bowe de l’oil	De la bowe de l’oil.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This ailment which is called "alcunnati" is not fierce except for the swelling which is assembled in oil, resembling descending water, and this is not plain water.
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the manner of appearance of the work is that if you make the patient sit on a chair that appears low and straight, then grasp the head between your hands from two parts, and move it until you see the swelling coming down to your eyes
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then either tie it up, and do not let it descend and be broken, see the light, and see the patient do things as he used to before;
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not descend spontaneously, like water, and if the swelling descends only partially, as we have said
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the sponge and place it on the cornea of the eye I by the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, as long as the eyebrow is visible.
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when it comes out, if you distill in hot oil mixed with honey, or vinegar or fennel boiled with honey, then let it be cured of another remedy until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
des aigues de l’oil	from the bowl of the oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have seen in the wounds the resemblance of worms in their division, and what it is necessary to pierce.</start_of_turn
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	if in work in accordance with health.</start_of_turn
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, and take light from the sun, and bind the oil clean and tighten the mouth firmly.</start_of_turn
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	Then put the thumb of the oil on your left hand if the eyes are left, or on your right hand if the eyes are right.
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	Then take in your right hand if the eyes are left, the instrument which is called the “almagda,” or in your left hand if the eyes are right.
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Then put the tip of the instrument below the crown by the thickness of a hair in that which there is a greater amount of oil, then hold the instrument called the “almagda” firmly, and withdraw your hand until it touches the oil, and feel that the “almagda” has reached the empty space
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	and that the measure of the “almagda” should be at the level of the measure of the space from the armpit to the end of the shoulder blade
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	And this is the navel of oil.
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	If you see the bone in that membrane by the clarity of the rough cloth, and then put the instrument almost until the liquid is gone, and press down slightly afterwards.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the pain increases now, if you see the patient before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After rest, a little, when the liquid returns the second time, put the force with the instrument, and when it is held firm and does not rise, if it is strained too much around your hand and your hand, then strain the bandage lightly around your hand and your hand
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	And then put back in the liquid a little bit of gum, and leave away that oil from there
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by force oil-soaked tampons or soaked cloth in rose oil and plenty of eggs, and tie with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Yes, and those who are of our household, put on common broth with plenty of eggs.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the oil by its hardness, because there are parts of bones that have too many hairs, it is recommended that you take the instrument which is called the “alberit,” which is like this in shape:

et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	And at the end of the work, appears to the patient I the sleeper, lying on his back in the dark;
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	Or be commanded to abstain from all movement, and take gentle food, and do not move his head forward or backward, or to the side, and keep him still according to his condition until three days have passed.
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	Then loosen him in this house alone, and uncover his face, and let him see nothing, and then bring him back to his place until seven days have passed.
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And do not do anything else in the hour of treatment or after the incision now, but only that you nourish him, for because of this the pain has increased greatly
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	since the oil must be loosened before the seventh day, and given to this which alleviates the abscess
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When he is calmed, if you remove the vein and put a little I orilliet on his face to cover any wound, and be sure to keep it in that dark place.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	Then go out of the house and out, and in his case he will recover naturally;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and let the wounds be such that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us from Yrach who told us that in the peace of peace he did often see all the maggots fall down when the vinegar was poured, but he never saw that happen anywhere else, neither did he read of it in the books of the ancients;
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and it is a new thing that has happened by chance

et soient d’arain proprement:	And let them be again properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their heads are of this same subtlety, and their backs in two angles like an eagle.</start_of_turn>
de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint downwards to the hand.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	And let them be again properly: For often at birth or at death various hairs seem like scorpions in their mouths;
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if there are such things or if there is hair entangled in yellow pus, and if there is hair of bone colour.

adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	Then you must take hold of the limb with a thumb and four fingers, and keep your hands steady, and there should be no space between each finger or less.
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and put the patient’s hand over the head of the shoulder at the base of the thumb, and keep smelling until it comes out of the socket
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and do this many times, and it is a light thing for one who sees it done;
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold the limb coming from the socket with one hand, and the limb coming from the mouth with the other hand, and pull one after the other as we have said before.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you are sure that the bone is not broken, then pull the limb out, wipe the blood, and moisten the thumb with Egyptian balsam, and reset the limb in its place as before
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char.
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	Do so for three days or more, until the swelling has eaten away all that is decayed of flesh; and then put on or take away a compress of lead for some days until it is healed, and if there is need of drying medicines, use them.</start_of_turn>
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	This is the form of the instrument for drawing out the head, from which we distill the oils and medicines or not.</start_of_turn>
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	Or of silver, like an overblown lamp, if like a cord, and it is carried along.</start_of_turn
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	And if you see it, if you make a closed cord, and the instrument is smooth for purging the head.</start_of_turn
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And he has one hand clasped at the shoulder to hold it when we pour oil or no liquid.
de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint downwards to the hand.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times there arises at the shoulder no disease which is called "telul," and grows and becomes large to such an extent that it is seen;
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and therefore you must first pull down the bone somewhat, and then put the cautery or burning medicine out;
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if it is delayed in covering it when it is large, if it has turned white, of foul colour, of poor sense
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	if you do not touch it with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, for when you touch it once, there comes great harm to the patient
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	And if the abscess bursts with a soft touch, not of fierce color, you see that you can cover it up completely; if the patient vomits and recoils in fear, cure the limb of dry and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the arm is cut and bound.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Do as much as you know until you sense that the hair has not been corrupted; then draw the thread, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian fashion, and reattach it as before; do this for three days or more, until the hair has consumed all that remains of the char; and then put on or remove a cauterizing bougie for a few days as long as it remains sound, and if there is a need for sedative medicines, if necessary; and this is the form of the instrument for extracting the head, from which we distill the oils and medicines or not.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is therefore necessary that this does not happen at all, if you see that the wound is fresh with all its blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then immediately join the two limbs to a splint, and then treat it until it is healed;
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the limbs are already dislocated from one side and the other, if you must support all the parts of their limb until they bleed, then reassemble the two limbs to a splint, and strain them, and sprinkle upon them dragon’s blood powder and incense
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put upon the wound a piece of dressing of great or other soft dressing that sticks, and leave it until it bleeds by itself, and then cure it of swelling until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	If the dressing is held in place, and the solution is assembled:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or by needles, as we have said in the wound of the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or by thread, as I have told you
des apostemes des levres	of the separation of the layers of the skin.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	At home, there are often grains of sand in the open wound, like grains of wheat, minor and greater
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	therefore it is necessary to tear the wound open, and open up each knot, and take hold of it with tweezers and pull it out whole;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	Then apply the broth after the incision of the carbuncle boils, until the wound is dry.
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let the broth drain easily, and cure the wound of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	From the roots of the gums.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times blood appears on the gums like little garlic cloves, which they formerly called "albulus".
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	If you hold it firmly and grasp its root, and leave the blood or the blood vessel alone;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	Then put out the boiling carbuncle, or other restraining and drying powders
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if it comes back after the incision, and happens many times, if the root grasps it a second time, and cauterize it.
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	If it does not return naturally after the cautery.
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	And these are the forms of the instruments for covering
des sordens	Des sordens.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Never are they assembled at the head of the dens, in the mouth between the gums, shields that are burdensome and harsh;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	Never are the teeth black and yellow and toward, until the corruption comes to the gum, and are the teeth biting;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	If you command that the patient sit between your hands, and his head rests in your stomach, and open the teeth or the shields wide, until nothing remains.
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	And so make blackness and greenness, and yellowness and other spots, until they are gone
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	And if its bone is fractured at the outset, that is well.
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	If not, if it starts to swell up again the second time and the third, as long as you still have everything;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and the teeth that are driven out must have various forms of instruments to remove them, according to what the work shows, for the roots of the teeth which we must extract are of different forms than those which are between the teeth
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these forms and others appear before you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	You must take care that you do not make the tooth worse with your treatment, for this must not be done
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	because it is a very sticky substance, so we have no excuse for leaving it
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the patient is unable to bear pain, if you are certain that he can endure it.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the patient complains of pain, whether it is acute or chronic, and makes the limb tremble.
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and indeed the pain does not depart from him until the evil is banished, because we have already wished to make them well;
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	when you are very certain of the pain that is groaning, if you wish, you must press the limb down firmly in order to stop the swelling from all parts
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then move the limb forward or backward slightly at the first moment and then fix it firmly;
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and if the patient’s limb hangs between the buttocks, hold it firmly if it does not move
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After that, if the tooth sticks directly forward, and if it does not jump up, take no one of these instruments and hold it loosely in the cheek; and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	if the disease is perceived and mixed, if you cover it with cloths, the pus or the hole is left open.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	If the strained thing is gently held, it will not break when strained.
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	You must keep your mouth absolutely quiet over the joint to prevent loosening the teeth
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Take care that you do not break it, and leave some of it, and return to the patient with the greater pain of the first time
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	Beware that you do not do anything like the ignorant who, by their haste and boldness, break the limb every time and bring no benefit except what we have told you
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	But it often happens by the loosening of that great disease from its roots or from the breaking of the limb, as we have often seen
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	When the flesh is raw, wash the limb with wine or vinegar and oil.
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	If blood comes, which often happens, use a little vitriol to stop it
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	If this does not suffice, if the burn cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	If this is not enough, if the burn cauterize. The forms of the instruments, indeed silent at first, are either long and pointed or broad-handed, that they do not double while you draw out the tooth.
et ce sont les formes:	These are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of large members if they do not bend when drawing, and be made of iron indeed well, and be toothless so that they may be held by hand
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth.
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root is grasped while drawing out, if you must put out the wet cotton swab in the burn I or II, as long as the wound is raw, because there remain the fangs which are called “algefri,” for the head of the shoulder seems like the beak of a sparrow
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	These are made in the same way as with a file and this is the form
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	If the roots do not suffice to support all these tensions, then it is recommended that you uncover the bark entirely around the root, and place the instrument called «althali», which is to say a palainche, since this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps by this, that is good;
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	If not, if you aid with all your tools, and if the forms come afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument which has teeth, since this is its form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments that are before in the ratio of the teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let your tools be strong that they cannot break, and nails like the teeth of beasts of prey.
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	And so with other tools, which are not counted here;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and he himself will find the right instrument according to his work and his ailment, for there are various diseases where the old ones did not teach any instrument because of the diversity of things; and if he breaks anything by chance with his hand or with anything else, or if he carries it, if he seeks these instruments, as I have said, and assists with gestures, so that this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be great and firm to hold the bone, that they do not escape, but can hold and restrain.
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	Then restore the limb of medicine suitable for this one, and if there is inflammation in the bone, and it is small, if the disease has all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the tooth appears does not match the natural curve, and the shape is harmful, and even in women of gentle birth, if you know that it will not come out on its own, and is not in its rightful place, and cannot be soothed or comforted
adonques lou raie;	Therefore the rasp;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	And if it is hollow with the tooth, take this instrument which has a small beak like I, and be like iron without a cut at the top
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And when the tooth persists in the gums and hands are clasped for a long time due to the duration of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, if it appears, it can be limed, if you use a file of the same shape as the tooth itself
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	And it is thus like when we make needles.
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	And thus like when we hold the teeth firmly in place with thumbs and index fingers, if they do not move until they bleed
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	Then the limb at the end has no sensation, and if the bone is too bent and it breaks the tongue, if you must restrain the biting until it is even, so that it does not break the tongue or impair speech
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth is loose.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the front teeth are loose, by percussion or biting, and the patient cannot press on what hurts him except when he bleeds, and you cure them with restrictive medicines, this is useless;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	if you must restrain them with gold wire, for the silver wire becomes green and corrupts, but the blood does not move anymore.
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	And let the son of the middle be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth.
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	And if you see the teeth leaning towards each other, if you take hold of the thread and double it between the two front teeth, then put the nails between the middle teeth, as many as there are, until you see clearly up to the sound tooth on the other side.
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	Then continue the covering up to the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and cautiously, so that it does not move again
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	And let the suture be at the root of the tooth if it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then grasp the nails of the thread with tweezers, assemble them, and put them between the sound tooth and the suture so that it does not catch the tongue;
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	Then leave it [the dislocation] somewhat tight as much as it can stay put; and if it slips or the thread breaks, if the strain of another thread.
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	if it should remain and hold it securely, and this is the shape of two teeth and the arrangement of two thumbs, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	When the tooth is loosened, if we reset it in its place, fresh and new, as we have said.
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and nothing else should intervene between them except for wisdom and solace, and never make it the shape of a decayed tooth, and put it back in its place or where the defect is, and strain it as we have said, and it will remain secure and serve its purpose for a long time
de coper lou liien de la lengue	De coper, lou liien de la lengue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Never is this life which comes from the tongue or nature that we are not born into.
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by an accidental wound beneath the skin;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the work is such that you must bite the mouth of the patient, and put your head in his body, and he will hold his tongue
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then you must bite the large nerve, so that the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is delay or not, it is a remedy for wounds, if you can bring back the joint and bite the large one again
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and keep that the fracture is not too deep, because of the artery which comes from below;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done this, if you lift the limb of rose and easily, or of cold water, then put the tongue back in a little attempt of silk;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	The sick man complains that at night his limbs do not cease tormenting him, that they cannot be comforted.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And when blood comes out, if it is from a vein that has been broken, it brings with it a piece of glass;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	If it does not stop, if you cauterize with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then you must cure it in another way while it is still healthy
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see black or red or hard pus, if the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is an abscess
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is declining with moisture, if there is moisture, if it breaks, and you wipe it off with a subtle sponge, and you deliver from both sides;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	And if it does not go without pain to your work, put on a broken glass shard as long as it is stained, and then return to your work until you have finished all your business.
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then lift up your limb easily and cautiously, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed
des apostemes de la gorge	Des apostemes de la gorge.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Never comes from the throat a boil that is called "godath", and the name has two almonds; and when you treat them, as we said in the division, and they are not healed, take care:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	if it is a hard abscess of little size and color of blood, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	and if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, even for the evacuation of blood;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	But leave it as long as it is strong, and when it is ready, you must take it out, or else it will break by itself.
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is of pale color and the root is flexible, if the instrument has been applied to cover it, but first look to see if the abscess is firm and calm.</start_of_turn>
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his arms at his sides, and cover his mouth and grasp his beard between his hands, and press the tongue downwards towards the instrument, for this is the shape.</start_of_turn
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	And it may be of silver or gold, as with a knife.</start_of_turn
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	Can you press the tongue towards the instrument, and you see the abscess, if you take the sponge and put it into the opening, and draw it out more than you wish.</start_of_turn
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	And take no heed of the threads with it, then hold the cup to the instrument, for this is its form, that seems like a force.
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And behold that the head of the cup is bent, and one place is opposite the other, and they are very acute, and is made of iron or tin:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument, if you can hold the wound tight, for this is the fashion:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And be split from one side and from the other side name.
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And when you have grasped one of the almonds, if you grasp the other according to this manner, and afterwards make an incision, gargle the patient with hot water, hot and easy, and remove the blood that comes out, if you gargle the patient with hot water, or if there are pomegranate seeds or myrtle berries, and similar things, until the wound is cleansed;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then the treatment must be such that it be healthy;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	Then the treatment must be such that it be healthy, and never again are there other abscesses in the throat except the two almonds, if the teeth are thus strong as the two almonds always.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was not in the throat, namely one abscess of little size
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and had the throat well closed, so that the woman could neither vomit through the passage that was blocked, nor could she eat or drink, and died because she fainted from pain in one or both of them
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had forced out two stones through the two holes of the neck
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I have often seen this, and I have bound one with an incision, then the patient went away, and he brought back great portions of vomit;
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	Then he should spit out the other part into the other part where it does not want to stay, and he should cover the mouth and press the tongue;
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	Then he should put the ointment on these abscesses, and close one part, and only a little blood should come out from there.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	And so he should loosen the windpipe from the throat of the woman, and now start to drink water and then wine, and do not stop biting this abscess for a long time
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscesses were coming back, and filled the belly as I had avoided vomiting, until they brought out large amounts of matter.
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	Therefore I grasped it and cauterized it inside the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	Then it makes sense crosswise;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	Then it departs from these parts, and only God knows what will be done to it after me.
de l’uve	De l’uve.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the wound descends into the limb, and it flees and becomes long, if it is called "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is thick and round, it is called "wound".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit me, and you see that the wounds are appeased, and it is subtle, so you must cover it
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and that which is round and assembled and is not long
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is bloody or dark brown in color or black, so you must avoid the incision of the vein.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great peril for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is fitting therefore, when you see it, as I have said, with its splendor and length, that you make the patient sit in the sunlight, and press the tongue to the instrument mentioned above.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Then insert the ointment in the eye, and draw out the dirt, and close with two instruments that I mentioned when incising the two almonds
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is fitting that you do not cover more than the surplus that is beyond the natural limit;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	because if you cover more, if he cries out with voice and with his throat;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and afterwards, use what was said concerning the incision of the two almonds, and heal as long as it is healthy
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of covering, you must know that you must use an engine in the cautery in the direction of the fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery if it is acute is harsh and severe
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is that the patient places his head in his mouth, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we have said or the chapter of cautery, and grasps with a sharp instrument, if it is neither too thick nor too thin.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and grasps with the cheek of this instrument, for this is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	Or he has a beard or something puts the medicine, as with the nails of a claw, and puts the instrument over the medicine;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient should remain standing beside his chest, so that saliva and mucus come from his mouth over the medicine, if it does not go down to the throat, and he bleats.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then hold your hand over the medicine and press it on the wound, for the amount of half an hour, until you see it scab over and the bites of the medicine are appeased
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	If you see it, take hold and encircle with no instrument, and moisten the cloth with medicine, and hold the instrument to its full extent within the wound until the cloth sticks to the limb.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	Do it often, until the cautery is complete, then leave it dry, and cut after three days or five.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you must repeat the cautery with medicine, if you repeat it, and after the cautery wipe around the limb with a cloth, tightly packing cotton around it, and bind up what is around the medicine
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Be bathed in cold water, and be cured of hiccups as long as you are well
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is better than an incision, than the cautery.
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	If it is cured by fumigation according to this method, take calamus, isop, origanum, rue, chamomile, chamomile, and ivy, and mix them all together in a pot, and put them in boiling.
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	And the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and in the pot put the instrument that is to be cauterized according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And it may be of silver or lead, and the one of the instruments should be pricked in the patient’s mouth until the vapor rises to the eye through the opening, until the eye is numb.
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	Repeat this several times until the eye is dry, and keep that you do not do this at the beginning of the burning of the abscess, for many things happen
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And do not force this [cautery] fire except at the decline of the abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, take a needle and put in the head of the patient a little egg, so that the patient does not suffer too much heat;
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	because the egg does not make the vapor irritate the mouth, and that is a good cure in general.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times has it happened at the gorge bone or thorn of fish, or nothing;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	So you must therefore treat what you see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and what is not seen and is returned to the throat, you must make the patient vomit so that the meat is cooked in the stomach
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	By chance, if this thing is revealed by vomiting.
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient swallows a sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a dry piece of bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and I tie the sponge with a thread, and then I transfix it
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes back, if it is vomited, I will pull it out again with force
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come out by itself, I will take an instrument to grasp it in this fashion:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	either the instrument is curved at the head so that it can enter the throat more easily, and the head is raised up
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, that it is alive, do not break the bone inside
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	And the movement is worth that the patient keeps the instrument, because either the movement is wanting or the thing is out of place.
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	if the limb goes back, or if it is forced too much with all the instrument equally, as much as it is forced.</start_of_turn>
de la sansue de la gorge	And let the tongue rest curved at the root if it can more easily enter the throat, and lift the head up; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, that all do not live, do not push the bone inwards; and must that the patient hold the instrument, because it is either moved or the matter is disturbed; if the epiglottis is swallowed, or he forces it out with all the instrument equally, as much as he is able.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	There is never medicine without bloodletting, as I have said in the division, by the treatment of medicines.</start_of_turn>
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when this does not help, then look at the patient’s face in the sunlight, and then press the tongue to the instrument that I have told you.</start_of_turn
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the limb without support, if it has a slight twist or subtle tension that persists.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	If this is not the case, take a needle and pierce the patient’s throat, then insert or pull out the needle with the cautery, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	If the patient suffers from acute pain throughout.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take full notice of cold water, and cover the mouth, and let the vomit go in the direction of swallowing, and move your hand often.</start_of_turn
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	And if the joint is pressed with the hand, if it feels pain, it must be released.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not yield as we have said, if the patient is tormented by excessive pain, with the instrument which I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	do it often, for it will be of service to the point.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the manner of fumigation is that you take one pot or there are charcoal pieces, and that the part to be treated is covered with a cloth about a mile wide, and that is pierced through at the point of the instrument
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	then I pour the fumigation, and the patient places the root of the tongue in his mouth, closes his mouth, so that the smoke does not go out but comes out only through the eye
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	And now the wound is weeping, and if it does not stop, repeat the fumigation many times.
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	And the patient is suffering from thirst, eating foul and dirty things, and does not drink water
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Therefore, it is necessary to force her to vomit by this treatment
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the form of the instrument with which we treat the wound, if it is seen, is like tongs to grasp the tongue so that it can enter the throat
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	It has the shape of a cork-cutter, and has the bitterness of lime, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go
et vez ci la forme:	And thus is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	it is possible to move forward with the following instructions:
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	The wounds caused by the opening of an abscess are like those remembered from one place and another in this book, and they vary in perforation and size; for in two ways it is like the one which has moisture in it.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method if the limb is hanging loose or fixed to the bone.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the swelling of the head is different from that of the bone, and the swelling of the limb is different from that which comes at the joints, and the flesh itself judges in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if the abscesses are not to be perceived, as long as the belly is dead according to its fulfillment;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	as those which must be perceived when they are solid, and do not die according to their fulfillment, like an abscess which is between joints
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	for when the swelling comes from the joints, and we leave it as long as it is stiff, by chance if the bone and the nerve of the joint are corrupted, because of this there is contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	or if the abscess is between the main member and the head of the member, and you delay the perforation until it is measured, it will go to the main member;
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	Or if it is from the root that the wound has proceeded, if one pricks it again, that it should not be killed.
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	Or it must only be pierced at the root end where digestion is running its course, except for the wound that is from the root, which must not be opened, but must be left along, and there will be fistula.
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	It cannot be cured in a great time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it must be known that you should wait for the pain to subside and the swelling to go down, and the fading of the heat, and the absence of pain and redness, and the debate and the tingling of the root of the abscess, and the other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	And it must be known that you should make the perforation or break more dependent on the abscess, and the place where it breaks loose.</start_of_turn>
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And let the perforation be through the long of the bone, and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all these things let the hairs be equal or there shall be no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to the location of that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when the wound is open in flesh, if you do not perceive that it is confirmed in digestion accompanying it, as we have said
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce before this, if it yields the bone marrow of it, and is full of thick mucus;
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and by chance toughen the flesh and pierce it through with it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is no wound perceived according to the large wound mark, according to what the limb has suffered.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	Therefore it is necessary to bring in little abscesses, little perforations;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and many cuts according to the greatness of the abscess.
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if there are such abscesses or it is necessary to close it quickly, and cover it over.
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	When it is necessary to stretch as I do a drape, and is softened, then it is possible to do as with bubbles.
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if there are such as are split into three angles, and if there are such as we handle like the fennel of Myrtle, like apostemes of grapes;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if there are such as we make a round size, and other sizes and similar to cope them
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who have no head, if like a superficial wound, you must simply pierce through;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and when the wound is large, and it has collected great blood, you must pierce through, but do not extract all the blood in that hour, but only a part
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	Then I press the abscess right up to the other ear, and leave it without doing anything further.
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	Do this many times with great force, until the swelling is completely gone.</start_of_turn>
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Likewise, if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman in childbirth, or a young child, or an old hunchback.</start_of_turn
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore avoid this chapter with great care, and when you have perceived the abscess, if the wound is small, look to see if the wound at the abscess is small.</start_of_turn
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	And if it is a large wound, if you can, try to insert linen or old cotton.</start_of_turn
