et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	And if it is a large abscess, and there is much pus, you must know that you must bite in the cheekbone two fingers so that one overlaps the other.</start_of_turn
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	And if you have grasped in the abscess a part of raw leather, and you have bound it around, then you must know that you must fill it with much cotton or lint of flaxseed towards moisture, and keep it until three-fourths.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the bone, and keep it oiled until it is healed
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood evacuates from your work, if you fear cold and ease, and moistness I drape, and take out the decorative limb many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if blood continues to discharge, if you mix with government and care, and the powders that I have mentioned before, and if it is cold or wet, or if the wound or the abscess is moist and nervous, then you must put on a cover and moisten with wine and oil
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if it is in this state, and the limb is swollen, if you must put on moist dressings with water and oil, or with wine and oil.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then take away the abscess, drain it, and treat it if necessary until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	This is the translation of the last line of the given text.
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	Or as you have said previously, thus must it be in the treatment of abscesses, and thus must it be in this chapter.
des soros	And this knowledge is sufficient for the treatment of abscesses: as you have said previously concerning the precautions before treating abscesses, and thus is this chapter.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or if small abscesses come out, and they are like those that are in towels, thus as the juice of a gooseberry, and there is resemblance in them.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are greasy ones and such as when there is moisture like pus;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	And if there are such ones that are tough and stony at the root, and there is no doubt that the artery is not opposed to it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And as for the work of the surgeon, if you suspect that everything that is called "entromissor" has come out, which thing contains what, etc.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, it remains for a long time
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	When the moisture is drained, if you leave the peel that contains that moisture, it will return as before when you leave it alone
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Then plunge the cotton into the Egyptian poultice if it is present.
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	If not, in water and oil, and use the bandage, and leave it until the other day
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and that which is remaining will depart on its own
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And when you renew the cotton, as before, the second day, and the third, until you are certain that it does not remain in place
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound of the poultice when it is appropriate, until it is healed
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess persists without fat, if the physician follows this form, for a long time
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and if it discharges your medicines, and the pus from all parts, and puts all your care to drain for the swelling or where it is located
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the artery opposes you, if you do what I have said afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same with an abscess that is pierced, and cut and cure as I have told you
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the size of the pierced abscess and the moisture, if it is less severe, because they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if there is no swelling in the abscess or the head or there is no moisture, and these are old abscesses that I cauterise or heads from old women;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and find the abscess just like a stone, rough and white, and cannot burst
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if there is no blood vessel nearby, we must make a wound as if with a stone.</start_of_turn>
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses coming from the head or the shoulders, because these arise from the joints of the limbs and the roots of the ears, they open all the more on the most dependent limb because of moisture.
et les cure si com il covient.	And so they must be cured as they ought.
des scrophules	And the size on the pierced wound and the moisture, if it is less severe, because they are of little blood. And if there are some of these wounds or chieftains or it has no moisture, and of those wounds which I cauterize or chieftain from an old woman; and find the wound just like a hard stone, rough and white, and cannot break it; and if no blood comes out, it is just as well to make a wound like a stone. In other wounds that come from chieftains and have roots of ears, it overturns if it is kept too long, for it makes the wound worse. And it cures as it should.
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often these abscesses occur at the collarbone, and the armpits, and in the groin, and never elsewhere or on the bones, and are bloody, and are joined together.</start_of_turn
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And indeed, every swelling must be properly treated within its container, as we have said before regarding its base and apex.
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And their signs are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are also cases where the body contains moisture, and if there are maligns that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	In such a case that you see a bone in a good position to the touch, and that looks like flesh, soft partly and not red like blood, neither dark as the marrow of the bone nor pale as the cartilage of the joint, and that is neither superficial nor deep;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	Then you must hold it together with sutures and a soft dressing, and if you must touch it, do so with two fingers as we have said in the previous instances concerning the apex of the swelling
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	And thus they do go back and forth, and so it is necessary that you do not cover the nerve or the vein, and do not be too hasty with the bandage or the forceps, but that your hands do not escape, and do not voice too much beforehand, that you do not cover anything that you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cover the vein or the artery, and this does not allow you to work, if you put in the wound a piece of vitriol or some powders that remain inside, and constrain the wound;
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	leave it until the abscess is calmed and the wound is softened, and begin to move.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	When the thing is not stained, if you return to your work until you have completed it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	Then if at your command there are to be no small vesicles remaining, if the head and the tail are coped and bound.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is in the root of the vesicle a great swelling, if you do not dare but to cope that vesicle at its root, but join it with a strong double thread, and leave it hanging loose;
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then apply the dressing of white cotton pressed in Egyptian fashion, and then suture.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	If you pull out all the pus, if you are certain that you have joined the two layers of the wound, and you sew them now, there will be no remaining pus because of the size of the abscess.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you are certain that you have grasped the root of the [disease], and that you have pulled out the foreign body, and you sew it as we have said
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	The vesicles which cause excess discharge, pierce them or they will open and die;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and pierce as before said, depending on the situation, and mix with ointment and similar things, so that it removes what remains of corruption;
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the wound is well closed, if the dressing of ointment covering the wound is sufficient, while it is healthy
de squinance	When the swelling is reduced, and if you return to your work until you have completed it, then if there are any remaining small abscesses, press them and squeeze them out.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancient ones spoke and wrote of the size of the gorge;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I have never seen anyone in our land who has performed it, and it is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	As for those who have a squint, it is necessary that the slit of the throat called the epiglottis be cut away
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and this does not help, for all the veins and the blood of the patient are at those which have been cauterized in the mouth, or the throat or in the two armpits.</start_of_turn>
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the blood vessels, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent loss of blood from strangulation.</start_of_turn
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is therefore necessary, when our tongues cut the epiglottis, to cut three circles or four, a small slit through two circles or according to the quantity of the slit of the epiglottis, not through the cartilage.</start_of_turn>
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And if the limb is coved with the epiglottis, there is no hair, and the vessel is long and thin.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is fearful, if you must cover the skin of the throat to the chin, then cut as much as you will until you reach the nail;
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	Avoid the blood vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then close the wound as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is shown by the section of the windpipe that the spasm arises from the broken bone, and by the defect of speech;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	When the hour has passed without coving, doubt the strangulation, join the two layers of the wound of the limb, and close it all around the cartilage
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then administer medicines that cause the growth of hair, as long as they are sound.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	The wound is not made whole until the throat is completely closed, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the default is abandoned.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	So you must place your hand on the epiglottis for the patient does not vomit, and he breathes through the wound; and thus is kept from death.</start_of_turn>
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And so they command the old man to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it is passed in three days or four. And then they command to suture the wound and cure it, when it is cured.</start_of_turn
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I saw.</start_of_turn>
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a woman who took a knife and plunged it into her throat, and grasped part of the windpipe.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And I went called to cure it, and found it as dead as death.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that had escaped from it, and saw that there was no vessel or conduit other than the throat that had been injured by the wound.</start_of_turn
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hastened, and cleansed the wound, and cured it until it was healed
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and did not cause her any more pain, since it returned to its natural state.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Therefore I believe that in the dressing of the epiglottis I did not find any fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the great throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	These abscesses are called "throat hernia," and are great abscesses in the color of jaundice, and are very common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	and there are two kinds of them:
naturez, et accidens;	natural and accidental
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	or the natural one has no cause
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the cause of the accident is twofold: sometimes it is like grease that adheres to us, and sometimes it is like an abscess that comes from an artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is doubt and fear, and it is not possible for me to work without fear of fire, only in that which is small, and I prove and seek all the surrounding parts:
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it as I do not know grease, and cannot enter any vein, if it bites, as we bite the hand, and it is taken away from its covering, if there is no mark;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and encircle well all around, and cure as if it should be sane once more
des nous	And encircle all around, and cure him as it seems right, until he is completely healed.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways in which we are like this; I will tell you of all the resemblances.
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And thus it must be known that I tell of all the difference that exists between a bruise and a dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that dislocation is a swelling and fever that lasts as long as the inflammation persists, and is accompanied by pain;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	therefore rests the fever and the swelling.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With no bruise there is neither fever nor swelling nor pain, and there is pus, which is its own sac, and it is like the color of blood, and it begins like a wound and becomes large
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are like boils, or grease, or moisture, and fluid of the color that I have mentioned before
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the knot, to ask and inquire first about all the instruments which are called “instruments of extraction,” according to the form that comes or the treatise that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the way to inquire about abscesses of the veins is that you take more moisture from the vessel than you find in the abscess, and turn your thumbs and little fingers inward, until you know that the instrument has grasped the hair, and only then do you proceed according to the size of the abscess
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then withdraw the entomissor and take hold of the leap that forces.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	When moisture covers it completely, that is when its color becomes dark; if it is so as I have said of other incisions.</start_of_turn>
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if afterwards the entomissor does not bring moisture, if it is greasy, if it is so, grasp it with tweezers and pinch it slightly from the edge and hold the cloth tightly over the area where you have pierced it until it is well bled;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you do not draw it out whole, if you tear it to pieces, so that nothing remains.</start_of_turn>
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if nothing remains, it comes back to us many times.</start_of_turn
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if it lingers a little while, and you grieve not, if you employ the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, hold the wound steady, and apply soothing things around the circumference; and cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if it is great, if cut the two pounds of the wound, and cure it of that which engulfs flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	And if the vein swells up against you or another if you are hasty and use broken glass, and leave it for two or three days, until the wound is healed, and rest the swelling of blood
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	Then return to covering that which remains delayed from now on.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See here the forms of the entrapped instruments, and there are three ways:
grans et moien et petit;	Great, middle, and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	There are three quarters which are called "albaret," and one which is called "breb," and there are three ways of doing it.
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Great, middle, and small, to encompass the fistulas of fistula.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And they are like needles which we sew up wounds, and they are of saffron, or iron, or silver, and the thread is yellow, and it is more proven with black soot to encompass the cortices of fistula
et sont de III manieres:	There are three ways of doing it
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Great, middle, and small, according to the quantity of the wound
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of the wounds are like clusters of seeds, as you can see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	Great, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	Great, medium, and small; and if there are three corbels of three ways each,
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if there are onicules which have three corbels, and are also of three ways.
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if there are onicules which have two corbels, and onicules of one corbel only, and are of three ways
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all these things are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these bones is often fractured, and there are some which do not split through the middle but only from one side, from which we must protect the nerves, because if we do not, we split the vein or the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and from these intrusions are the bones which are placed in sleeves, so that the patient does not lose them when the abscesses are opened
et sont de III manieres:	And there are three methods:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	And there are three methods: great, small, and medium, as you see.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and do not use them except in the case of bone fractures, such as legs, arms, breasts, and armpits, and similar things.
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and never make another small instrument, like the handles of fists, according to this form, because it stops the blood
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And do not put it on any part which has recently bled, and has veins, and never again according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Never swell the breasts of the sick when they begin to decay, as they seem like female breasts
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and endure pain and escape, and whoever sees them cured, if he covers them according to this form from line .b. up to line .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then scrape off the fat, and apply the medicinal poultice thickly smeared with char, and assemble the two layers of the wound with stitches, and cure until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the mother’s milk flows downwards, and is softened by its greatness as with women, if it comes out through two ribs below, through two similar incisions;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	then the larger line should contain the smaller one according to this form, from this line B up to line G
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape off the skin between the two layers, and bone the fat, and mix in what we have said about stitching and powders, and anything necessary for the cure, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	If he is not well, or the incision is not thoroughly made, because the patient does not wish to rest, or for the discharge of blood, if you must, fill the wound with moist cotton in corrosive order.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And leave it until it has consumed the remnants and fat, then cure it when it is well healed.</start_of_turn>
des apostemes des asselles	And let him leave it [hair] until it has eaten up the remaining fat and grease; then cure it when it is healthy.
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	And let him leave it [hair] until it has eaten up the remaining fat and grease; then cure it when it is healthy
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the hair in the abscess is drained out, if the wound is of great extent, apply a piece of cotton wool, and leave it in place until the other side is reached, then extract all the cotton wool, and cure the wound that has resulted from this until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess appears like boils, if you do as we have said about incisions of boils, and if the wound has penetrated the hair, if necessary perform cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the course of a vein
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is open, and the skin is split which is above, if there are many abscesses there, and also in the vein running away and splitting;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if the surgeon knows that it is for the artery, if the abscesses are long and deeply embedded.</start_of_turn
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	When you sense it, if you sense it is drawing;
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	And when it is a vein, if it is reopened suddenly, it must be cauterized at a distance.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	It is foolish to close this incision too soon, and the same when there are abscesses and boils, or wounds of the head and teeth, and in the mouth of other bones, it is much the same.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	You must withdraw the cautery, and the one at the head must also withdraw, and in that where the artery is inflamed by the above, the skin will become long
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then you must carefully move the limb, and withdraw the artery from the wound, until it is uncovered;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	then you must pull out the awl, and make it pierce until the other side, and tighten the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries which are in the temples
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then point out the limb that is between the two bonds of an introversion until it is loose there; and sever the aponeurosis.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then support the cure that embraces the wound, until it is loosened; and hold the bone tight
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat the swelling that follows this, until it is healed; and let it rest
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	and if the abscess is the size of a vein, if you can, hold your hand over the abscess as much as possible, and then pierce the vein with a needle at the same place, and pass two threads through, so that you can grasp it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	then tie the aponeurosis, as I have said, or bind two parts of it with two threads each;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	And if you doubt that the wound does not bleed, if it returns a third splinter at the site of the first splinter, hold the wound steady for three days.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then close the wound as much as necessary until the bleeding stops, and keep the wound clean and dry until the discharge has ceased; leave only what is bound over the wound
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply a wet dressing of wine and oil, and bind the wound with sutures and compresses until it is healed
des apostemes des ners	Then apply a warm compress soaked in wine and oil, and then bandage the wound until it is healed.
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Then apply a warm compress soaked in wine and oil, and then bandage the wound until it is healed.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	This often happens when the surrounding bones are diseased or broken, or when there are joints involved, and it is the cause of many postmortem changes, and its color is like that of saffron, and is a sign of numerous affections of the body in pain
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is strained, if the patient feels pain, and does not wish to move for fear of pain, but groans with fear;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	he remains silent in all parts, neither goes forward nor backward, neither does he move from side to side, and that which is in the joints cannot be covered with iron.
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	because by chance it may go into contraction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and the skin that is over the head, shoulder or front, makes the leather wrinkled
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the swelling is small, if the limb has a slight tension, and one grasps it at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, if the swelling has reached the bone, and the bone is bruised, and the wound is opened, and the bone is brought together at the suture, and the wound is cured when it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	When it hangs downwards, swollen, from the socket.</start_of_turn>
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	Never before have I seen such a thing in the belly and nowhere else, and it is a disease which is called "funge" because of its resemblance to barley, and its root is subtle, and its head is large.
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and there are small and great swellings in it.
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw two people who had it in their bellies who seemed more like barley than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a thick root, and were split open, and there was moisture coming out of them
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I dressed them and found one of them weighing eighteen ounces, and the other six and a half pounds, and the works on the incision if you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the blood is pale and moist and has a subtle root.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	If the scapula at the greater wing be tense, and if it be in your presence the fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For in your presence comes often too great discharge of blood, and if you delay, if you do not hasten, then indeed you must cauterize;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	and if you see the patient groaning and fearful from the incision of the wound, if you take a thread of silk well made, and bind the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	Then the restraint, and do not cease to tighten the thread of silk until it holds the artery, and ask him to work for you;
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	and if the roots are large, if there is fear at the same time on the other side for the belly, but you must well cover half, then cauterize what does not return
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then treat the wound and keep that you do not cover the hair which is of a harsh color and of poor sense and of milk-like discharge.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an inflamed abscess, and I will come to the cure of the abscess later.</start_of_turn>
quant li boude ist fuer	When the head of the shoulder is for.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	Then if a bubble appears, it comes from the cautery of the wound or from a bursting of a cyst, and is above the belly and in the chest, as it happens in other ways, or blood that clots veins or arteries according to what is before, or from swelling;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is through the opening of the cyst and the coming out of the bubble, if it is the color of the abscess, it seems like the color of blood, and is a light matter causing little pain, and is open from various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	and if it is from the bursting of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it with the hands if it returns, and then comes back, and sometimes if it is caught, it swells out at the entrance to the bath and by great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light matter, and opens well when you press it with your hand, do not constrain me;
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is for blood, if it is widely apparent by these signs, the abscess is great and hard, and is closed according to a quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is for wind, if it is soft at the touch, and the work is that you see if it appears to be from the blood of an artery or a vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you leave the cure like that.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have already said or as the chapter discusses concerning abscesses, concerning the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if it appears to be from the intestine or the bowel, if you command the patient to hold his breath, and that he strain himself thoroughly, and mark that he has evacuated everything to the bottom;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	Then command him to grasp between your hands, then go round the limb that you have marked throughout the circumference, and take hold of half of the abscess at its base to the greatest extent
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	Then hold the limb firmly with a strong thread or a strong thread of silk, and keep it firmly in place.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then expose half of the abscess that is extended over the limb, and hold your thumb and index finger, and keep the intestines in place;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it grasped in the limb, if you pull it out, and pull the intestines away from the belly
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you find pus, if you grasp it with the tweezers, and drain the excess blood.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	And if the artery or vein is bleeding, if it is going to burst, then go back to your work and take two needles and put two strong threads, and pass the two needles through what you have made in the form of a cross that you make pierce
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then strain the abscess in four days on the nails, and if you see, break the nails, and leave the wound alone until it bursts, and extract the pus by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	Or you can bandage it when it is slight and soft, then cure it of what it covers, and cut the abscess as we have said before.</start_of_turn>
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	Then drain the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the wound of what it covers, and close the wound.</start_of_turn>
dou chancre	And extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the wound of what is necessary, and suture the wound.
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have said in the division the signs of an abscess, and how one should work on it with medicine, and how one should shun the cautery treatment.</start_of_turn>
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	We say that an abscess is always in the marrow, and great caution should be taken in its treatment, and they say that the old people often say that when an abscess is in the bone or we can break it if it is like an abscess that is in marrow, and in the marrow, and in similar things, and we must remove it when it is at its beginning.</start_of_turn
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	When it is large and old, if you do not approach it cautiously, for I know of no cure;
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	for I know of no healing for it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	When it is in the body or we can remove it, as we have said, you must never purge the black bile from the patient;
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	then make him healthy again if he has shown signs of fullness, and afterwards let the patient drink well to make the work easier
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then give your ointments or plaster, and the head and all parts, and the bone of all parts round about do not leave anything undone
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow freely, and press well the limb at your hand or at nothing, and if it breaks from the incision of the artery or vein, if you cauterize too much it will stain
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then perform another cure while he is conscious.
de ydropisie	De ydropisie.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have already mentioned in the preceding sections the signs of dropsy, and that when the collection of liquid is made, and the signs of congestion are similar, and the treatment which is done with medicines, and that which is done with fire.
si est eclites soulement;	if only it is illuminated only;
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one must not touch the fire in these two instances:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	namely, tympanites and yposclerosis, because it is a deadly thing
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	then when you give these medicines for this sign of dropsy which is called "eclipses" of medicines, and the cure does not benefit, if you notice that the patient is weak, or if there is another disease besides dropsy, as all other diseases and their solutions for the belly and similar things;
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	If there is doubt, do not touch the iron, for there is danger.
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	If you see the patient with great strength, and he has only the hydropisy of a simple dropsy, and he is neither too lean nor too fat, then you must surely work on him.
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	Believe the patient right on your hands, and press his belly down towards the lower part of his foot, then take the thumb of the hand that you use for this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let two parts be excised.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	almost without causing him to bleed; and do not let him scream
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	then look if the hydropisy is settled towards the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	if you think you have reached the third degree of hydropisy, do two right incisions above the navel;
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	And if dropsy is due to liver disease, if so make a incision at the left side of the abdomen below the third rib.
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	And if it is due to urine, if so make it at the right side, and do not let the patient lie on the incision where the fluid will flow towards the weaker limb.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	Then pierce through the skin with the instrument, and extract the stone, and hold your hand over the wound with all your might between the skin and the cartilage as if grasping the quantity of an nail or an inch in length
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Then pierce the cartilage until the muscle comes out whole, and that is the cause of the pain, then pull out the instrument, and there will be the shape of this instrument left there:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it is similar to a silver needle, and is of spider or slender barley, and has at its end a little hole.
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	or costs from one side, three holes.</start_of_turn>
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and two from the other side, and one from the other.</start_of_turn
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	and the head is cut off like a pen, and this is the shape of the incision which is written to cut off the head.</start_of_turn
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	above is the nourishment, so that when the instruments come into the water, if they go into the water now;
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	leave half or a third of it out, for if you take out more than that in this hour, by chance the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he will vomit, or he approaches death.</start_of_turn
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	But in emptiness according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the provisions of the virtue to the patient signify, and his pains.
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	Then take the instrument and hold the pain, and it is retained now by the thumb which stamps the part which is above the scapula, as I have said, that you pierce according to this manner.
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	Then take the instrument again the other way, if you see the patient suffering from this, and take out a small amount of pain;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	Do nothing of the sort, and take care not to use it until there remains only a little bit of pain.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you doubt about the patient, and you put too much pain, if the surgeon of the burial or sand burns, and by too much sweat or bath and sun, and if you take wine;
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And the treatment of drying medicines must be continued as long as the patient is well; and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the urine, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stomach of the sheath.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Never are children born without a mark in the belly, or the mark is small, or it is not firmly in its place.

puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	Then put or pull out I cloth of felt under the armpit, and bind and keep it in place for III days or IV; and when he wants to urinate, if he is kept closed, he will urinate, and then put him back again.</start_of_turn>
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	And by chance it must not be, for the urine that comes out will not leave him closed.</start_of_turn>
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the opening is small, if medicine is applied with lead weights, as we have said, and it swells up.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the head of the shoulder dislocated in their limb are blistered, for no one is born with the head of the shoulder at the top of the limb, for it will not urinate before it is elevated.</start_of_turn
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	And they do not manage to recover because the material cannot come up to the marrow, which is a bad disease.

des pustules de la verge	Des pustules de la verge.

Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the swelling is malignant, dark in color and purulent, it is advisable to apply cautery to it.

Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you treat it whole, if you do not keep the root firm, it will cause blackness and corruption in the root or bone.</start_of_turn

c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	namely, in the case of blood clots and corruption;

de la circoncision	except in the case of circumcision.</start_of_turn>
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not merely the omission of a continuation like other wounds.</start_of_turn
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	However, when we perform this work of our will, and do it properly, if it is necessary that we make it better, and the most pleasant for health.</start_of_turn
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not teach us circumcision, for they did not use it in their laws, and we have only what we have learned through experience
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have seen the greatest part of masters and physicians who perform circumcision in this way, have force and all a new instrument.</start_of_turn
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	If the urine flees like water because of two stones, and by chance if one of these comes up and stops the other below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	Or the bladder recoils, and there is double pain, and with swelling which is dull and does not firmly support the point of the limb.
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and with the swelling of the spleen by chance escapes the iron, repairs the work, and many times grow until they have no need of swelling and I have wished it so

Or the covering returns, and the pain is doubled, and with the support which is too slight to assure the tip of the limb; and with the support of the cord by chance escapes the iron, and completes the work, and many times it happens that they are born without any support and I want it.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, if it is equally taut throughout, you can easily pull it out.

et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and that the manner of the first work should make the child think, if he understands, that you do not make him suffer more than to tie the thread around the limb only lightly, and then let him do whatever he wishes

et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And I put powder on and over the powder I drape a layer of glue made from the yolk of an egg beaten with rosewater, confirmed with rosemary oil and balsam, and I leave it on until the other side is done, and I treat the other wound until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The forces are formed at the circumference of the wound when this is the case:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	When the two heads are tense and bent, and the arms are as wide as the palm of the hand:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	The wound of the circumference is when the cords around the incisions are loose.

si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	if you do not move it as you wish and keep hold of the lower part of the belly, it will do you no good.</start_of_turn>

cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure it as we have said until it is healed.</start_of_turn
dou retenement de l’urine	Dou retenement de l’urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	Urine is retained if it is from the obstruction of a stone, or blood congealed, or bile, or chaff, or similar things, as we have said in the division.</start_of_turn
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	And if the urine does not flow freely, and you see that the retention is caused by the stone which is in the kidney or the neck of the bladder, if you suspect that the patient is hunching over his knees;

et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	And if it be of subtle silver coin, as much as a hen’s egg;
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	And if it be of blunt silver coin, as much as half an egg, and if it is subtle at the head.

et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And cover the surplus of wool and pass the syringe up to the head of the syringe, then join the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on one chair, and raise the bladder and the verge of oil moist and oily with olive oil and warm water.

puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	Then withdraw the syringe until it reaches the bladder, and the patient will feel it coming out until it reaches the empty thing; this should not be done except in this order because otherwise it will cause damage to the body.
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then stretch the thread throughout its length, and the urine will follow the thread, then pull out the thread forcefully, and correct the urine;
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And restart the syringe until the bladder is empty, and align the patient
des maladies de la vessie	Des maladies de la vessie.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there are dropsy or blood in the bladder, or putrefaction is assembled, and you see urine and medicines distilled, if you do everything that is called the «clepsedre», which is its shape:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and if there are three holes:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	Two from one side, and one from the other, as you see;
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	And he must bend his head downwards so that the medicine can penetrate as well as possible, if we can remove the moisture, and push firmly as is necessary.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	When you see the medicine dripping in the bladder, put the chief dexterous over the moisture, and push away what is hindering.
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	If you remove the moisture from the dexterous, and then push strongly the hindering away

et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	This is the form of the subtle fistula from which we must cure the bladder.
si est ci:	If this is the case:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	It is of silver or gold, and the head is more raised
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	And from the eye inwards, or from the joint which is hurt;

et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And do as you would with a bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture goes from the bladder.
de la piere	De la piere.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have already said in the division the ways of cutting into stones, and the extraction of medicines together.
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	And I have said the difference between the enclosed stone and the open stone, and all the signs, and when one must work on a stone of what size;

et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	And it is light to heal the wounds until they are three years old, and it is grief in old men, and is as young as middling age, to those who are between youth and old age
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	And it is the easier cure for those who have the big stone, than for those who have the small one
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is necessary, we must first cleanse the patient by blistering, to drive out all the evil that is in the intestines.

puis la quier et la touche dedens;	Then the sweat and the touch within;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	if you feel the stone in the cavity, if you hurry now to clamp above the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	and if it does not bleed at the touch, put your left thumb oil on the index finger, if the patient is old, or your middle finger, if the patient is young with accomplices;

puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	then press on your finger, and hold the stone away from the eye or you see the clamp
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	and instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and he commands him to extend with his right hand the ribs above, and with his left hand to stretch the skin that is below the ribs in the part where the incision is made
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Then I touch the scab with my thumb, since this is its form.

par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	By chance the pressure if the thumb that is or is rooted, that it leaps for work;
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	And nails that are part of the stone or that have angles, and margins.
si est griés a issir;	If it is grasped to irritate;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And if a limb is swollen, seems bulky and round, from which issue is generous.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	And thus when there are angles and margins [in the swelling], make the size greater.
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and if it does not burst, you must know that you must pull on the nails which are as much as a file at the head, so that you can pull out the stone if it does not escape;

Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For two things happen to the patient:

de la piere des femmes	If you cannot do this for any reason, take hold of the bone at its upper and lower extremities, then place the thumb between the two tendons, and grasp firmly; then extract the foreign body, loosen the tendon, and solidify the blood that is in the wound; and cure until it is healed.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	When the stone is embedded in flesh, and if it does not happen every time, if it is cured, it is defended by three things:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	one is that by chance the woman is a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	And the second is that no woman can be known to be truly wise who hides her wisdom as deeply as she can, even though she is learned.

de la routure dou syfac	from the root to the surface
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The outcome of this limb is by the section which comes from above or from the flank, or the extension above the belly in the part of the groin, for in this way the intestines descend from that passage to one of the buttocks.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	And this passage is either by section or by extension of the bowels, and comes from these two methods of eating which are the cause of these two matters
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	or by percussion, or by jump, or by pressure, or by lifting of burden, or by similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	And the sign that it is an extension of the flank is that there is swelling and swelling, in a long tense, and does not come immediately
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	And it is the abscesses which are equal in size until towards the belly, forasmuch the spleen presses the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when the jaw is fractured, that it causes sudden pain at the start, and the abscesses are diverse in appearance, such as bursting skin and exposed bone, because of the escape of the intestine and the hardness of the jaw.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never should the limb be moved with the intestine, and is retained when it is held, and causes great pain to the patient, even when it is pressed
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments with fire there is fear, for it is known to escape.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And as for the work if you command or patient that he pull the intestine back into its place in the wound, if it can enter there again.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	Then hold his collar between your hands, and keep his thighs still;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	Then stretch his arm downward, and grasp all the skin of his buttocks long
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	Then keep the liver from the size of a nut according to what you must do to open the wound, and be like that so that it does not swell up again
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then loosen the spleen that is under the skin of the buttocks, until the fatty spleen has become uncovered throughout
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;	Then hold your thumb against the joint that teaches the connection, in that which is between the white tuff which is below the skin of the egg-shell, and between the second tuff, and depart that which is behind the egg-shell, and between the second tuff.
et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	And thus move the hand downwards from the shoulder joint, and when the white tuff is at the top of your left hand, keep the egg-shell against all the tufts towards the size
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	And command the minister to extend the egg-shell upwards, and loosen that which is behind the ligament.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	And if there is any intestine or white tuff enclosed or hardened, and if you find nothing, if the egg-shell is below the belly
puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions;	Then take a needle or if there is a thick thread made of X threads, and pass it through the back part of the scapula, which is behind the skin of the shoulder blades.
aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz;	Then the size, then tie off the head of the dislocation that appears from the threads, until there are three threads remaining.
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;	Then gather them together in the form of a cross, and bind the scapula, as we have said which is behind the skin of the shoulder blades, with a strong thread of two parts
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	Then encircle the head of the dislocation with the threads, and bind them firmly with two parts, so that no vessels which nourish them can enter there, only the incision which we made.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	And put the thread straight according to the first thread as long as two fingers, and after these two fingers leave the scapula which is behind the shoulder blades as much as the great toe of the boot
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte;	And afterwards according to the roundness of the eggshell.
puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	Then they are cut in the part which is below the skin of the testicles, as much as without repair, and they swell, as we have said before
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	Then mix coarse wool with oil, put in wounds, and bring in the thread that we have mentioned before
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never is the bladder cauterized after the incision, out of doubt of the discharge of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui;	For this often happens, and let the thread alone until it stops itching for itself
et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	and if it hangs too long, if it is raised by hot water, and put on what we have mentioned, until it stops itching
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then cure the wound of another way, until it is perfectly healed
de hernie carnouse	of a hernia.

de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	from the softening of the skin of the armpits.

dou chastrement	of great suffering.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	Wounds that are scraped off are forbidden in our laws, and for this reason I would not speak of them in this book.
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	and are necessary only in two ways:
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	one is that the owner of the wound responds when asked, and in the wound the cure;
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	and the other is that we often see bestes being scraped off by our assistants, as with pigs and sheep and goats and other beasts.</start_of_turn>
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	I say therefore that scrapes are done in two ways:</start_of_turn>
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	Or by traction, or by incision.
