puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	Then grasp it with your hand, until it is reset and you can no longer feel it
Du chastrement de taille:	From the armpit downwards:

des hermofrodites	Hairs that are scorched with fire are commanded to the patient to leave them long and even; and if they prick at their root, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	Then cure the wound until it is healed.
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Then cure the wound until it is healed

de la tentigene	Hermaphroditism is in two ways like that of women: one if between the two testicles appears as in the nature of a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in the urine.  And the other way if it is in women, and has on the navel like a beard and two testicles.  And the cure for the shame and the fame if it is that you cut off the testicles altogether, and the cure is like other wounds; in the second way, of those homes whose urine spurts through the skin of the testicles, if there is no cure.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	Then cure the wound until it is healed
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Then cure the wound until it is healed

et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And do not go too far from the wound, for the blood does not come from there; then take care of another remedy until it is healed.
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	And there is another case where it comes from the root of the marrow, and the swelling, and by chance it leaps up, and this is like the semblance of a wound, and for this reason it is called the old "cowardly disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you manage to hold it firmly, as we have said, and cure it until it is healed.
de erratique	De erratique.

et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	and it is natural in childbirth, or an accident from illness that it comes about;

des emorroides	From hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Hemorrhoids are veins that swell excessively and usually do not recover without treatment, and when they become old they harden.</start_of_turn
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	And we have said above concerning the signs and symptoms, and I will tell you those which bring about recovery.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and thrombi, when they are pressed down in the rectum, and are not felt, if not treated by force.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those which are at the mouth of the rectum, we can feel, are those which we can cure.

des apostemes de la marris	Emoroids are openings of veins which without restraint usually occur; and when they are old, they become thickened. We have already mentioned in the division the signs and symptoms; and I will say here those which resolve the cure. I say that emorroids and thick blood, when they are mixed in the marrow, and are not perceptible to the touch, if not treated with iron. Those which are at the edge of the marrow, we can perceive, are those which we can cure. It is therefore necessary that you place the woman in a cold house, then extend the ankle and grasp the heel, then sprinkle on medicinal astringents such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then remove the pieces an hour later, and put them in cold water; and if there is any bleeding, if you make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and saffron and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and assails, and make one plaster on her back. And if it is fainting, that is good. If this does not happen, if there is still bleeding at the edge, make a wound there with a needle; then take lint and moisten it in the juice of plantain or in the juice of elderberry with wine vinegar, and make the wound bleed. And when the wound has healed, if the bleeding has ceased, that which is called ‘albathir’ is red, and is similar to a rough chief, if you cover it as I have said the thickened blood; and then the bleeding will cease. And when the wound has healed, if the bleeding has ceased, that which is called ‘albathir’ is red, and is similar to a rough chief, if you cover it as I have said the thickened blood; and then the bleeding will cease.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	There are many kinds of abscesses that come in the belly, such as carbuncles and pierced abscesses and herpes and worms and tumors and fistula and hemorrhoids and burnt abscesses, and other diseases that I have mentioned in the previous division
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	It is necessary that I say that in this treatment of the cautery abscess that comes in the marrow, which is not like ordinary abscesses that are only painful
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	And if you see the work of the iron, if the abscess is already formed at the beginning of its coming, and is full of heat and fever, and if it turns red, then you must know it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	Therefore do not hasten to pierce, but let me measure until the pain is eased;
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	and then make the patient sit on a seat, and take two small stools or he leans, and support his back and join his limbs together so that the limb is supported;
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	and spread his thighs, and put his arms down by his knees, and bind them well with a strong bandage
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	then mix the bail towards the breastbone, and bring the instrument from which we expect the pus to come out; for in this way it will form
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	And it must be known that when you see it approaching with this instrument, grasp the root first in order to know the depth of the wound, so that what enters between the instrument and the wound does not go deeper than it should, and does not harm the patient.
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	and if the instrument is greater, if you must cover the depth of the wound with cloths, so that the instrument does not cause pain
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	and you must put the horn of the instrument at the base, and hold the instrument firmly.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	When the wound is opened and the hand is bled, if you must cover the head and the armpit with a cloth, respectively;
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	When the wound is emptied, if you must put in the wound some soft cotton wads soaked in rose oil or in dry green oil
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	And put the tension force of the wound at the bottom of the marrow, and put by default above the marrow and above the ribcage linen net soaked in water or cooked mallows.
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure afterwards two days following this, until it is healed;
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	and never lift the marrow and the wound with a clamp of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lilies and irises long are cooked
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	Then return to the wound.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound has been closed in the wound, if you wish, that you take care not to burn it, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	From infancy.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	The master is first at play that he knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman press down the jaw, and desire odor the er:

et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	And when you see these signs, if you must gently press his belly, so that the fetus is thrust out;

Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	For it never comes from its bones, but from force of the body, the head or the shoulder, the arms, or it comes from his belly or from the side, and is converted by an accident from his collar and by other harmful figures;
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier. Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	If she comes upon his head by natural issue, and the woman groans, and her virtue is weak, if she sits on a chair, or the women hold her;
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	and she arose her nature of oil or rue, or whatever is fragrant, and then she must dance between her two little toes which are the form of a foot

de l’issue des gemelz	When the dislocation is slight

de l’enfant mort	From childhood death.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you cure a woman of a dead child or belly, as I said in the division, and there is no great force, and you are compelled to work with your hands;

et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	This is the form of the ointment:

Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly had two fetuses inside, one died and the other remained.

Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvel indeed, for in this belly there is no bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.

et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And this is the shape of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the treatment neither be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the blister with oil or balm of egg, or something similar, and then cover it lightly
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	Then grasp the minister with both hands together, until it is quite visible, then remove the blister, and let the patient rest his legs at the surface, and if the medicine wishes, it should suffice as long as the thread can stay in its place
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And if it sleeps all night, there is greater aid
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see him lying in sickness with a swelling of the belly, and the physician hastens to leave, if he resumes as soon as he is well.</start_of_turn>
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if it swells up on the skin or foundation, or abscess, if the blister is as fine as for a child
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And this is the shape of a subtle blister on which the skin is strained:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have already said in the previous chapter the treatment of wounds.
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	or you will say the treatments of hands and medicines, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on what causes them, and depending on the limbs or wounds that are made, and how they are made
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things which are done for wounds are done by cutting stone, and the size of spear, nail, lance or fist, or stone or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or that are done according to the rules of the body, as when there is a wound on the neck, or the head, or the foot, or the belly, or the liver, or similar parts
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment for a chest wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, because the memory will come to you in this chapter
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes or a fracture occurs, and the bone is not broken, if you take care that it is not from a stone or similar things, and the skin is thoroughly ruptured and the wound is large, and you doubt the abscess is hot:
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if you do so soon as the head of the skull itself comes from the wound, or if the blood comes from the part furthest from the wound;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and you will hear the patient's pulse full of wine and meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	and if he does not recover, if he vomits blood or does not drink wine, does not eat meat;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and draw out the wound, if an abscess comes, cover it with soft wool soaked in rose oil only, or in astringent wine.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	If there is no surrounding tissue around the wound, put the wound on the fresh blood, which is not moved by air, dust, or anything else; I will tell you about this later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the blood has moved, put on some sponges until it is whole.</start_of_turn>
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great like the size of a spear and similar, and the limbs do not naturally unite, if you unite them with sutures, as I will say, for wounds of the belly, with sutures.</start_of_turn
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and is gaping, and only held by a thread, if the surgeon sees it.</start_of_turn
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	Then cure the wound with medicine, and restore the flesh hard instead of leather, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as testicles and bread, as well as poultry, and the like.</start_of_turn
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find or leather spoiled, and there is no bone, if the surgeon sees it, pull out all the decay and throw it away, then cure it.</start_of_turn
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which without support, and it cannot be staunched by medicines, if the artery is torn, and if you find it displaced, bind it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if that does not help, if you must cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is gentle:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and put on this powder that will harden as soon as it touches the air
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	The powder is to be applied in the form of a paste
pren encens une partie;	take incense in one part;
sanc de dragon II parties;	blood of a dragon two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	live charcoal three parts, and the powdered [substance], and apply to the wound, and hold firmly, until it contracts well and unites with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then bind it firmly, and let it loosen, if it does not swell
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for one must not administer the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never shall one do this treatment alone, when there is neither incense nor blood of a dragon, but only when the wound has not moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	and if the wound has moved, even in this state, if one does not put on this powder;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some unguents that digest, or poulps of flour of barley made of water and honey, until it boils over
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other treatments until it is healed
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if a break of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, if the bone is extracted with fine needles;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And I will tell you of this later.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If there is no difference between the fracture of the head and the fracture of the neck, but if the neck or the artery is cut
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is bone marrow, if there is no other remedy except to leave the wound open, and do not put anything restrictive, because it hinders the marrow and makes it recede.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	Do not put anything rough on the wound, for the substance of the marrow is cold, and the continuation of the pain is with the brain, which is the most tender member
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	But if the medicine be soft, like warm water in sweet oil, and mixed with rosemary oil, and vinegar washed in sweet water, and other stones of mine according to this method, and moist compresses.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, if the blood vessel and the nerves are torn, then cure as long as it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and closed and full of pus, if the hole is high or more towards the base;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	If the artery is severed and blood flows profusely, if the swelling and the wound, and the cautery are mixed together, then.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	If the spine of the shoulder is severed, or the scapula, and the bone is held, so that the meat is not damaged, if the scapula is above the glenoid fossa, do not touch the shoulder but reset it to its natural position.
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then strain the wound immediately, and leave it alone for a while, then treat it with ointment until it is healed;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	And if the wound has made an imprint in the bone, if the marrow;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	If there are pieces of bone, if the wounds are severe throughout, if these you cannot have, if you leave them as they are, let them burst open and align the issue.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wound is fresh, if powder is applied as I have said.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is fistula, if the wound must be closed as I have said in this chapter.</start_of_turn>
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a wound from a lance or a knife.</start_of_turn
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is from a spear or a knife, and the wound is deep, look if the wound is surrounded by swelling so that the patient cannot align their limb.</start_of_turn>
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	Then let the wound be mortal.</start_of_turn
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	And if it is not deep and is fresh throughout, do not put anything on it for the first hour, do not bind it up with the dressing until it is painful and bursting, return to the body and comfort the patient.</start_of_turn
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	But I put an attractive weight upon it, and I bind it twice over.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	And if there is no weight, put on the wound a great quantity of cotton to absorb the moisture, and let the patient rest on the wound for three days, or four, or more
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	If there is no spasm, do not cause the body to tremble excessively or excessive straining of the limbs
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	When you see the bones in their place, consider the wound to be healed
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Treat the wound and other cures, as long as it is healthy
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	And if it does not heal, and there is pus, consider that there is a fistula
si la cure si com on doit.	If the treatment must be so.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	If the wound is a cut or incision of a spear or knife, and it is simple or deep, or at the back, if the treatment of what is before [is insufficient];
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	then it requires stitching
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, powder is sufficient, and if it is embedded in the bone, and if pieces break off, if there is pain in the wound, and the surrounding area is blackened;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	if they are not blackened, let the wound rest, if it aligns the extractions
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds, as for other limbs, it is the judge’s decision as we have said
dou derrompement dou ventre	indeed
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The pain of the belly is great, medium, and small.
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	The great wound of the belly never stops bleeding, or the nerves of the intestines are cut, because of the admission of blood.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	The wound is more painful, and never worth more than the small wound, because of this we must return the intestines to their place immediately, if we do not return them bit by bit;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	because they swell so much that they feel the pain, if we return them bit by bit, it is worth less than the greater wound, because in this way we leave the intestines in their place along with the others two times
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And the swelling of the belly is according to three methods:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	The two common sutures are in the belly suture and the other wound in the flesh and two other proper sutures are common as other wounds.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	And indeed, they are more proper with the belly suture, and I will say a little bit and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small and there is nothing of the intestines inside, and if there is anything, it is by one of these two methods:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen by the fruit.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, freeze it partly in this way:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	wet a sponge or lay a cloth in cold water only, or you will burn in cold water stinging and pricking and spiking, and elevate the intestine until the swelling is bony;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And never again did I make this wine restraining, for it is mute that it stirs the soul to burst.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	When you see the swelling depart, if the gut of water or the belly is high and bloated, for by this is the entrance to things aligned
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	If it cannot enter, if there is a wound there, with the instrument we hold the swellings still
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	The first cure is to make it mute that the size does not require great necessity or that there be no need;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	And this is the instrument for cutting
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	If you trench downwards in the shoulder and do not withdraw, and once this is done, the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is swollen, and the intestines protrude outwards, if you stop bleeding in accordance with the natural form in its place, know that you have done well, for this is enough.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is large and is in the lower part of the belly, if you must manage the patient on his back, raise his legs above his head.
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	If it is in the lower part of the belly, put the head and arm higher than the lower parts, and if the wound is in the lower part of the belly, if it is in one of the two lower parts, put your hand over that which is higher than the other
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and so it is necessary to support what I say in large and gaping wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	Small wounds put what appears to be holding, then put your hands between the wounds and support the wound with your hands, and close the wound
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	This is the common method of stitching, and take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the wound’s size, then leave the head of the wound at a distance, and pierce with a needle or there is strong thread.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	And pierce the two armpits with the two fingers of the siphac, which is to say the skin of the armpits, until you have pierced to that part; and reunite the two fingers of the siphac with the three fingers together.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then strain with a double thread around the needle of two parts, and reunite the two fingers of the wound immediately, and then leave one space, and pierce another hole.</start_of_turn>
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Then tie the thread like the first needle, and do not stop doing so until you have finished piercing according to what you have learned from the needles, until the wound is restricted.</start_of_turn
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	And let the needles be neither too fine nor too thick, for the fine needles will not grasp the flesh, and the thick ones will not enter well.</start_of_turn>
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	For this reason, it is recommended that they be blunt;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and it is not recommended to press the needles too far into the flesh and skin, as they may break and open the wound before the suture is complete.</start_of_turn>
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then keep the head of the needles still, so that they do not irritate the patient at night, and put on tension or a bandage on the head of the needles to hold them in place, and leave them in until the wound is healed.</start_of_turn
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this way of stitching with needles is more convenient in small wounds, because there is only one or two needles involved.</start_of_turn>
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second suture is common, and is that you join the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the substance together with a needle or there is one strong middle thread.</start_of_turn
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	And when you have perceived these things altogether, if you rejoin the needle at the place where you began, in the manner in which it is customary to close the edges;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put some space between each stitch the thickness of a barleycorn.
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This stitch should be made on the flesh, and I sew a wound which has been caused by a knife, which is greater than a palm of the hand, and it is in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I shall bring back the intestine when it has been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound has healed for fifteen days; then I shall cure it, and it will be healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the blood spurted from the wound as if it would die, and this was a miracle.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not care for it, because I was in the wilderness where there was no healing, no medicines of any kind;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the method more effective for the wound is to apply a compress twice a day, and to wash it with honey water until it is healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Or thus I shall tell you two ways to suture:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and pass it from the underside of the edge just as far as necessary to reach the underside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	When it has grasped the edge on the right, if there is a slip or the needle has pierced, and you have passed the needle through from the underside of the edge just as far as necessary to reach the underside again;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And the understanding of this suture is that you should stitch as a tailor does the leather, and that you leave once the slip has passed from one side, and you take it back from the other, until the suture is complete
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second method of stitching, which Galiens does indeed know well, if it is so with any, that joins the two parts together naturally, and leans one chief against the other chief, in part manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	He sews on a hook or chief near the edge, and makes the latter pass only through the latter, and leaves the two chiefs of the spic;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	then he turns the hook, and makes him pass through from the back until he reaches this far side, as two chiefs of spic.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	and makes him pass through one and the other from the back until he reaches this far side, in two other hooks that are on the other side
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and that is the quiet method of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galiens if this word is false, and no one testifies, we must suture the belly with two needles, or there must be thread in the seam.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and we must push one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who suture wounds
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and the stitches must be strong enough so that when the wound is opened again the belly does not burst more than usual.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judge of the wound is like the judge of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and if you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even if it has moved, you must stop the bleeding and the pain
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then apply powder to the wound and if it has moved, do not put any dressing that is present, until the wound is closed
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	And the hair grows, and the scabs are soldered, and the mark is seen.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure the wound like the others, as long as it is healthy;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you have no medicine, if you put it on, as long as it begins to swell, cotton wool, and move twice the juice as long as it is healthy
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you must not have any other medicine except in simple wounds
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you doubt that the wound will not heal properly, cover the principal parts with coarse linen soaked in warm oil of thyme or rose oil, and put it between the edges, and drain the abscesses
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if there is pain or putrefaction in the bowels, and it happens many times, if you immerse in clusters of black wine it will help, and the same if the putrefaction comes up to the intestines;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	And the large intestines, their masses more readily cured than the small intestines.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jeuns" cannot recover when they are swollen, because of the swelling of the veins, and for the subtlety of all the body, and for the proximity of their nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	If the spleen bursts from the wound, if it is returned backwards just like the intestine while it is still fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	And if it is black and becomes towards black or white, if you must know that you must bind the black part, because there are veins and arteries there;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	Then hold that which is between the ribs, and put the two thumbs hanging down from the part under the wound until they are withdrawn to align the extraction when the spleen bursts, and the wound is closed
de la routure dou boueil	Of the root of the boil.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestine is round and the wound is small, if you can restore it in small pieces, because I know that one has been grazed by a spear or the belly of a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	And it was the wound on the right side of the stomach, and it became filled and turned into an fistula, and in this there was vomiting and flatulence.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I put it to cure as I could, and did not cease to support it until it was healed, and the wound closed.</start_of_turn>

et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	Then he grasps the head, and if it does not slip away, put in another support afterwards in the same way as before, until the wound is completely healed.

Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If the head of the intestines is burnt, and there is no further discomfort for the patient, and it can be tied up with a fine thread which is cut from the intestines themselves, in part like this:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	take hold of this thread of intestine that is already discharged, and then tie at the head of this thread a thread of fine linen twisted, and then pass the thread through the needle, and sew the intestine, and hold it in place.</start_of_turn>
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this way of stitching is not strong except according to the way of engaging and hoping;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if the wound is large and wide, even if it is in one of the great intestines, if there is no swelling or contamination, it is only due to its slightness.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of fistula or that it be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Wounds and abscesses, when they swell, if they are called universally 'fistules,' and even when they are sewn and rent bowe.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	A fistula is confirmed by a hard and white nodulation, and there is no pain, and is just like the foot of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	never in clear water, but sometimes thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	never too little, but sometimes enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not sanitized, and there is pus, is only fierce from one of the seven causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the small amount of blood or pus;
ou por sa malice;	or for its malice;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or for its malice; or because there is great hardness within and on the limbs, that they do not allow new hair to grow.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there is too much tension;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the limb is twisted, and the matter is of poor quality
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the treatment is not good for the cure
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because corruption is like a plague
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because in that area property is late for digestion, and late for health, and escapes by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already mentioned these causes, signs, and treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or you must know that I will tell you the cure of fistula which is made by an egg of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Wounds that have become fistulated appear in all limbs with pain.
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	For there are fistulas that arise from great veins, arteries, nerves, or the spleen, intestines, bladder, or some bones, or the spin of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if in part it comes from the primary limb, and similar things happen.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all these fistulas of this kind are bad for healing, and there is only toil and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is no fistula that does not go beyond what I have said, and you have promised a cure, and you see it is known, if you take an attempt to drain or burn it, if the fistula is straight, if not;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	If the fistula is tortuous, if the hook of a slender needle attempts to plunge, for the swelling swells inward towards the curvature;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	If the fistula has holes and you do not secure it well with hooks, if the swelling bursts through one of the holes, for the moisture is too strong from one hole to another, and it deflates.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	Then if the limb is hanging limply from your hand, that you know if there is bone or nerve damage, and that it is swollen, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press your hand, and where it hurts
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you know truly where it is, if it is far from a joint or nerve, or an artery or vein, or any of the bones that I have mentioned, if you have accepted what I have said, and if the fracture is displaced and the corrupt parts that are within
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	And then the treatment must be continued until it is healed; and if the fistula is well formed from the outset, if you can, close it from the start, just as you would do with a wound; then put in some soft patches in medicine, and leave them until the medicine consumes the superfluous matter that is remaining at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then put in absorbent dressings to keep it dry until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And if it is not healed by that, if the burn it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, if it is closed
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If the vein or nerve does not swell or the main parts do not ache, as we have said
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if the bone is discovered and there is corruption and blackness, if the limb is lame as long as the corruption is all bone, then treat with absorbent dressings until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	If he is not sane, and returns bowed as before, take hold of his hair that you may not let him go until he is well.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	if he pulls and wants as long as you stay at the bottom, and breaks through all the corruption, then restore the limb.</start_of_turn>
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if he is already sane, that is good.</start_of_turn>

si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is nothing else to do but to leave it to its natural course.</start_of_turn

et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, grasp firmly and moisten and stretch, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	If you do not remove them at once, if you put on the wound something that causes putrefaction, and leave them until the bones become soft within the bones, then indeed they will become lighter.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	And if it is a large bone, such as a limb or thigh, if you remove the corruption as much as possible until the black is entirely bony, then restore the wound.

et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And I will tell you of a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so that you may take note and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	There was once a young man about XXX years of age who had a pain in his leg caused by something within the body, until the matter came out through a large abscess; there was no known cause for opening it.</start_of_turn>
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but he became mad with worry about the abscess opening up so much that he bled profusely from the matter coming out, and it became a fistula, and there came out much pus that flowed over the body and moistened the wound.</start_of_turn

et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	And became red the colour of youth, and had the colour of citrine.

dou feu	indeed fire.
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, or by pressure, or by force;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have treated that decay by the means of medicines, and it does no good, if you can cover that limb until the decay goes away, or the disease escapes by that, for the patient either escapes by death, or by the malice, which is greater, of the defect of the limb

si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you are in a hurry and it is by the percussion of venomous creatures such as scorpions of the sea and vipers and similar, if the corrosion is at the root of the tooth, if you bite and do not give it space to come until the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	If it comes until the hand, if the bite has reached the joint, if the corrosion does not reach the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it comes to the arm, if the bite is on the nail;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the nail, it is death, and there is no remedy but the quantity of its virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and thus do all things when the corrosion comes or the tooth is broken
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it comes in the first joint, if the bite follows the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	And if it comes or if it is pressed, if you seize all the hair;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	And if it comes or if it is pressed, if you seize all the hair; and if it comes up in the limb, if you grasp at the joint of the armpit.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it comes from below the armpit, if there is no other remedy but to leave the patient dead;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you must grasp the member below and above, and extend one minister of the lower limb and another minister of the upper limb, and you must saw the flesh between the two limbs at a wide space, until the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Then grasp the bone or the skin, and put some lint between the drape and the limb, so that the skin does not touch the sound limb, and bring to the patient other lesions and incisions

puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then return to your medicine until it is accompanied, and then bind the limb firmly with a strong thread, and cure it while it is whole.</start_of_turn>
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you that I have seen at home in this matter.</start_of_turn>
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	there was a blackness that seemed to burn like fire, and that corruption began at its root in the bone, so that it consumed the whole limb.</start_of_turn
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when we saw the corruption, if we covered the limb and it was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and long after it returned the corruption or the bone of the hand, and I came to it, and I put on things that rebound after the purification of the ulcer, and I could not stop the corruption.</start_of_turn
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	And he says that I should grasp his hand, and I will not, for I avoid all hope of recovering the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	I also doubt that if I cut off his hand, he will not die, for the virtue of the man was weak.
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	And he awoke entirely, returned to his land, and covered his hand, and was healed
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	I have heard of this case only because of the other things we have seen in this matter
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Never comes abscess in flesh without making great swelling.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	And then bursts and breaks, and in leaping the swelling comes out, and leaves the wound open as if it were a vessel
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And the skin that lies below is just as flexible as draped fabrics, and does not adhere to bone or nerve, and such a condition is called "sain", and is not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is stretched too far as to reach the bone, it is called "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin if it is tightly stretched over this skin and the same when it is flexible, is like a draped fabric
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not adhere to its corruption.

regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Look if the wound is large, and if the foul odor comes from it, then clusterize the Egyptian medicine which is made like this.
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take oil, and herbs, and beeswax, equally, and mix them up in a vessel over a fire, until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	And then take according to your need, and make it into water and honey, and clusterize the wound, and restrain the opening.

et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	And never clusterize with vinegar, when this medicine is not present, and only take vinegar of must of grapes, and pour out water, then drain, and clusterize, until you are sure that the wound is well healed.

et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	If the nail of the thumb is pierced, and the flesh around the nail does not enter, if a nail has become loose, put in an attempt of Egyptian resin, or beeswax, as much as it is enlarged.

If the wound is too wide, if the thumb and index finger leave such space that the nail can enter, and if the nail has pierced too deeply, if the pulp has gone below the nail, if the nail is higher than the skin below.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the nail is deeply pierced, if it does not leave enough space to grasp the hair;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you do not cover the nail end if you see, if it appears in such a manner that the nail goes below the lowest level, for when the nail is deeply pierced, if it does not leave enough space to grasp the hair and if you do not cover the nail end if you see, if it appears in part in this way

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the boil.</start_of_turn>

et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, put something above which will soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	And if it happens, if you put something on that relieves the pain of the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints that naturally grow in the hands of certain people are always fleshy, and in some cases there is a part where there is bone, and never a nail, or that they are born at the root of the joint, or that the birth is in our thumbs.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	That which is born without fear of pain does not move, and that which is born at the joint is by chance moved;

In him who is born or must afterwards without a doubt, if you must, first bend the rounded flesh around the bone, then grasp the bone at a convenient place like this, then hold it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The sudden pains that ensue must be brought about by birth, or by wound, or by fire cautery, or by similar things.

des vils	Des vils.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The veins are large veins enclosed in fat filled with black bile, which causes swelling in many limbs with pain;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more often come from those that are fat and lazy and work and bear burdens, than from others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	You must not give the patient any purgatives or enemas of any kind, and then afterwards the rest of the treatment.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The treatment of iron is in two ways:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is with the cautery, and one treats the black blood
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And thus too, if you tie up the vein and push it out, do it with all your might.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The size of this method is as follows:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	first rise the hot water-soaked limb very high, until the large vessels are not constricted, then strain the limb of the patient downwards from the buttocks to the part below the knee
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then grasp the vein in one, or two, or three places, of a large size, then cut and pull out the black blood from your hand, from the top to the bottom, as much as the patient can tolerate;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bind it and command him to keep pressure with meat pressing on the black bile;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And he recommences the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The ailments of this sort are according to this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Raise the limb of the patient, if there is moisture in the hair, then wash it out, and elevate the limb until it turns red, and swell the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bath, if the fire burns, and then hold the vein long at the shoulder or at the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then cover the skin with fat, and stretch the vein carefully from the armpit, until it appears when you touch it

puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then pull the skin over the vein until it appears, then pull the thumb towards the heel as you have done before, and then pull at another nail as you have done before.</start_of_turn>
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	Then grasp another size, or more if you wish, and pull it out, and grasp the thumb and index finger, and pull them until the second size is reached.</start_of_turn
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then pull out the size by size until it is all out, and then grasp it.</start_of_turn>
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you do not pull it out and lift it, if there is a splinter at the root of the hair, grasp it and pull it out, and grasp the limb from the top and bottom, until it is freed.</start_of_turn
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And keep it still, for if it moves, it cannot be treated or lifted, and comes to the harm of the patient.

Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	and if its vein is contracted and tortuous and surrounded together, and is not straight, as we have said, if you must do violence to it, do so with all your might, but do not cover it over
