Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron from which the limb is treated if it is crooked, do not twist it, but only hold it still;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	And it is of great danger, for if it were subtle, it would burst the vein; but whether it is great or small, as we have said, this is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein.</start_of_turn>
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	And this vein is enclosed in the limb, in hot parts or where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	And it appears in another place besides the limb, and this comes from the corruption that comes from the decomposition of the skin, as it comes from the belly of a serpent towards the back, enclosed between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if there is a sign of the commencement of this vein, that is to say if there comes into the limb a very great inflammation, then it must be bound up tightly, and the vein must be forced to desist, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the head of the shoulder is burst, if you think you should wrap around a piece of lead from one and a half inches to two and a half inches, and the knot, and leave the lead in the limb, and every time it swells up, if you wrap around the lead the knot and the limb again
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, if in a part it is cut off, and it embraces the remainder, do not cover it in its root, until it is completely expelled.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cover it, if it returns to the bone, it causes inflammation and gangrene or death, and makes the disease worse.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	therefore it is necessary to treat it thoroughly and completely, and leave nothing or bone behind
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	never is this vein treated with five palms of length, or ten, and one hand comes out to me, from ten palms of length, and when you cover it, if there remains even a hair or hole, and you pierce it through to the end, so that everything is gone
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	or the matter that is inside is evacuated, and mix with the medicine that prevents gangrene, and then cure it like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And never in this vein have hands rained, even when it opens at the elbow or the wrist, and there comes forth a spurt of blood, and from which it leaps downwards.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never in this vein have hands rained, even when it opens at the elbow or the wrist, and there comes forth a spurt of blood, and from which it leaps downwards.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	And never has this vein had hands rain, even when it opens at the elbow, or at the wrist, and there comes forth blood spurting; cure it as we have said before.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	And this disease is called in our land "buffalo disease," forasmuch as it often causes swelling of the calves, and is a small wound that arises between skin and bone, and goes throughout the body, upwards and downwards, and it causes pain all along the limb, until the skin is broken or it bursts, and spurts out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And is accompanied by the putrefaction of some humors, such as bile, serum, urine, and worms or belly-ache
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	And doubt arises from its malice, for when it goes through the body and reaches the head, it comes to the oil, by chance returns, and destroys the oil.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it heal and abate, if one cannot force it until it goes away:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then you must tightly bind the limb above and below with strong thread, and then hold above and push down, and if it does not go away, if you cauterize with fire above, until it dies
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greater harm it does is when it contaminates the oil, as we have said
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or near the oil, seize its tail and push down, then hold above, and force it out
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And it is recommended to use the patient for the evacuation of solid medicines which solve the bad humors carried, and to feed him with nourishing foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	When you see it cured and treated, if you cannot force it, do not force it until it goes: if you must, then bind the limb above and below with a strong ligature, and press above and below, and as it comes out, seize it by the hair and burn it with fire; and the greater harm it does is when it comes out with the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or close to the oil, grasp its lash and press, then press above and below; and you must use the patient of cooling down the body with medicines that dissolve harmful humors and eating nourishing foods.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and is a pain that comes in the limbs, and as it moves from limb to limb.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	I have seen this to be the case
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and found her arm swollen, and saw a small swelling in the pit of her elbow
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and I observed that it had become like a worm in the armpit, more swollen than anything, as if alive silver when it breaks from its root
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain went away from that limb, and settled in the armpit, and then later returned throughout the whole limb, until it reached the other arm
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then he told me that it twisted back towards the body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered how it managed to move from limb to limb, because I had never seen anyone with this disease before.</start_of_turn
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	However, I would rather keep silent than move with pain in a limb, but I do not wish to keep silent, as I saw her in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	And I thought that this was the reason why the woman had dry skin, and her veins uncovered, and because of that appeared that constraint of the wind;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And it does not appear to me according to this reason to those who are delicious, and who have moist skin and veins restored
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see that this disease is cured, and the patient feels that pain, if she shows you if as we have said, if the swelling above and below has vanished, and then rest until that constraint of the wind has disappeared from the limb
et cauterize le leu;	And cauterize the limb;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And if you do not see it at your eyes, if you cure it of what evacuates the wind, as with foul pills, and oily pills, and similar things.
des saiettes	When you see the healing of this ailment, and the patient feels that pain, if it tears open as we have said, if the flesh above and below has become swollen, and then hold above as much as this constraint of the limb is strong; and cauterize the limb; and if you do not see it at your eyes, if he cures what evacuates the constraint, as with foul pills, and pills of serpin, and similar others.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	If the doctor gives vent to these winds, if like foul pills, and pills of serpin, and like other things of that sort.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	When there is variety in their points, some large, some small, and some with hooks and nails;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those which have two angles, and those which have tongues, and those which have pieces
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and that which breaks in no limb breaks in two ways
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in the principal limb breaks, as with the brain, shoulder, forearm, hand, foot, rib, intestine, bladder, and similar members
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When the limb snaps, indeed in no part of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, will teach you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	When the limb snaps, indeed in no part of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, will teach you: if you are aware of the extraction of this arrow, for the corpse will follow afterwards in many positions.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, if the limb is fractured, and the wound is cured.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the brain when the arrow pierces the bone, and blood spurts from the socket which is above the brain, is like a scourging, swelling and turning inward, and redness in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasm and mixing of senses, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	And sometimes it is without cause, without any bruises or wounds.
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and sometimes it causes speechlessness and deafness;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and leaps from a moist wound that looks like boils, and in the leap just like burnt hair
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if you notice this sign, if you are to take care of it, draw out the splinter if it is not embedded
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the splinter when it hurts or aches is that it is close to the left nipple, and it feels just like if it were stuck in something hard, do not remove it freely
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and sometimes the splinter moves just like boils, and leaves black blood, and comes with cold sweat and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The wounds therefore signify doubt that the blood has drained away.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the dislocated shoulder that never lets go is when it jumps out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, and breathes high and quets the food away.</start_of_turn
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the sponge tears in the covering of the wound, if it is too small, leave the small bones;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	it gives great swelling and pain and breathing difficulty
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and the limb moves out of its place
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	If the spleen or stomach is broken, by chance if there is a jump from the wound, nothing of the indigestible meat is left.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	If the spleen or stomach is broken, and in the jump there is no stool from the large intestine, if there is no hope of recovery, do not attempt to extract the stone.</start_of_turn>
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	and if the sponge tears in the bladder, and the urine spurts out and comes out, the patient feels great pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	As for the other limb, if the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the armpit and the spine and the buttocks and the thigh and the foot and the limb mentioned above, are all in more or less the same condition.</start_of_turn
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I have already told you, because of that which you do.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	There is at home a sponge that fell or drooled in the root of the nail:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I grasped it, and it slipped from the other side of the ear, and it was healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And thus he took a dart that had fallen into the fat of the oil of olives, and the dart was whole, and did not reach anything except the tip towards the foot, and the dart was as long as an arc of a Turkish bow, all in all a foolish thing to do.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	he game was sound, and there was no bad accident to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And thus he took a dart from the throat to the groin, and the dart was an Arab dart at an ear
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I saw the barbers, and I deceived them as long as I could, and was sound with the groin
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And thus he took a dart at home, that was in the thigh or belly, and I thought he was going to die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	And then, if he does not recover within XXX days, if he does not mend his ways;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I shall then cut off his limb, burn out his entrails, break his bones, and cause him no further harm.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	If I see that there is a fracture of bone or a wound that has penetrated deeply,
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	I will leave the limb whole and permit him to return to his natural habits; I will find no rest in his works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	If another man has fractured his face and the wound is deep,
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	he will suffer great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	And he will groan in pain.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And she drew out an arrow at home of the prince the king, who was sitting crooked among the lice, and there was a swelling downwards on the right side.
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was fully withdrawn.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat her after she had been crooked for three days
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I find the wound very painful.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I saw her with great anxiety and did not feel well;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and there was pain and swelling in her right ear
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I put on her ear plaster with digestive medicine, so that it would not swell further
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and there appeared to me the head of the arrow
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I put the thumb and index finger in their places, closed the wound, and held the patient’s hand tight, until he felt the arrow go out of his body.
et il le me dist.	and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I put upon the wound a corrosive ointment with my hands, until it was thick, and held it, and felt the head of the arrow that was coming out of place at its root
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I aided the opening of the wound with that ointment, until the head of the arrow appeared to me visibly
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and it passed well three months, and then it grew so large that I put in the nails and held it apart with one hand and the other, and I could not bear it anymore.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Therefore, I will continue to try subtle and ingenious methods until I have firmly secured the dressings, as is done in the end of this chapter, until I have completed the treatment, and I will restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the physicians judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it therefore, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Or as you have said concerning the quality of the extraction of some arrows, if you apply your treatment to what I do not understand, for the books do not teach me everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but the learned masters know very well both great and small things, and concerning what is present and lacking, true that you will find nine works and a new instrument, following the sequence of the strange things that arise in this art
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that the arrows do not issue from members or are ficketed except in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by loosening from the limb or they enter, or by some other means.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which issues forth by itself is an arrow that has penetrated flesh, and it issues forth never more.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not issue forth now, if you leave it until the wound is complete, and rejoice in its issue;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	even if it is fixed in bone and cannot issue, if you leave it alone for a few days, and move it every day
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	then it will issue, and if it does not issue, if you pierce through all the surrounding parts, until the limb is swollen, and then take it away
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the splinter is fixed in the bone of the head, and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and no other accidents have occurred as I have mentioned to the patient.
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if I do not treat it, but leave it as it is, it will be equal after some days, for if the splinter comes up to the surface, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	If the hair is only caught in the bone and does not come up to the surface, and remains fixed in the bone for several days without any other mishap, do not force the drawing out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is firmly fixed and cannot be removed, if I give medicine, as I have told you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the limb while it is still sound
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the splinter is replaced in the bone if we cannot see it, if the patient tries in every way
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	If you feel it, if the pain has no palpable cause;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	if you do not find it by the swelling of the wound, or by the depth of the wound, and there is no bone, nerve or vein, if the pain lasts as long as the wound is great.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	if you pull out the splinter if you find it, and if there is cartilage in the splinter which is split into two parts at the bone that you pull, and then break or crush the cartilage of the splinter as much as you can pull it out
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	but take care not to break the splinter, only pull it out firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you do not do it once, if the limb is already swollen, then grasp it more firmly, for the extraction will be joyful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	and if bleeding prevents you, do what we have said in this chapter about the cure of it.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	Be wary of cutting into the nerve and the vein, and put them in such a way that you can easily draw out the arrow without danger, or to break or tear, or firmly or gently.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	Put the patient in the posture in which he was when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest aid of all, and if you do not know how, follow what he shows you
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another place, or there is no wound, or the skin is stretched at the place where it is seen or felt.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	Take hold until the bone can be grasped, and then remove it.
si saut fuer maintenant.	If the bone is fractured now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, if you twist your hand round and round, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then withdraw it.</start_of_turn
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be set, if you leave it in peace, and then resume the extraction until it is fractured again;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if it is of an arrow, it is, if it has struck completely;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	And if it is of an arrow, it is, if it has struck completely; and if you see an instrument hanging, if you administer it, let the point of the arrow enter the hole of the instrument.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	Then withdraw the force, and if the arrow is caught, let the instrument with the pointed end enter in order to ease the extraction.

et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And the treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the tweezers with which we treat the wounds is similar to the beak of an osprey, and thus is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways to do it

li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	For to stop the bleeding at the tip of the arrow, if this is the shape: the form of a clamp to stop and to hold if it is like this.
des voinnes dou cors communes	it is common for veins to bleed when they are opened or cut.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	From veins from which one has bled for a long time, for in this case there is either a head wound or a wound at the sixteenth, that is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two veins that are behind the ears, which are covered with coarse hair.

Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The common veins are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, which is on the left side of the chest, and they call it the "chief vein".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	And the marrow is called "fast," and is composed of the cephalic and basal parts, and they call it the common people "bone marrow.
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet. Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the collateral vein is the one that is between the ulnar and the annular, and if there are two of them;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the arm and the forearm there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is from the elbow of the left side of the armpit, and the second is the sural which is at the ankle of the right side

Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The blood of the veins that are behind the ears helps as old evacuations and has emigration.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	And the qualities of the blood, as I have told you, are that you raise the head of the patient and rub the limb or the veins are rough
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	Then tighten the patient's neck with a screw, as long as the two veins behind the ears appear behind the ears depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	So you must know that when you feel the pulse from behind your ears, it is a sign of strangulation;

Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The blood of the two arteries in the two temples is worth an ancient emigration, sode, and obtalmia accustomed, and at the root of the tears there are vesicles.

et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	As for what we have said about it in other books concerning its treatment and extraction, or its commencement in the book itself.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The blood of the front vein is as valuable as that of the cephalic vein, for it has ancient diseases of the face, emigration, and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And if the patient strains his neck by twisting, as the vein bursts.

Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and hold with your hand, or something else, and let blood flow out as much as you see fit;

de la sainie des leivres	The blood of the armpits helps in the swelling of the groin, in the beginning of mumps, and in many diseases, and in swelling, and in corrosions, and in herpes, and in stones; and the quality of the blood is that when the patient strains his neck alternately, as we have said; either the master is standing above the patient's head, and the patient sits on one seat, then grasps the vein long and widely, then pulls out the blood gently, or as much as is necessary; and then repeat the operation in the other vein, then release the thread, and strain moderately the middle veins, so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the upper limbs helps to clot in the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and fissures of the lips, and toothaches and pains.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And if the patient is able to sit before you, and you restrain his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	Then turn the face up, and look at two veins, one on the right cheek and the other on the left, and know them by their blackness, and by the fact that there are small black veins running alongside them
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Therefore take both of them, and if you do not know them, and if you are in doubt, if the larger one is at the back of the jaw, and both of the smaller ones below and beside, for this is a foolish way
de la sainie desoz la lengue	And if the quality of the blood is to make the patient sit before thee, and restrain his neck as I have said; then turn the liver, and look at two veins, one on the right side of the liver and the other on the left, and know them by this that they are black, and that they have small black veins running through them: so do one and the other; and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, if one of the largest parts of the spleen is pale, and both veins that are below and above are pale, for this is the same method.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The blood of the veins below the tongue helps after the cephalic blood, and this is at the widening of the throat, and with eye diseases, and with mouth diseases
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And if the patient is a healthy man, if he sits between your hands before the sun, and he sticks out his tongue, and looks downwards at every cost, he will see a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Then he will see both of them [the veins] together, and do not fear them too much, for these are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins which we commonly call healthy are commonly sick in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or when they are pricked by a sharp flame or olive oil as with a saw, and are called "aneurysm".

Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The flame of fire is soft if it is mild, and is broad as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And they have the master to open the superficial veins filled with large blood and containing great blood and trouble;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And thus is the form of the olive-tree flame:

Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	And thus is the form of the olive-tree flame: the sap of the basilisk, which is one of these veins, helps with ailments such as nausea of the throat, or cough, or pain in the belly;

La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thoughts.</start_of_turn>

et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And must not be restored more than twelve years, and women carrying for more than four months until the seventh month
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	One must not strengthen the ones who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when anyone sees that he has been healed in any way, if it is necessary, if there is a hernia of a lesser fistula, if there is much retained saliva, so that the veins do not draw out the nutritious humors from the principal limbs
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Neither must one keep oneself too fat with meat, nor drunk, when it is necessary, for there is need of it; neither must one be overly cold nor too hot
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And if one suffers from madness after a fierce passion, and vomiting, and belly distress, and many times of urination in women, and childbirth, and watching and lying down, and all that is good or bad;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then subtile the humors, if they are not great, by foods and drinks and medicines, if you can.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	Then bathe in cold or hot water, so that nothing hinders, to subtilize the blood, and restore from the vein to the third part, as we have said before
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And keep yourself from work, from worry, from luxury, and from similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	And bind and soothe, and keep the patient higher than the one who is caring for him, and wipe the hands twice or thrice, and then extract the thread slowly, because if it is too tight or loose, if cannot correct it without
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then he rubs the limb with his hands, until the veins swell, and one feels them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And then he moistens the skin with a little oil, then puts his thumb of his left hand on that vein below the limb a thumb’s breadth or as much as he wants to make it bleed.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flee just like strings to the wound, and if they are of such a kind that are filled with blood, so that when one puts on the flame, if one takes it away from the flame, it cannot open the vein, and that is what is often the result of this
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it is necessary to open the vein, if the wound is too wide, because of this one must be cautious so that the patient is warned about these things
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein bursts the first time, that is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If not, if it bursts again, even more so, one must hold the limb still or at least as much as possible, for if it is not done, the wound will not heal.</start_of_turn>
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	If the limb is swollen and the patient groans, and if one leaves it for a day or two, and does not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	then there will certainly be pus.</start_of_turn>
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not enter or bathe, then reset the blood if it clots;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the blood vessel is small, or if it is without support and you doubt that there is not as much blood as you see, if you are confident in the loss itself with all your might.</start_of_turn
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	And the work a little patient, even though his limbs are swollen.
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for often in this work, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the limb swollen, do not renew the bleeding, put on a little oil, for it softens the flesh of blood and makes it limp in this limb the oil that you put on it
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and give the oil to absorb the blood that comes out to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and this also makes the limb tremble and bow down when you put it on the limb.
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	if you do it carelessly and it comes out when it is too large
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens, even if it is not very serious except for this time or the opening of the vein is small, if you are in a hurry, put on the wet sponge and roll up a bandage, and bind for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And do this after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if it remains fixed afterwards for some days without any blackening or greening, do not trouble me with it.</start_of_turn>
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see it, put nothing of aloe or myrrh moistened in calamus juice, mustard, or the like.</start_of_turn>
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often happens an abscess and appearance of blood from the basilisk.</start_of_turn
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Put your hand on it, and if you find the limb soft under the compression of the hand, that is an evil sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Heed what we have said and do not place anything on it, for by chance in this way without an artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but it makes the limb swell dry to strengthen the limb, then treat it with another treatment, until it is healed
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	Treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.</start_of_turn
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if it is without color, if you leave it to its swelling as long as it is red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it big, if you leave it until it is faint
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too yellow, if you leave it cool.</start_of_turn>
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is expedient for the plains and strong person, and has the skill of extracting blood, to make the wound wider and the flame bigger.</start_of_turn>
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for the weakling, do the opposite; make him whole again quickly and often, and one must make him whole by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of healing is useful for the restoration of blood and the preservation of nerves, and is better than if the blood were long rather than wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for the one whose limb needs blood, it is recommended to give soft bread soaked in pomegranate juice
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	if he is pale, if there is three or four times more blood; and if he has a cold complexion, let him beforehand eat soft bread soaked in sweet syrup or honey with spices, as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If he pricks at the blood vessels after the evacuation of blood, it is necessary to know that he will spit frothy bile, an odoriferous sweat, and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter of syncope for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he sees his arm turn pale, and recovers again, if it is known, when he is filled with great blood, that he must rise up and rise up again, according to the quantity of his continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever has seen his arm swollen after the first bleeding, and has great pain, if he stays like this for three days after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever has seen himself recover from the other side, if he must recover by the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For there is much blood in the limb that is already pale, and it causes fever.
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	if it is necessary to manage a great quantity, and to widen the opening as much as it bleeds in the palm of the hand.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then you must restore all the blood vessels and put your hand over the wound while it is still bleeding in the palm of the hand, for many times the blood escapes when the vessel is neglected
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and do not hesitate to pull out the limb if you see it slipping again, and close the wound, pressing firmly over it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	if it is crooked, extend the limb as much as possible, for that would be bad
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	leave it until it is healed again
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you put on the tip of the flame, until the blood vessel that is frozen at the opening of the vein comes out, and put on some water above it and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has escaped, if you leave it and do not restrain me, as long as the incision is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary is to drain blood a second time, if the same in this limb or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is stained in leu of the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And if the patient’s hand is plunged into hot water, as long as the flesh is red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it should be firmly bound so that the wound opens well, and that the limb is neither too wide nor too long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and if it cannot be closed, let the wound be large and close to the joint of the hand, and if it does not heal, plunge the hand into hot water again and leave the blood to clot in the water until enough time has passed
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	otherwise do not reinsert the hand into the hot water, for we put more in danger than in this state;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	The blood of this vein is more valuable than all the others, for there is neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The saliva from the right hand is worth for all the diseases of the liver, and this is the manner:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	The saliva from the right hand is worth for all the diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: strain the hand and bathe it in warm water, until the swelling has gone down, if you see it
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	The saliva from the right hand is worth for all the diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: strain the hand and bathe it in warm water, until the swelling has gone down, if you see it all the way through, and if you handle it carefully, it will not grieve anything.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Do not handle it too much, for the nerves are already loosened from their sheath, and then reset the hand in warm water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and do not attempt to move it.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary with the cautery, if you put oil and lint on the wound to close it, do so carefully.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood in the left hand is worth the disease of mice, and do the same as I have said before for the upper part.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The blood of the armpit is worth for all diseases that are in the chest, as with diseases of the marrow, retention of flowers, disease of the reins, and of the calves and the ancient legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of its saliva is that if the patient has been soaked in warm water, and has rubbed on the swelling until it has gone down, and has placed a bandage over the joint of the limb.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And if the vein is at the ankle, and below it there are loose threads of hair in the vicinity, there will be a discharge of blood.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	healthy or bloody discharge, or at the ankle, that much blood flows out.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you see blood on the hair near the nail, protect the nerves that are below, and drain just as if you were grasping;
et soit li flaimes anesil.	or the fire is extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot be kept in place, if you reset the bone in water, and let the vein drain well.</start_of_turn
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the blood vessel must be reset the first time, if you do it again later, because the blood vessel is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt the nerves, as we have said, and do the same with the other nail equally
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The pulse of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle of fire, and its blood is worth the pain of the groin, when it is for blood that is hot.</start_of_turn>
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	When the patient is between or in water, and pulls below the ankle twice in twisting, because otherwise the vein will not open;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	And if she [the wound] opens, if the same in all ways that you can, and through and through.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	it is better that you close it, for the wound is deep and it is likely to burst again at home.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not manage it, if the same does not bleed from its opening or its depth, and toward the little toe, and guard against nerves.</start_of_turn
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and make so much pressure on the blood that you see, and then loosen the knot, and put on cotton and bind.</start_of_turn
ele est maintenant sanee.	it is now healed.</start_of_turn>
des sainies de ventouse	of bloodletting
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Bandages are made of horn, or cobwebs, or wool.</start_of_turn
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	And if the dressing is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Or by cutting and drawing out blood, or by cutting only.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this bleeding which is done by cutting if it is done in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	Or it is very hot, or it is done with heat;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	And the bleeding which is done by cutting and by drawing out blood if it is done in twelve days of pain, for in that case one is all at the head of the sufferer.
et li autres est emmi le col;	And the other is at the collarbone;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	And two others in two ribs of the collarbone;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And the patient should suck on a ventouse to loosen the wind from the belly.
et li ventouse des II espaules;	And the patient should suck on a ventouse twice to loosen the wind from the belly
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the patient should suck on a ventouse over the crupies
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	And the patient should suck on the ventouse at both arms together
et les ventouses des II jambes;	And the patient should suck on the ventouse at both legs together
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	And the patient should suck on the ventouse at both ankles together
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And the vomiting does not help in any way, for there are many veins that are scattered throughout the body, and for this reason it does not do any good to vomit, as if we were draining blood from a vein
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	It is only useful to vomit when it comes from repletion, without any fire or sensation of fire, in no disease that comes from eating, until all the food is emptied from the stomach
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if necessity or custom demands it, if the physician must give a sneeze at the beginning or at the end of a month, or at any time, and must do so with every yawn and sigh.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are those who, when they must sneeze, feel a heavy head.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are those who experience swelling and redness in their face, head, neck, and eyes
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who have a discharge of blood in their mouth, and have lost their tongue, and are spitting blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and those who think, and see nothing but blood and fear and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	When these signs appear, and even if it is only lightly moist, we command the patient to wind after two hours.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	Blood from the vein helps to relieve the pain in the head … which comes from the eyes, and it is not permitted to do anything else before evacuating all the pus
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And if this vomiting is in lieu of the blood of the cephalic vein, it does not suffice only those who are of cold complexion in use, or who have a dullness, for this can cause great discomfort.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And for this reason it does not suffice only those who are of cold temperament in use, but those who have or suffer from chief colds illnesses.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And for this reason I advise you not to use it on patients suffering from cold or severe diseases
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	Vomiting in the collar is in lieu of the blood of the chief and the basal veins, and for this reason it is worth at the greatest extent to the point of pain in the chest, and to swelling of the channel of the windpipe, and all that is similar to this.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	It is not to be forced too much, for if it stays too firmly, it can cause an obstruction of the belly or the stomach or the bowels.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The winds blow as two ribs of the collar cause pains of the head, and swelling and inflammation, and constriction, and pain at the root of the teeth, and is in lieu of the blood of the vein.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And you must command the patient to express his hand to put it in, that he does not cut the artery, and does not bleed excessively.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The vomiting of these days is like a disease of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	And is in lieu of the blood of the two livers.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds of the spleen are harmful to health, coming from heat and congestion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The vomiting of the belly is as much as three veins of the arm, because it draws blood from these three veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And instruct the patient not to fear too much pain, for the blood is thick and knows the bones and nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The swelling that is on the buttocks is worth as much as blood clot at the foundation, and has diseases of bones, and it is recommended that the swelling be large and of hair, that it has to be well treated.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	And by chance, if it should be subtle, if it breaks;
et i fai grans plaies.	it makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The swellings of the legs swell open, because they draw blood from all over the body, and cause as much pain as the ancient rains, and the marrow, and the bladder, and restore the flowers
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and are in place of the two shoulders, and the two knees, and all of them weaken the body after a long time, and cause death in many positions
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The manner of applying the ventouse is as follows: if you apply it at first sight, and with immediate effect, and put it on firmly, and move it evenly, and do not cease doing so until you see blood flowing freely and bloodstained, and open the wound.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then be quick, and remove the ventouse, and take care of the body, for there are some who have sustained severe pain and opened wounds:
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	if it is necessary to wound only once, and to make large wounds, and a deep wound;
et suce legierement.	and do so gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if it is not too big, if you can wound twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time in order to narrow the large wound
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if it is not very thick, if you must wound it for the third time.
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when our veins swell with blood, too much, too little, if we must puncture it once more.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	and when our veins burst with blood, if we must repeat this treatment often;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if it is not very thick, if you must wound it for the third time; if you perceive that the wound has become perceptible, and it is for those who have thick skin and tough nails, and who have swollen pores, that you must apply liniment of essential oils which are aperitif and dissolving:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in this state, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	If it is in the armpit, with oil of cresson, or of poppy seed, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is large and cold, if you take amaranth oil, or balsam oil, or rue oil, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	If he has a tender pulse and large pores, one must not put oil on, but it is necessary to wash afterwards with rose water, or cold water, or lime water, or pumpkin seed water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if there is moisture in the mouth, if it lifts easily, or with vinegar of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.</start_of_turn>
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And if there are yellow spots, they rise from old wine, or from sea water, or from a decoction of elderberry or chamomile, or from other similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	Do not put on a suction cup in front of the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	Do not sleep after the suction, but keep warm when you must suctor and when you are sucturing.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And take care that the one who is being suctioned is not feverish, and that he is not too rough or inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	If he grasps cold things, such as pomegranates, grapes, onions, and lettuce at ease, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and mixes herbs, mustard, and fat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, if he grasps honey syrup, and fragrant wine which is between autumn and summer, and broth, and herbs and small oils and marjoram;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and when he has a cold wind, he must drink more than eat
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and must give to others homes never three times in a row before or after, because of the ventilation, or for comfort of the main parts;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	or be silent about it, but do not say it unless the cold ones drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The wounds which are made to be cauterized are those which are made upon the liver, and upon the spleen, and under the kidney, and upon the belly and the buttock and the groin and the heel, for in no limb does the fire cause any wound except to draw blood from limb to limb, as we do when we put on the cautery to the nipples when they are bleeding.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	in order to reduce the viscosity which is in the limb, as we do when we make incisions on the belly and the buttock to lighten the limb.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and to stop the pain, when there is swelling or fracture, if by its attractive virtue it pulls out the swelling, or evacuates the fracture from its place
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and in this way when it is put on the liver and the spleen when there is retained moisture, these incisions are administered empty in order to suck up so little
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	Neither fire nor water is ever administered together, and neither is it ever plain water that is used for these diseases; for in such cases we fill the sponge with hot water, or water alone, or we add herbs that are conducive to this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the wound administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And there must be two broad and half palms of butter, and there must be oil or cost oil at the bottom of the mileu, as for extracting an awl, and whether it be hair or wool in front so that it does not burn the patient when putting it on the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And there must be in the mileu a rod of barley or iron, to put a bandage in, and there must be both large and small according to the diseases and the extent of these which take them
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the wounds of the veins are different from those of meats, and fats from bones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And must one place this ventouse upon the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	And must one place this ventouse upon the limb: grasp the sleeve of silk or linen and put it between the ventouse and the limb, so that it closes either at the bottom of the ventouse or that it does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it upon the limb, and you must either place it upon the opening that we have mentioned, so that when we see that there is vapor, and the bone is loosened, we can remove the ventouse.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and grasp the lining as before, and repeat it often, if you are skillful.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the ventouse, which is administered in cases of pneumonia, at all severity, there is no opening or hole, and it is only administered when it is clear of inflammation, and is placed upon the limb only slightly
et c’est li forme:	And thus it is that form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	The wounds do not yield until they are treated in limbs or where it is impossible to apply a bandage due to their smallness, as with books and gums, and similar things.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	And in such things as flesh stripped of hair, if it is desired or not, and other similar things;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the sufferer is that when you find wounds that are in soft and delicate tissues without sensation of pain, if you touch them, they bleed
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in hot water, until they are soft, and do not have any pain in their bellies
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then either drain the vein and apply a bandage, then rub the limb until it is red, and apply the wound
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	When they are even and smooth, and shine, if it is bone or we can put on a suction cup, put it on, for it is worth more afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, if you lift the bone easily, then slightly with water, move it well, and then release it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if it remains too much afterwards, wet the edges with cold water, and put on, until the wound is closed
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the wound is multiplied, put on crushed glass or fragments of tile, and similar things, until it is closed.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you remove half of the burnt bones, and leave them until they are consumed by the bone, if it stops now.
