et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If you have more pain, take other medicines.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	If the medicines do not suffice, rub the limb with fresh blood, or insert a needle into it until blood flows, and then withdraw the needle.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	When you see that it is bleeding, sprinkle some alum or bruised herbs or ashes on it, and it will stop now.</start_of_turn>
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the end of the text.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is restoration of fracture and displacement.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Beware, dear son, that in this book, you will not find anything that the ancient books do not contain, no letter or writing.</start_of_turn>
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason it is strange in our land, for I have never found it elsewhere.</start_of_turn
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know of nothing, except by the science of ancient books, or because I have studied it so thoroughly that I have mastered the science, and by experiment, and by the habit of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	And I have described in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have abbreviated at the end, and I have made it clear the forms of the instruments which are mentioned, as I have done in the two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, I say that the prologue of this book and the chapters contain the essence of the word and that the learned man who reads and comprehends them will find true understanding, for those who have been proven to be skilled in this noble art and have learned it well.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twist or sprain occurs, if you can, you must hasten the healing of the patient from one side and the other, if nothing else hinders you, if there is weakness of the limb, or immaturity, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the tension is not very strong, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	And eat cold juices, such as broth and ale, and do not drink wine, do not eat greasy foods, and do not eat too much meat that fills the veins of blood, until you have no doubt of the post-cautery, or of the swelling of the limb.
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if he returns to his senses at the first moment, take governance as he used to.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to restore, if you must know that you must nourish the patient with foods that make great nourishment, or that have viscosity, such as barley cooked in broth, peas, and beans, fish, eggs, cheese, and fat, and similar things.</start_of_turn>
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at a part of nourishment, rest returns muscle and more easily breaks the fracture.</start_of_turn>
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that bones that are fractured of splintered do not mend well together, neither do they knit according to their nature because of the drying out of the limb, nor those that are too tender, as bones of small children
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but there is no remedy, rest on the fractured bone that is large and firm which is found and joins the limb together, as long as it remains firm as it was before
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And do not eat anything from its source, and for this reason we advise nourishing of coarse foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are of various kinds in many ways.</start_of_turn>
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the skull is different from that of the limb, or of the bone, and I shall tell you in this chapter all the ways of fracture.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go only skin-deep, and others by cutting, like the size of a needle to write with.</start_of_turn>
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small tear.</start_of_turn
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And if there is any reason that has its own instrument and its own method in restoring, according to what is remembered to come into its place
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and is known to break bones by this that it leaps up well by pushing and by the pressure of the hand
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no swelling or pain, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no break
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have swelling or fracture or small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you do not know with certainty whether it is twisted or broken, but only that the hand is moved, but put on medicines that will come afterwards, and then strain it now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And the veins that break that go into the marrow, and are the two parts of the joint, it is necessary to put them in place equally, even as after the abscesses have gone away
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if a boil comes out with a burst, do not leave any hair, until the boil is calmed;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then put it equal to the muscle that you must grasp firmly and steadily, and hair that the healing is more gentle than the healing of this or that there are pieces.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then hold it, as it should be after that
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there are broken bones, if they extend from two parts, if it is hands or feet, or at your hand if it is a small limb, or at two strings, or at a string and at your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the limb in its natural position, so that when the parts of the limb break, if they are dislocated, remember by all means to keep the addition to the bone at the muscle that you must grasp, and keep that by your work no wound or pain comes to the patient
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And hold the arms firmly by the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And he should feel well in the hand if it seems that it is not well:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if it is twisted well, and do not constrain it too much, do not press as those who do who cause it to come out at the incision and contraction of the limb as we have often seen
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	When the limb is at a point, if the patient feels well that it does not move, do not watch or sleep or turn or move in any way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and keep the limb so secure that he does not feel any pain
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he does not feel any pain, if it is not at a point, and you can put it in partial disposal that he does not feel any pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And keep it properly aligned, so that no twisting arises when you restore it.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the quality of the limb is as I have told you
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The fractures of the limb are diverse in small and large size and in shape.</start_of_turn>
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs like arms and feet and the like:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	it is necessary to cover them with soft and fine linen cloths
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	those which are large, like thighs and legs
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	it is necessary to cover them with a wide and strong thread, for the large threads embrace the whole large limb and constrain it evenly, so that there is no tension;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then take hold of the limb firmly, three turns or four according to the size of the limb, and grasp the hand one hand at the top of the break and strain less, so that the break slips a little bit;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And soften the limb a little more, both front and back, as much as you grasp a large part of the limb still sound, then take hold of the limb once more, and turn the dislocation back to its proper position.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then raise up the lower part of the break, and hold it moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we mentioned before
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then put between the broken bones some flaxseed or bandages, so that they are all even, and then bind them up above with a bandage, and put on your crutches well made above, if there is no abscess or swelling
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, put on something soothing to the abscess, which will soften the swelling, and leave it untouched for a few days
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then strain upon your thumbs, and let them be half the length of a broad cane resting firmly, or of the kind made from sticks, or of barley straws, and let them be as follows:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the thumb which you put on the fracture be thicker and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	And be as long as it is necessary for the little finger or the great toe
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then strain upon the thumbs as you did before, and then bind them with a thread conveniently, as you did in the first instance on the fracture
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	The closer it is bound, the less.
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	And let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, and be of hemp.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the thread is thick, as I would like works of fools who make their knots like twisted linen threads, this is a great error, for the knot will not be even if it is too subtle, and it will hold only if there is between the thumb and the index finger some space.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is scorched by the nails after the stretching of the limbs, if you put on stockings of linen or coarse cloth, so that it does not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a splinter, and the bone is fractured, I will tell the cure of that later.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And the wounds which he cannot restrain must be stripped off from these bones to break them first in order.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For if the limb is large, I will not put in stitches until after five or seven days, or more according to the severity of the wound coming out;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and thus the manner of old bandaging to restore a fracture, dislocation, and torsion:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and take flour that is held in the walls of the mill, and mix it with an abundance of eggs, and make this confection, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it. This is the common manner of bandaging that restores the fracture in various positions, and even for women and young children, because it is neither too tight nor too loose
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Other methods of treatment restore fracture, dislocation and torsion.
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Other methods of treatment restore fracture, dislocation and torsion: barley, lentil, alum, saffron, Arabic gum, mugwort, and vinegar in the amount of X times three.</start_of_turn>
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Myrrh and aloe, in the amount of five times three.</start_of_turn
alechil VIIII З.;	Mustard seed seven times three.</start_of_turn
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	And make a powder of them, and mix them with egg white.</start_of_turn
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the complexion of the patient is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth more than many homes.</start_of_turn>
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Other methods of plastering that are worth for torsion.</start_of_turn>
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	Take mugwort and vinegar, at ten parts; and aloes and salt, at seven parts.
acaice VI З.;	Juniper berries six parts
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Juniper berries ten parts, and grind them well, and mix with water or egg yolk, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another method of treating joints and bones that have become loosened from their sockets, and relieves pain, and strengthens bones, and breaks down swelling:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take fresh linen, and moisten it with oil and broth, and put it on the wound
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These treatments do not restore health, but are good for relieving post-cautery pain, and bones properly relieve the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another method of treating bones that have been fractured
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Pren feuille de figuier sèches, et feuille de pavol terrestre, et broie ensemblé, et fais emplaustre.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of treating is to restore the fracture of the bone and to diminish the remaining post-cautery swelling.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take dry fig tree leaves and terrestrial chamomile leaves, grind them together, and make plaster.
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Grind them, mix with wine, and if the limb is swollen, soak it with moist coriander water or water, and use it
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Other methods of restoring the limb are more forceful than the first, when an abscess hardens during restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take root of vismalve, linseed seed, marshmallow, quince seed, violets and chamomile flowers, of each kind an equal part
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Grind them, mix with salt water or sweet water or wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras in his book does not put anything on the broken limb to restore it except for some wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between two things not too soft not too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen recommends placing something dry and warm upon the affected limb to restore it, such as myrrh, aloes, incense and the like, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Other means of immobilizing that is worth for lesions and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Other means of immobilizing that is worth for lesions and pain: take mugwort and chopped onions, or poppy seeds, and beeswax, mix them evenly, and grind them up, and make plaster of it and bind it tightly.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then loosen a little afterwards, and take care that the patient feels no pain, that the bones are not fractured in their place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	otherwise loosen by hand day and night.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	If pain comes to the limb, or swelling, rest or move slowly; if you delay, and loosen it, and bind it up again immediately
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	put on a lighter drape, and a wet sponge of sea salt, and immerse in water, and elevate the limb until the swelling ceases and the pain is relieved;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, soak in water or oil rose, and bind up with a knot, until you are sure of the afterburn of the cautery.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	And rest the inflamed limb, and if it swells, then begin the ligation again, and a little displacement, and do not strain it more than necessary;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that the abscess is inflamed, swollen, red, and painful, and that it returns again after you have placed it and bound it, as you did the first time, then you must repeat the procedure.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if no improvement appears in the limb for what we have said, if you must remove the dressing after three days or four, or five or seven;
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	Never leave it for twenty days, according to what we see, until the wound has healed, and approach the joint slowly over the wound
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	When he has received more restraint than before, and engrosses his flesh, as I have said before.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see that his limb is drying out more than usual, do not permit that nourishment should come from nourishment alone;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	it is necessary to give him warm water, every time you loosen it, and this every third hour, and cut a vein every fourth hour
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	for in this work, indeed, nourish the limb well and quickly restore what the fools make fall, that restore the limb violently
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	it is wrong, and if it is urgent, and I see nothing else but to leave it and do it violently.
des diverses manieres de brisure	from various breaks
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many ways of breaks are, and various figures, and the causes are diverse;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	For there are fractures that are made by percussion of a spear, and the collarbone is broken all the way up to the syphus which is the socket of the bone, as if made by a saw or an axe.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for this reason this kind of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Or the spear pierces the bone from the inside outwards, and is called this kind of fracture "absolue".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	And there is the wound of these two fractures, great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is embedded percussion, or fissure or split of the bone, or dislocation of the shoulder or fracture of the bone, or other similar things.</start_of_turn
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a burst vessel, which approaches the gut that is adjacent to the bone, or it is on the bone, this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is sutured in the bone as subtly as a hair, and the split is small, and for this reason this is called a "capillary" fracture
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound is made or by cutting with a knife, or by a thorn, or by something similar, and it causes the piece of bone to enter the hollow, and the limb is bent like the cauldron when it boils
si entre li piere dedens.	If between the teeth.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this often happens under those who have or chew moist bones, like children's teeth;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and often results from bites of various kinds that split into small pieces like stars;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	I will speak of it later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know of all the ways of breaking due to the subtraction above them, the inquiry into tentatives, and the corrupted flesh which is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary appearance is known by that which when we have discovered the bone, and we wipe on it, if there appears a black break.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take care of the patient’s condition, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, extension, and swelling, and fever, and the eyes to become pale and flushed, and other similar things in various situations, if you cannot do otherwise
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you do not see an imminent mishap, and you hope for health, if so, commence the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When you come to the aid first, and it is in sweat, if so, it is necessary to obstruct the bone before the fourteenth day over the muscle that you must support.</start_of_turn>
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	If it is in this state, if you haste to obstruct the bone before the seventh day over which the cloth of the bone is corrupted, then comes the accident that we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone comes up to the skin that covers the brain, you must cut off the fractured part immediately
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and take hold of the patient’s head and uncover the bone thoroughly in every way possible, and if blood comes out from uncovering the bone, or from a wound, use what is necessary and soak the wound with oily cloths
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	And keep the wound closed until the swelling subsides, and be sure to drain blood;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	Then begin to set the bone in place, and this is done in two ways:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	The first method if the fracture is close in front, and this is the shape
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then there is another fracture more extensive than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	The second method if there are several different sizes, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed and iron-like
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And gently support it, that you do not bruise the head
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is tough and hard, if you must pierce to set it, even though you administer splints, do not pierce through the bone beyond the test, and should have under the point a margin or circle, that does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	And you must know that many die if the scapulae come into the place of the bone ends, if you have filled them up to the test.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And that is the form of three ways of testing.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality by which to perceive the broken bone is that you place one finger on the bone and press two until you are certain that the bone is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then put the finger back in another place a little later, and do everything around, and close the gap between the fragments of the bone as skillfully as possible, and gently, as we have said, until you have brought the bone to your hand, or to any instruments that you may have like tenailles, pins or sutures
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	Leave the brain and the jaw untouched.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have grasped the bone firmly, and treated, if it is possible, restore the fragment that is loosened from the bone to all other instruments resembling an incisor, but it must be more tense and slender than the others.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	And if it loosens no small bones, no nails, if the bones rest lightly on other instruments;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	Then treat the wound with sutures and bandages as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And another method of work is like the Galicians do, which is more common.
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the voice is very strong, and that is its word
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a portion of the bone, either where it is fractured or broken, so that when you have uncovered that part, put on gloves and grasp the handle of this incisor lens, for this is its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side, but from the middle of two ribs, so that the cut reaches the bone.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then hold a little mallet above, so that you can easily break the bone and take care of the clot that is below;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is close to the bone, if you break it slightly, because we must break it properly without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if a bone breaks without piercing the skin, it is only slightly fractured from above; there are small pieces [of bone] which, if necessary, can be removed with a rasp of various sizes, to bring about the greatest possible healing, according to the work and the nature of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If there is a great deal of razing beforehand, and after that more subtly, and it does not cease to do so until it is well done.</start_of_turn>
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In these other small cuts and breaks, you must bring the cause according to its place;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this is something that is not reported by him who has studied in this art
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	and if the scab is discovered, you must take one bandage of linen, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and put it on the wound
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	Then take another bandage doubled in two or three, and wet it in wine and rose oil, and put it on the first bandage.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and make it lighter than you would like, so as not to press too hard on the surface, then give him another linen, and do not tighten it more than is necessary to hold the wound in place only.</start_of_turn>
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and leave it for an hour or two, until the swelling of the wound has subsided, then remove it, and give him medicines such as elderberry root, oatmeal, and incense powder, and an astringent; and similar things.</start_of_turn
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and grind these things into a powder, and put it on the wound, and give him other medicines as before, with a bite.</start_of_turn>
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	And keep that the wound is perfectly closed, neither leaving it open nor letting it gather pus, for when pus gathers on the brain membrane, if it breaks and bursts, it causes great harm to the patient.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when one puts on the side of the jaw any biting thing, if it does not desist downwards.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Beware then, if no other misfortune befalls the patient, as we have said, if there is any doubt or suspicion.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if the swelling does not go away except by the medicine that we have put on, if it has strength, if you can take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and one drape of gum, and put it on the jaw;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then you must manage the healing in the way that is necessary, as long as he is well.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Never break the two parts of the nose, or one of them only, for these are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	And thus the cartilage is brittle, and does not break easily, unless it is forced to bend or twist, and then it is whole again.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of these two parts is broken, if you drink a little wine or open the wound, and put the broken piece back into your index finger and the palm by forcing, until it returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	Do it gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the fracture is in the upper part of the limb and cannot be brought down naturally, as is often the case, you must assume that the limb is fractured at the root of the bone like the head of a club.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is of two parts, do it again, and hurry to restore the first joint if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the inflammation of the wound has subsided, then bind up the wound at the head of the bone, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you bite at another part, if it breaks there;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bite at another part, if it breaks there, and the teeth are so wide that they fill the holes of the gums.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no restorer should mill the tents in the burrow, and die every other day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	I do not think it is good, but it is right that they should be soft in confection of egg yolk and flour dust
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	Then leave the tooth until the bone is firm, and the cartilages hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And never put goose feathers or pins in place of teeth, and if there is sulfur cloth around, and it is held by the break, and blows on the patient among;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or make him do what you see
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	If blood clots come to the surface while you are working, if you put some lint or gauze soaked in rose oil, or some alum, on it.</start_of_turn
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the afterbirth does not come, if you put on plaster by default, of oatmeal flour and incense powder, confirmed with egg yolk, then put on light covers, and do not bind me more
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the bone of the limb breaks but is only slightly fractured, and is broken into small pieces, if you have suitable instruments for this, then extract the fragments, close the wound, and treat the surrounding tissues with oil and poultices.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no visible wound on the limb, if you treat the pain, and apply ointment, as long as it is necessary.</start_of_turn>
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the root of the mandible.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is fractured without any wound, and there is no fracture displacement, and the fracture is not displaced too much, except for the curvature inwards, if one knows it lightly
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is proper, if the fracture is in the lower part, that you bite your thumb of the affected limb in the patient’s mouth.</start_of_turn
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	And if the fracture is in the left mandible, if you hold your right thumb of the right hand, and hold the fracture lightly, and support it with the other hand in front, and make it even.</start_of_turn
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is displaced in .ij., if you must administer extension of .ij. parts, as long as they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if movement of the teeth comes, or swelling, if strained by a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put on the broken jaw cerate and put on a double drape.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And put on a great sponge well made, or a piece of leather equal in size, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it on to the bone that you put in, and command the patient to rest, and eat soft food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the figure is changing, if the pulp comes loose at the third joint, and then reset it to its place.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	And put on plaster, with powder of almonds with abundance of eggs or flour of linseed, after that you have put on the cerate.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	And put upon the wound a linen bandage, and if it bursts open, and the patient remains quiet, leave it as it is until it heals;
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Often it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if postmortem comes, if it is as we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a break and wound together, repair it so that no part of the bone remains exposed;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if the bone is slightly bent, cover it with covering instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, if it has flared up as required.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have boned all these fragments, and there is no more displacement, if the wound is wide, put on appropriate dressings to protect the wound, as long as it is necessary.</start_of_turn>
de la forcele	because of force.</start_of_turn
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The forcele breaks several times in front of the shoulder, towards the armpit, and the fracture is in three positions:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	or it is fractured and broken in two places, and there are fragments, and it is the lightest to restore
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	Or there is a break with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	When there is a break with a wound, if there are two attendants, one should hold the limb that feels the force of the break.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the head towards the part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	Then set the break even, so that its formation is as it should be, and there is neither swelling nor bruising
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	If you must extend further, put a round ball of lead or lint on the patient’s shoulder, and make it large as needed;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And extend and hold the force with your hand, so that you can make the break even as it should be
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you do not manage to push back the head of the shoulder, because it comes out of its socket, you must know that the patient lies groaning on his belly, and put a cushion under the shoulder blade, that is, the middle rib, and support the shoulder from below, until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then address the fracture to your shoulder, and if you find debris there, if you can, make an incision above.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and draw out the fragments lightly, and if the bone cannot reunite by any means, if the pulp has gone from one of the incisors that you have done;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but put the forceps in place, for to hold the tissue in place.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and appear like a spoon, and is not at all curved, and be as wide as it can be, according to the size of the bone and the extent of the work;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and there are two holes, as you see, and one is large and the other is small, as is the fracture of the wound that you made when you treated the bone.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are certain of the depth of the wound, if the wound is small, or if you doubt the depth, if you employ the dressing and bandage, as much as is necessary.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	If there is moisture in the wound, if it is oily, apply cloths soaked in rose oil and balsam, and wine, and put on top.</start_of_turn>
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The stiffness of the bone, when it is painful and swollen, is that you put on the bone the plaster of fine powder and egg yolk, and put on soft dressings above, and put a sponge below the socket if you need it.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very broad bandage of a palm of good size, then put on two layers of dressing and plaster it on
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a staple of about three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the head of the bandage is resting on the edge.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	And place the heel on the trochanter, and turn the bandle on the collar, and drain the right hip, and drain the left hip.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And retain the thigh part, and when you see that the ligament holds the trochanter in place, and you clearly see that the heel does not move from the greater trochanter, if you rewarm the thigh again, and when the thigh is released;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	And make the patient lie on his back, and put under his buttock a little cushion to lift the shoulder up.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	if you align the fracture of the scapula with the alignment of the shoulder, or if you bind the arm to the collar, and do not release it until it is well healed, for up to 20 days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	Then resume the support, if you see that it has shifted, hold and leave it as it is until it is restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored in eight days, and in less than a fortnight.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Then resume the displacement, if you see that it is necessary, and hold and leave it in place until it is restored; and it is usually restored in about 26 days, and less in most homes.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	There is no break or wide displacement of the bone, and only by force can it be moved;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if it appears according to the figure of the fracture, and is repositioned according to its natural form, in all the ways that you can
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then put out the limb powder with millstone with abundance of egg white, and bandage lightly, and put on a double dressing
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then put on a broad and soft cushion, a cushion wider than the shoulder, and when the cushion is set, do not let it rest on any part of the shoulder, if you use this braid of hemp, so that the cushion rests evenly
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then the stretching at the whole great bend firmly, so that the limb does not move from its place, and look at the mark of each joint.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And every time that it quivers, if the stretching is made, and makes the limb equal to its place if it has gone out of its place, and lies the patient upon his chest;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the dislocation is restored in twenty days or in twenty-five.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number is completed, if the limb is loosened, and the pain and swelling have subsided, because it is not a bone that has moved too easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone bends forward, and not a little, if it persists, and the bone, do as we said at the bursting of the forceps to calm the abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	And if a piece of the bone bends forward, and not a little, if it persists, and the bone, do as we said at the bursting of the forceps to calm the abscess.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The limb is never broken in a thousand, but this is often the case.
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks suddenly.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	When it is broken in the middle, if it declines downwards, and causes the patient great pain, and there is no marrow, and swelling, and by chance vomiting blood, and opens the marrow cavity in the broken bone, and all this is felt.</start_of_turn>
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And if the patient lies prone on his back, put a cushion between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulder blades together, and unite the edges of the two ribs with your hands, and slightly force them into place until the bone is set as it should be.
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Then place on the wound dressings and stamp below the tip of the collarbone, or some other soft substance, and cover with a bandage, and bind over the bone break, so that it does not move.
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and twist the limb round at the back, and hold it firmly, and give it time for the swelling to subside, and if it relaxes, do it again
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it comes loose, by corrosion or by inflammation that comes from within, or pain or swelling, if you are hasty, do not delay, loosen the wound and scrape away the pus, and address the cause of the trouble
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then restrain the shoulder and hold it steady until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of bones
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	The wounds that break the ribs only come forward in the buttocks and at the head of the thigh, and do not protrude except because they are slimy;
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and he feels well at the interrogation as two should.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	The restoration is when you put the fracture back in its place as it should be.</start_of_turn
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put on the dressing and bind it with an elastic bandage if necessary.</start_of_turn
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	If the ribs break downwards, if he feels great pain and itching, like with pleurisy, for the bone is touching the gut
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and the limbs are pale, vomiting and spitting up large amounts of blood, which is a grievous disease, and the old men have put great effort into it
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if any of those who say it should administer food that swells the belly, to push back the pangs of hunger.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, for after these things have been eaten, they do not go away unless they have already begun.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have already begun, if they are well.</start_of_turn>
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	They say that no one has ever seen a wound there without causing harm, for it seems to be the reason;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	All that remains is doubt that the vacuum does not pull out the superfluous matters at once by the arrangement of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that on must not cover the limb with coarse linen soaked in oil, but put on bandages between the ribs to measure an even inch of the circumference, then either cure with the cure for pleurisin, meat and medicine.
