et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then one must break the bone again, and treat it lightly, and then suture the two layers of the wound, if it is large, and bandage it, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if there is pus coming from the wound, put on damp cloths soaked in rose oil, and put on the limb.</start_of_turn
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cure while the limb of that which you must incision, and be without any surplus on the coast, or it must, as long as it is sane.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the collarbone.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	There is never wanting to break a bone of the collarbone, and indeed it happens that it rains;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	And also at the spine of the back
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	If this happens to anyone, and you know whether it will heal or not, take care if you see his hands softened and limp and dead, and do not move them or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, do not feel it.</start_of_turn>
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	The veins that are deadly in many situations, if you move them and feel well when you stretch and pull them, the veins that the joint of the bone is saved, and the patient will be cured, if you put on cure.</start_of_turn
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if something similar comes to the spine of the back, and you know if it is sane or not, if you take care that the pieces are softened, and that the accident which is in the hands and on the back is from the wind and the egestion of the will;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And when it is softened on its belly, if you make an egestion of the will
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	When it is soothed on the back and it vomits, it cannot be stopped
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Wounds that are mortal:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	If he does not toil diligently in his treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	If this mishap does not occur, then the matter is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	If he does not toil diligently in his treatment, and if there is an abscess at the root of the hair, if you put oil of thistle or oil of rue on the spine, until it is calmed down.
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	Then put on a soothing and drying dressing, and bind it with a thread, and command the patient to rest
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	If the bones break, if you can cover over that part quickly;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and fix the bone, then gather the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a bandage, and cure it with ointment until it is healed
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	And if the head of the shoulder is broken, which is called the "shoulder dislocation", if you have twisted your left hand pouch and placed it equal to the other hand at your side, then place the support and stay on, if you need them.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then strain it, and if there is a displacement of bones, if it remains so, and the bone, cure the wound until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the thigh bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	When the thigh bone is broken, and if it happens, if there is no sign of improvement at the head;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	then it is long and declines downward, and brings pain to the patient, and swelling, and breaks the limb.</start_of_turn>
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that if you extend your hand over, as long as you are over the breeze;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and the sleeves which are the breeze and the form of the limb.
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the breeze is at the shoulder only, if put equal this breeze, as long as it is in a natural position.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it bends inwards, if you make the patient sit on his belly, until the restoration of this fracture is apparent.</start_of_turn
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have put it equal, if put on the socket, then put on a cushion of cloth or wool, and restrain the breeze, so that it does not move;
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and hold the limb steady, so that the limb is even
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	and if there is a spasm of the limb, do not touch it, until the spasm of the limb is appeased, and put on what we have said before
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	And then return to the restoration, and tighten if it is necessary, if there is no mishap.
et c’est li maniere.	This is the end of the text.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	De la brisure de l’ajutoire.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The assistant is that which is between the shoulder blade and the head of the shoulder, and if it is fractured, it must be restored in one of two ways:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	One is to take one fist full of myrrh, according to this fashion
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And hold the two thumbs and two fingers upwards, and hold the patient above a seat;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	Then gently pull down the arm until it reaches the armpit, and there put a fist of myrrh, then do not put any weight on it or the attendant will extend it backwards.
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then he puts his thumbs together in his hands, until the thumb returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	Or the other method is to hold the patient’s arm at his collarbone, and bind the hand to his neck, and command the attendants to hold the part above the break at his hands, and the other to hold below at all the joints, and extend the chest towards the part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, if you strain the limb from the shoulder to the elbow, and from the elbow to the wrist, extend the thumbs of the assistants to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the thumb is close to the head of the shoulder, if you must, put one thumb in the middle of the elbow and the other towards the wrist, from the thumb.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	And thus if the thumb is towards the wrist, if you must, put one thumb lightly and gently, with some force, until the thumb is even on the palm and on the wrist
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then put the thumb even, if you can, and hold it, if necessary, for fear that the thumb does not come back
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if the thumb comes back, if it does not stay put, do not hold it for more than seven days, put on moist linen and rose oil, until the thumb is calmed down
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Then the strain, and the manner of straining if you place the dressing over the wound, then assemble the arm on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	Put the bandage on, and strain on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its place, without any hindrance, or without moving the bones.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone is not moving, if you use staples, put on the wound a wider and stronger staple than the others, and put between the knuckles two staples at least one inch apart; and let one staple be as long as to pass through three knuckles.</start_of_turn>
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then strain on the staples, as I said at the beginning of this chapter, more strongly and less loosely.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if thou seest the elevation of the shoulder-blade, and the stretching, as we have said, in the course of restoring the limb, and thou doubtest the incision, if thou leave it until the seventh day, as we have said;
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	Then look carefully for three days after the limb has been restored, that it does not swell or cause pain, or that the swelling does not return to the limb because it is too taut.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the sufferer persists, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such things occur, if thou must remove the dressing only after three days or more, and the patient lies down on his back and rests his hands on his stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	put on the shoulder-blade a cushion of plain wool equally, and look for an hour or two to see whether the limb remains broken or whether the ligaments are softened
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	If by the power of medicine, and you do the meat which we have before us, in part as much as the meat is at the first degree;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when it starts to recover, if it be large
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	It is customary that the shoulder and limb should be taken back in 40 days in all cases
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then one must loosen and administer poultices and medicines for the limb in question
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is painful and embedded, if it stays for more than a day or two, it must be loosened.
de la brisure du bras	And if the fracture of the arm is displaced, leave it undisplaced for one day or two months.
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two “humerus,” of which one is small, and is that which supports the pouch;
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and is that which is below the little thumb;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	By chance, the great bone breaks alone, or the small one, and by chance the wrist is fractured together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small bone is fractured, restoration is easy, and the healing is quick.</start_of_turn>
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the great bone is fractured, if the healing is bad, it is more painful than when they are fractured together.</start_of_turn>
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bone is fractured, if the limb is slightly extended and put in its place.</start_of_turn
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is the great bone, if you must extract it, do it with greater force.</start_of_turn
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	Hold the thumb above the wrist, and grasp the pouch of the hand higher up than the other, and the small one must be lower than the others, and let the patient cross his arm over himself, and the thumb in front of him higher than the patient, so that the patient does not feel any pain.</start_of_turn
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	Then extend the minister's arm at the shoulder to the outside of his hand, or at I liien, and one other minister at I other at the base.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he sets the eye equal, following its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the burst (dislocation) it breaks into pieces, if you place some support in its place, and if there is no slippage that pricks like before, you shall not be able to restore it to its place; then leave it as it is and support the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the forceps the wound is open, as I have already spoken to the singular chapter;
si pren la cure.	take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if in the beginning of the restoration blood comes out from the abscess, if glue I drape it with a cloth made of rose oil and white wax, neither too thick nor too soft;
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and tie I drape it above all subtly, until the abscess blood vessels are calmed down
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	and then put on the cerate, and put in the plaster of the powder of the mill with abundance of eggs, because put the staples, and let the staple of the forceps be firm, and one space wider than the others;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and the wicks which he must have six stars or arms in more diverse positions.
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	or if the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two.
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and is strained more above the fracture than elsewhere, and all the days less in aligning, as I said at the beginning of this chapter
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and the cloths that are above the fracture are soft and moist, and are neither hard nor rough
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and the thread, which is strained, should be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And rest the limb and the tendon afterwards for some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if other bad accidents come to the limb, if there is itching that comes to the limb, you must raise the limb with warm water, until the itching is appeased.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the limb rest still.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the traction, and if the tendon is softened and the bone is loosened, and similar things, if necessary
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	If you take care that the nourishment does not come to the limb because it is too stiff, then you must soften it somewhat, and leave it for a while, until the nourishment returns, and then strain it.</start_of_turn>
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said happen to the patient, keep it detached for twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	or when it hangs limp, then he must hold the hands to his throat, and let his collar be even, and guard against movement and vomiting, and sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and the swelling that caused this fracture will disappear in XXX days or in XXXV, and by chance in XX days, according to the compositions and temperaments of the virtues
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	The nails on the back of the hand, and we have had two breaks there, often comes from fractures, and comes no more than once or twice.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	and when the limb is broken or twisted, if he must believe that the patient walks crookedly, and stands directly in front of him equally
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then put his hand on the extended cloth, and extend the minister the broken bones, and put them even with the eyes, until they are well joined
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and put on the plaster and the supports, if the incisions do not come out, then I put in a splint as much as is necessary.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and be enveloped in linen cloth.</start_of_turn>
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the fracture is at the edge of the bone of the limb, if you make a ball of gauze and command the patient to hold it against the fractured limb.</start_of_turn
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	Then I bind it with a long bandage, and put in a splint as thick as the limb, and bind it firmly.</start_of_turn
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is outward, if you command that you place a pin above and another below at the joint, so that the hand is overextended and straight, then hold it firmly around the hand, and staunch the bleeding between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the fracture comes neither from above nor from below, if it is a pouch, if I put it even, if it is right.</start_of_turn
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	And with the pressure, strain the limb, and if you see that it will not move, put in a small right pin to raise the swelling, and do not move it.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	And if the swelling is like others, as in the index or any other, if you put it even and hold it with the sound thing that follows
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you bind them together while holding it, when the movement is finished, or you put on a pin, as with a pouch.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	Take care in restoring and disposing of the burnt tissue, and cure what comes from it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	and if the break is outward, if you command that you place a pin above and another below at the joint, so that the hand is overextended and straight, then hold it firmly around the hand, and staunch the bleeding between the two.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The thigh bone is often fractured, and one can see it when it is twisted before and behind
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is when it is bound under the swelling, and the other below
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on his face, then extends his chin slightly so that his tongue rests evenly on the part below.
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and this is when the fracture breaks through the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	If the fracture is close to the root of the thigh, if one of the tendons below the bulge and the other below the fracture.

Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	and if there is excessive swelling, if you leave it calm and come back to your work and your treatment;
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	the limb is made in a crooked way
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is proper that you wrap around the armpit, a bend of hair doubled in two or three, and hold the superfluous hair, then stretch the limb until the nails reach the root of the nail, and keep the thread long between the elbow and the limb, from below the elbow to above the wrist;
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	then stretch the limb and the elbow the hair, and put on the bandage, and put on the bandage on the bone of the limb.
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	then use the remaining cloth between the limb and the elbow of soft wool to make it even, and start to bind in three tours or four on the armpit;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and the more you go up the armpit, the less you will strain;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	Then take as I said two fingers that you have placed between the leg and the hip, and join them with three nails that are below, then raise the head of the nails to the foot, as long as you see below the bone.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	Then hold it tight, if it does not move from its place, then leave it alone, and do not cause any further bleeding or swelling or anything similar.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if there is swelling, if the dislocation is addressed, and you address this which has come, as we have said many times.</start_of_turn
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	And if there are pieces of bone that prick, if you cover it well, it will not matter.</start_of_turn
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	And if it will not stay in place, if you must cut the limb and drain it.</start_of_turn
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is as we have said, when it is sound.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And never is the limb broken in this way that we set it, as in the shoulder and the arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	although in the setting that is done it does not please the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And sometimes the bone is restored in a day, or less or more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin area.
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Hair that in the groin has often burst, but it falls many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, if not a mere tear, or an opening, and there is pain at every wound, and sense of pain, and this is well known.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the setting is done so that what is round is put back in its place, as long as it is put together firmly
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	then put the bandage on, and put a round cushion in, if you must, and hold it firmly, then reward all the precautions that we have said before, as for cautery and other like that
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	if there is any other accident that may occur when it is sound
de la brisure de la jambe	And if it is set right, do this: put the rounded peg back in its place until it is well assembled; then put the stuffing in, and put a round pin in if you have need of it, and hold it as it should be held; then restore all the arrangements that we have mentioned before, as for example incisions and other similar things; if you put in every mishap that it should be put in, as long as it is healthy.
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Hair that is on the leg has two bones, of which one is called the right non-muscle and the other is called the fossilized.
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And there is often a fracture with the arm, and because of this the restoration is just as it is with an equal arm, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones are fractured together, if the limb is broken throughout.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if a subtle bone is broken, it will twist forward.</start_of_turn>
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the big bone is fractured, if one sees great pain, and it is well seen;
et torne desoz.	it breaks apart
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Therefore bring extension, and put it equal, and tie the laces equally;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but always if the fracture is serious, and there are many pieces, that the extension be less strong and lighter;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And do likewise according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have finished your work, if you take two strips of cloth that are long enough to circle the limb from hip to knee, and bind them from hip to ankle;
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap the limb with two bands below and above, and bind them in the middle, and with this binding the limb will not droop to the right or left, and that is good.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and no one should administer any medicine that has a long duration, and if there is cloth, and you put it on the limb to prevent movement, and do it quickly in the fracture or wound
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move the limb around to see if there is any other fracture or accident.
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is clean and healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fracture of bones due to violence.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, fracture does not arise; but in bones of violence, fracture never comes alone, and there must be two together; and there is no other cause of death but certainty and fear.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	If there are broken bones that are seen to be moving against each other, if you put the limb down on the earth as though it were falling, and then put the limb back onto the ground, where the bones were lifted, then press down until they return to their proper place
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	Then place the dressing and bandage on, and put on a small weight on the limb at two fingerbreadths, then support the limb steadily, and when you have bound up the limb with cloth and other things as needed
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when two or three days have passed, if the limb is loose, because you will find the bones equal, whether fractured or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if there are any broken bones that you have restored, as we have said above;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then set the bone with a pin according to the length of the bone, and make the hole a little wider, and then put on the weight that I mentioned above, and support steadily
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	And if there are two or three, or more, break [the skin], and put upon each two stitches according to their quantity, covered in one layer of linen, and strain the wound from below the heel.
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And keep upon the head of the wound against the belly of the heel if it is held firmly.</start_of_turn>
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	Remember also the other things I have said about other breaks, as we have mentioned.</start_of_turn>
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And treat each case as it should be treated.</start_of_turn
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the clavicle bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bones of the nature of a woman are broken, if you make her sit enlarged, then incline towards the back part and be held behind.</start_of_turn
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	Then fill in the belly the nature of the patient's condition, and put in as many as I stop.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	Then empty the woman, and keep her back and belly firm, and then leap the cotton, as long as it comes to the limit of the nature, and returns the bone with the stop.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	And when she vomits, if she has grasped the cotton, and when she has vomited, she returns, and thus make seven days or more
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	If she is restored the fracture, and if you see it, take a bladder of rhubarb, and bind it to the belly with a bandage, and squeeze the whole bladder into the nature
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	Then blow in the bandage forms, until the bladder is expelled completely.
la nature si revenra li brisure;	The nature will return the fracture.
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then fill it with cotton and leave it untouched for days until it heals
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of a man or woman is fractured, if you restore it as we have said concerning the thigh bone;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and they are not hidden by those who put their studies and their work into it, and they understand my book.</start_of_turn>
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fracture means in many ways the right way of restoration:</start_of_turn>
enten le donques.	except that.</start_of_turn>
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the limb, when it is fractured, take a gooseberry and hold the limb.</start_of_turn
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	Then cover the wound with a cloth, and leave it for three days or until it is healed. And it will be completely healed.
de brisure avec plaie	Of sudden with wound.
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	In the case of sudden fracture with wound, even if it is great, as with the bone of the thigh or the shoulder or the like, that it be set right now, as the symptoms which we have mentioned bear witness.</start_of_turn>
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is well closed, if the vitriol has been retained, if you have nothing else, then repeat the restoration of the fracture in this way, or that way, for if it does not come, after these measures.</start_of_turn
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the swelling comes, if you must leave the restoration until the swelling has gone down, as long as the swelling is appeased, and do not touch either the third or the fourth part, for you will otherwise cause a worse accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if a bone breaks suddenly, it appears above like a wound discovered, so you must cautiously hold it at a slight extension with your hands.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the swelling does not disappear so that you can make your hands even, if the disease has this instrument which is of iron, which is seven or eight inches long, and its size is according to the extent of the wound.
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and because of this, when it grasps three or four, according to what is necessary in the bruise of a wound
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and be round and somewhat thick, that it does not cause pain in the compression on the limb at your work, and be thick in front, and large from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	It is called "palainche", because it must be placed on the head of the visible bone
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And the limb has once again, as it returns, and be equal the one meets the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is slight and the instruments cannot firmly grasp the bone, if you must cover the head of the bone, as long as the instruments have possession of it.</start_of_turn
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you are unable to restore the limb, as we have said, if you see that the edge of an instrument, or an incision or suture, approaches this, at your peril;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	Then restore what is displaced from the bone with rough grasping and little pressure.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, it is because the marrow is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	If you do that, then moisten it with black styptic plaster, and hold it in place;
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put anything on the wound except cerate or anything else that may cause oil, for it will cause putrefaction and corruption
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	Then administer stars when you have restored the limb, and leave the wound uncovered, and bind the covering around the wound, according to the extent of the wound, and take care that the wound is not strained with a fracture
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	And often have I seen that this has happened to fools, that it has caused the patient to become mad or to die or has caused no less damage.
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	Or it is more flexible and softer than the other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is small or large, and you doubt that the treatment will suffice, as we have said, and you feel pain in the limb, if it does not suffice to put it on stars;
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but cover it around with soft cloth, instead of stars, and bind it tightly
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	When you see after one or two days that the swelling has gone down at the wound, if the one you put on previously has fallen off, put on a healing bandage, as with a bandage of four herbs and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you bind the limb three times a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be supported in a gentle way that the limb can move slightly without causing discomfort
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If the limb persists, and cannot be reunited at its proper place, because there are small bone fragments, it is necessary that you close the wound with great care, and remove all these fragments which cause pain
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	If a fistula arises in the limb, or other sign of corruption, if it is possible to cure it, according to what is written in this chapter above
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	When the bone is broken and is opened on the limb, as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder, and other similar bones of the large limbs, if I do not treat it, for often death comes from this, but I leave it as long as it bleeds
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	By chance, after twenty days or thirty, then cure the wound if you wish.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you do not wish, leave it alone.</start_of_turn>
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Hair that comes out with the scab
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	Many times after the brightness of the breeze, even close to the joint, the good thing is to see the shape of the limb.</start_of_turn
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and by chance cannot make the limb move naturally.</start_of_turn
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Therefore take care lest it be fresh.</start_of_turn
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if you administer astringent medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocoll, acacia, and similar things, that you take none of these things, or all together, and mix them with a stiff wine or with egg white or with vinegar.</start_of_turn
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and puts them on the knot in dumplings, and holds them well, and does not loosen them from the hands for days.
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then dislocates it again, and starts another one until the swelling is bony;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or you strain on a piece of flesh well made;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the owner of the flesh is that if it is bony all the swellings under the limbs
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the swelling is already converted into hardness as much as stone, and it is necessary to pierce, if the swelling above is large, and make the apparent surplus disappear.
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	or you leave it without any support, until it is bony, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Weak limb after care
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the fracture has been restored, and remains fixed after the limb is weak and limp, if there is any cause for it:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	or because it was too tightly bound and was not allowed to move as much as it should have been.
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because there were too many bands on it, and it could not move freely.
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or for excessive bruising.
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or because of too great a movement, which did not suit it
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because there was too much blood in its substance, if the limb is weak.</start_of_turn>
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	and the treatment is to give the patient rest and make the limb firm, until the swelling is reduced in it.</start_of_turn>
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	And he gives a bath, and he does rejoice and is merry.
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	Then he puts poultices on the limb, so that the poultices attract at the great nourishment, and the swelling often becomes acute, until the nourishment returns to the limb.
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The limb is twisted after the seizure.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the limb is deformed, although it does not lose its natural work
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	since it is not believed that we must break the limb anew, and many have experienced this in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	these works are blamed, and there comes great evil, and by chance the patient dies
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	Whenever swelling and pain are fresh, if it is caused by hot water, or soft herbs are boiled, like rue malve, and radish, and honey, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and you make an emollient plaster, like aquaint well made, and you take the bruise of rue malve, and confirm it with fat of gelatine or oil of alum, and make plaster over it.
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	or you take fat figs, and grind them with dung, and similar medicines that appease the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the bone loosened by continuous rubbing and length of time with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	Or else be moved to the limb from the armpit hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the swelling is thickened and hardened, like stone, and the bone needs to be cauterized, if you cover it just up to the bone, make an incision slightly deeper;
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And put cushions and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	And so begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to no more, if you can now restore the limb to its proper position.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if one delays, if by chance one should reset it, there will be pain in the limb;
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	because it is painful to move it when it is swollen.
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	causing great swelling and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	although when this happens, if you make the patient comfortable, then leave him, until the swelling subsides;
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then the limb will grow hot and oily, and move gently, and cure each limb as it comes into its place
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters concerning dislocations of the shoulder joint to the end.
des mandibules	Des mandibules.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	When the jaws are loosened and the dislocations are done twice:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	Or they are a sign of bony lesions of their limbs, and soften a sign.
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Or they are completely loosened, and hang towards the side, and cause him to spit out saliva from his mouth that he cannot hold, cannot close his mouth, and engulfs his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, if it returns by itself in several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is whole and accompanied, if you must certainly hold it firmly, and do not delay me;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a way that the minister holds the head of the patient, and look with your eye at the pocket of one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw in the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other two hands are displaced, to put them even
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And command the patient to soften his teeth, his jaw, and move them all around.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And behold the eye that is beside the pocket, until it returns to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if they are gripped, even if both jaws are together, if they arise with hot oil, as long as you keep them slightly soft;
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	do not force the return, as we have said before.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are returned equally, and the patient’s mouth is closed well with soft pressure, put upon moist cloths soaked in rose oil and wax, then bind them lightly with thread;
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and keep the patient lying on his back, and his arms resting between two cushions, so that they do not move forwards or backwards, do not attempt to force it, but take hold of the teeth lightly, until the pain is gone, and close the jaws
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	Then let him swallow what he wants lightly, and do not make him open his mouth to swallow or drink, until his jaw is well oiled and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	If the teeth do not return to their place at a single hour, and are not otherwise converted, fever and nausea will ensue, and sometimes vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	When you see this, then know that it is a loss;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And many times death comes to him who has it, in eight days
de la forcelle	of the forceps.</start_of_turn>
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot grasp deep within without causing displacement, and is worth nothing when removing it, and it is often felt.</start_of_turn
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is that the patient lies still on his back, and extends his arms;

de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	This must be done three times in order to restore the shoulder

et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and at the head of the shoulder there will be a hollow, and the bones of the buttocks will touch the head of the shoulder, as if it were a knot

li jointure reva ens maintenant.	The jointure reva ens maintenant.

Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary to keep it moving until the limb is comfortable, because it will heal more quickly.

If after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses the limb many times, until the grief is relieved and returns to its former state.
de la dislocation dou coute	If after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses the limb many times, until the grief is relieved and returns to its former state.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	The joints that are loosened by blows are loosened at points, and return at points.</start_of_turn>
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and are loosened throughout, both front and back, and the dislocation is not remedied, for it is seen and felt well.</start_of_turn

puis le deslie.	Then he must be loosened.

li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joint of the limb is loosened, and the return is easy, more than the others.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	However, it is necessary to reattach it immediately while it is loosened, even if there is swelling or if there is an opening

Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	However, note that you must watch if it is truly back in place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Then put the patient’s hand on a table at extension and flexion
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of his hand on the table, and I will look and put his hand on the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, that is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, if the strain of supporting muscles relaxes after the incisions, and you leave it in its place, let it return naturally.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if it cannot bear it, and you do not wish to put it back in place after some days, the joint will become stiff
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and causes no further pain for the patient as long as the limb is soft, and cannot move anything at all

de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the shoulder of the hand.

dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	From the loosening of the shoulder joint at the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder or neck joint is loosened, or there are several such loosenings, if no cure is found, for the patient’s death is imminent.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	If the signs are that the blood vessels flow in the opposite direction, do not hold it, for many times it is softened in no limb, or the two thighs or two arms or one foot.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And many times it moves the scapula to its three parts.
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	that which moves at the back is called "gilbositez".
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	the cure is that if it comes from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	if there is no cure or healing for all that
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	and that which comes from fear or percussion or similar things, say the old physicians in great words, or there is no benefit at all;
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and I have made instruments in various ways
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the scapula that comes before the elbow, there is no healing at all
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	And thus also when it comes directly from two sides, and one cannot cure the fever except for that which comes from behind, as I have said.
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	And that the patient is stretched out on his face in one league even, and has strained his eyes from him, that they do not close.
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	Then take I cushion at the head in the earth forms, and I another has pieces, and I bind one limb outside the patient’s buttocks, and I another has haunches, and has knees, and has ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and two ministers know the strings, one at the head and the other at the pieces, among the two cushions
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and be well closed, the cushion as we have said, and the patient puts his palms on the spine forms, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a thumb three fingers long, and hold the skin taut over the part, and let the patient lie on their side, and hold the head of the thumb taut over the part, then put the middle of the thumb over the spinous process.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	put the thumbs side by side over the other head of the thumb, and press firmly, until it returns to its place.
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and if you see that it is fractured at the wrist, do it at the nut that turns at the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And put two stitches at the head of the patient’s arm from a great hand, and over the pieces two others, and have between each stitch, a suture and a piece of cloth, a palm of spice long;
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	And every time a tick is pierced, or the thorn is twisted, and the hairs remain firmly in the earth, if they do not move.
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	And between two hairs there is one hair that has twisted, so that the thread that has twisted is twice that of one palm of its length, because of the thorn.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	Then the thread which is among the armpits towards the thorn at the head, and the other thread towards the pieces towards the other thorn, and the hairs of the servants twist their thorn at the whole thread, and the master puts the thorn even as we have said
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, put on a dry dressing with a lot of eggs, and then press, and then support with a tablet of three fingers’ length, which covers the area of the swelling and the sensitive part of the spine, and then bind with a thread, as we have said, and use the patient some nourishing herbs until they are healed
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	And if nothing comes to an end of the sickness, if it is necessary, administer soothing and calming medicines, with the exception that we have mentioned before.
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	And never administer on a piece of lead, and never does its appearance appear behind the shoulder bone at the back, and take care that this is not a dislocation.
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	And it is the bone that opens, for which we must not presume
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	because of this there may come death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the shoulder
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	The joints of the thigh and the shoulder only come loose with dislocations, not as with others
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	and the joint of the thigh is loosened in three parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	Within and outside, before and behind;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	More inward it goes, the more it swells outside; and more inward it comes, the more it unvalues before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation inward is that when you join the painful limb with the flesh, if it is longer, and opens more the patient’s joints than the known, and cannot double his elbow at the fire;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And this is the cause of the displacement of the shoulder socket from its place, because the head of the humerus comes loose from its socket
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of the one who comes to the rescue, if it is that this accident is contrary to those mentioned above.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of that which happens in front, if it is well supported, are that the limb is well placed according to the completion;
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	Thus do not double the elbow in pain, and if you see it happen, do not do it again, but retain the urine, and swell the groin, and when he goes, it passes over the heel
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of the one who comes to the rescue, if it is that he cannot extend his knee, cannot double it, and that this limb is shorter than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the shoulder is dislocated at the root of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	When this semblance of dislocation is repeated, if it is an ancient dislocation and remains fixed according to its nature, there is no cure.
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and I do not know that there is any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in such cases where the dislocation is fresh, and there are three ways of dislocation, if you hurry to rejoin the limb, and stretch it inwards and outwards, and move it to the right and left;
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	it will return by itself, and there is no need for any other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this way, if you must, apply four strong fingers, and stretch the limb with two hands, or with one hand that is bound to the groin
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	And another minister extends his hand downwards almost as far as his elbows, then grasps with a loop of thread the hair on the buttock;
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another holds the head of the thread there.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and extends upwards and downwards together until the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains suspended
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is often used as in three similar cases, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.</start_of_turn>
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If not, if you must put an antidote for its appearance
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is loosened, if you must that the patient rest on his chest, then put the thread on the root of the buttock, and the limb which is below the ankle, then stretch the thread upwards towards the ankle, and downwards towards the heel
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	Then take another assistant and grasp the great head of the shoulder of the ailing person, and extend it towards the front.
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	if it returns to its place now;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this method of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you do not tighten it in this method as we have said, if you must, bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong thread over the two toes and over the two knees, and let the limb be extended two fingers more than the others
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	then either suspend it above the head of a pole, or on the ground two long arms;
